Source Materials Used
This volume is based on the master planning documents, the BT Quick product notes, and the system 
design images supplied for Blumetara AI. The uploaded planning material establishes that the MVP uses 
Flutter, React Admin, FastAPI, MongoDB Atlas, AWS S3, Firebase Auth and FCM, Docker, GitHub Actions, 
AWS, and Gemini/OpenAI. The BT Quick notes describe Blumetara as a Health Co-Pilot and TARA AI as 
an in-app caretaker, coach, and guide.
Important limitation
This document is an engineering and product planning artifact. It is not a clinical compliance document and does 
not make Blumetara a regulated medical device. Any future clinical, diagnostic, or emergency-care capabilities 
must be reviewed by qualified medical, legal, and compliance professionals.

Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 1
Draft v1.0 | Executive Summary, Project Context & Product Vision
1. Executive Overview
Blumetara AI is planned as an AI-powered personal healthcare assistant designed to help individuals 
organize health information, understand health reports, track goals, receive reminders, and interact 
with a personalized AI assistant called TARA. The product should feel less like a generic chatbot and 
more like a health co-pilot that remembers the user's profile, reports, goals, reminders, and long-term 
progress.
The initial product direction is a mobile-first MVP supported by a web-based admin dashboard. The 
mobile application is expected to be built in Flutter so that Android and iOS can be developed from one 
codebase. The admin dashboard is expected to be built using React or Next.js. The backend is expected 
to use FastAPI in Python with a modular monolith architecture. MongoDB Atlas is the primary database, 
AWS S3 is the file storage layer, Firebase handles authentication and notifications, and Gemini/OpenAI 
provide the LLM layer.
The MVP should be ambitious enough to demonstrate the core value of the startup but controlled 
enough to be delivered in a reasonable timeline. The key early value should come from health report 
upload, OCR extraction, RAG-based question answering, personalized AI chat, reminders, goals, 
dashboards, and basic admin operations.
A major architectural decision is to avoid premature microservices. Blumetara should begin as a 
modular monolith, where the codebase is structured by domain modules but still deployed as a single 
backend application. This gives faster development, simpler debugging, easier deployment, lower cost, 
and a cleaner path for a small engineering team. Later, high-load modules such as AI processing, 
notifications, analytics, or file processing can be extracted into separate services if scale demands it.
This Volume 1 document establishes the project context, business purpose, stakeholder requirements, 
product identity, engineering principles, and long-term vision. Later volumes should expand this 
foundation into formal requirements, architecture, database design, APIs, AI/RAG design, DevOps, 
security, testing, pricing, and development roadmap.
Executive decision
Build a serious but controlled MVP: mobile app + admin dashboard + FastAPI modular monolith + MongoDB 
Atlas + AWS S3 + Firebase + LLM integration. Avoid unnecessary complexity until the product proves user 
demand.
1.1 What Blumetara AI Is
 A personal health co-pilot for individuals.
 A secure place to store and interpret health reports.
 A personalized AI chat assistant that uses the user profile and uploaded reports as context.
 A reminder and habit-tracking platform for medicines, hydration, and goals.
 A future ecosystem that may connect users, family members, doctors, pharmacies, hospitals, wearables, 
and insurance APIs.
1.2 What Blumetara AI Is Not
 It is not a replacement for doctors.
 It should not provide emergency medical diagnosis.
--- PAGE 5 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 1

 It should not claim regulatory approval unless that approval is formally obtained.
 It is not building its own large language model in the MVP.
 It should not store large PDFs or images inside MongoDB; files belong in S3.
2. Founder and Project Background
The project is being led by Pranav NS, a Computer Science student at the University of Alberta. This 
project is also being treated as a first serious freelance software engineering engagement. Because this 
is not just a demo project, the planning standard must be higher than a normal student prototype.
The founder context matters because the delivery strategy must balance professional ambition with 
practical execution. Blumetara should be designed in a way that can be developed using AI-assisted 
tools while still following real engineering discipline. AI coding assistants can accelerate 
implementation, but they cannot replace architecture, testing, security review, debugging, deployment 
discipline, and client communication.
2.1 Founder Operating Principles
 Use AI tools aggressively for productivity, but do not blindly trust generated code.
 Prioritize architecture before coding.
 Build the MVP like a production system, not a temporary prototype.
 Document important trade-offs so future developers can understand why decisions were made.
 Charge for engineering value, not just coding time.
 Keep the MVP scope realistic so the first version can actually be delivered.
3. Client and Business Context
The client owns a marketing agency and wants to launch an AI-powered healthcare startup. This 
context creates two important realities. First, the client may understand branding, growth, and market 
positioning better than deep software architecture. Second, the engineering team must explain 
technical decisions clearly and translate complex architecture into business value.
The client understands that existing LLMs such as Gemini, OpenAI, or Claude will be used. Blumetara is 
not building a custom foundation model. The product value comes from workflow design, 
personalization, data storage, report analysis, reminders, RAG, and a trustworthy AI experience built 
around the user's health context.
3.1 Client Expectations
 A usable MVP that can be shown to real users or early investors.
 A clean mobile experience for individuals.
 A functional admin dashboard for operational visibility.
 AI features that feel personalized and helpful.
 A system that can later grow into Version 1 and Version 2.
 A professional delivery process with documentation, deployment, and handover.
--- PAGE 6 ---

3.2 Business Reality
Healthcare products must build trust. A weak AI experience, confusing medical outputs, poor security, 
or unstable reminders can damage user confidence quickly. Therefore, the MVP must be designed 
around reliability, clarity, and responsible boundaries. The app should repeatedly remind users that AI-
generated information is educational and supportive, not a replacement for medical consultation.
4. Product Definition
Blumetara AI should be positioned as a personal health co-pilot. The product combines health records, 
AI chat, reminders, goals, summaries, and future integrations into one user-centered platform. Instead 
of making users manually interpret scattered health information, Blumetara centralizes data and uses 
TARA AI to convert that data into understandable guidance, reminders, and insights.
4.1 Core Product Statement
Product Statement
Blumetara AI helps individuals understand, organize, and act on their health information through a personalized 
AI co-pilot named TARA, supported by secure storage, report analysis, reminders, goal tracking, and health 
summaries.
4.2 Product Pillars
Pillar Meaning MVP Relevance
Understand Explain health reports and medical 
terms in simple language. OCR + RAG + AI chat
Remember Store reports, profile data, medicines, 
goals, and habits. MongoDB metadata + S3 files
Guide Provide personalized suggestions based 
on available profile context. TARA prompt builder + user profile
Remind Help the user stay consistent with 
medicines, water, and goals. Firebase notifications + scheduler
Summarize Produce daily or periodic summaries of 
user activity and gaps. Daily summary module
Scale Allow future expansion into family 
accounts, wearables, and APIs. Modular architecture
5. TARA AI Health Co-Pilot Vision
TARA is the emotional and functional center of Blumetara. The product should not present AI as a 
generic chat window. It should present TARA as an always-available in-app caretaker, coach, and guide. 
This naming and positioning can create product identity, improve user recall, and make the AI 
experience feel more personal.
5.1 TARA Role Model
Role Description Example MVP Capability
Caretaker Helps the user remember medicines, 
hydration, and basic routines. Medicine and water reminders
Coach Encourages users toward goals such as 
weight loss, calorie control, BP tracking, Goal tracking and nudging

or diabetes management.
Guide Explains uploaded reports and answers 
questions based on stored user context. Report analysis and RAG chat
Summarizer Turns daily health activity into simple 
summaries. Daily end-of-day summary
Analyzer Connects goals, reports, profile data, 
and reminders into meaningful context. Personalized prompt builder
5.2 TARA Design Principles
 Speak clearly and avoid unnecessary medical jargon.
 Use the user's health profile and report context where available.
 Avoid pretending to be a doctor.
 Encourage medical consultation for concerning or unclear results.
 Be supportive without being overly casual for serious health topics.
 Keep track of goals, medicines, and reminders through structured backend data rather than relying only 
on chat memory.
 Use source-aware RAG outputs when answering questions about uploaded reports.
6. Problem Statement
Most individuals do not have a single intelligent system that understands their health records, 
remembers their goals, reminds them about actions, and explains medical information in simple 
language. Health data is fragmented across PDFs, prescriptions, mobile fitness apps, lab reports, photos, 
doctor notes, and human memory.
Users often receive blood reports or prescriptions without fully understanding the meaning of values, 
trends, risks, or next steps. They may also forget medicines, fail to drink enough water, abandon goals, 
or lack a simple way to see progress. Blumetara attempts to solve this by combining secure record 
storage, AI interpretation, structured tracking, and intelligent reminders.
6.1 Pain Points
 Medical reports are difficult for non-medical users to understand.
 Health records are scattered across WhatsApp, email, paper, and phone galleries.
 Users forget medication schedules and refills.
 Health goals are started with motivation but not tracked consistently.
 Generic AI chatbots do not remember a user's reports and profile unless a system is built around them.
 Family members may want to monitor elderly parents or dependents, but this should be carefully scoped 
for later versions.
 Users need simple summaries, not complex dashboards filled with numbers.
7. Target Users and Personas
The initial target users are individuals who want help managing personal health information. The 
product can later expand to families, doctors, and healthcare providers, but the MVP should primarily 
solve the individual user experience.

7.1 MVP Primary User
The primary MVP user should be a normal individual who wants to upload health reports, ask 
questions, set reminders, and track simple goals. The MVP should not try to satisfy hospitals, doctors, 
pharmacies, insurance companies, and families all at once. Those are future ecosystem layers.
8. Value Proposition
The central value proposition is personalization. A normal chatbot gives generic answers. Blumetara 
should answer using the user's profile, uploaded reports, goals, medicine schedule, and activity history. 
The user should feel that TARA remembers important health context and helps them act on it.
User Problem Blumetara Value Implementation Mechanism
I do not understand my report. Explain report values in simple terms. OCR + chunking + embeddings + RAG + 
LLM
I forget medicines. Scheduled medicine reminders. Reminder module + scheduler + FCM
I lose track of health goals. Goal meter and progress nudges. Goals + progress collection + dashboard
My health data is scattered. Central health profile and report 
storage. MongoDB metadata + S3 files
Generic AI is not personal. Answers use user context. Prompt builder + profile + relevant 
retrieved chunks
I need daily accountability. End-of-day summary. Scheduled summary generation
9. Business Model Direction
The product notes suggest a Free and Paid structure. The free tier can be used for acquisition and habit 
formation, while the paid tier unlocks higher usage limits, richer tracking, family monitoring, deeper 
analytics, and ad-free experience. The MVP should implement subscription readiness even if full 
monetization is phased in later.
9.1 Free vs Paid Positioning
Feature Area Free Direction Paid Direction
AI Chat Limited daily messages Higher daily message quota
Medicine Reminder Basic reminder Multiple medicines + stock monitor
Water Reminder Limited reminders Multiple reminder options
Goals One goal Multiple goals with nudging and 
analyzer
Daily Summary Basic daily summary Richer summaries and weekly/monthly 
insights

Food Analyzer Limited image analysis Higher image limit + nutrition tracking

A key recommendation is to avoid implementing too many monetization mechanics before the product 
is validated. The MVP can include subscription architecture and payment integration placeholders, 
while the initial launch focuses on user feedback and AI experience quality.
10. MVP Context
The MVP must prove the core Blumetara promise: TARA can use health profile data and uploaded 
reports to help a user understand and act on their health information. Everything else should support 
that promise.
10.1 MVP Must-Have Scope
 User authentication and onboarding.
 Basic user health profile.
 Health report upload to S3.
 Report metadata saved in MongoDB.
 OCR extraction from uploaded reports.
 Chunking and embedding of report text.
 Vector search over user-specific report chunks.
 AI chat with TARA using profile context and retrieved report chunks.
 Medicine reminders.
 Water reminders.
 Goal tracking and simple goal meter.
 Daily health summary.
 Basic notifications through Firebase Cloud Messaging.
 Admin dashboard for users, reports, analytics, subscriptions, and system overview.
10.2 MVP Should Avoid
 Full hospital integration.
 Insurance API integration.
 Medical-device-grade risk prediction.
 Complex doctor dashboard.
 Advanced wearable integrations.
 Too many AI agents before one core TARA experience works well.
 Microservices unless scale or team size demands them.
 Overpromising diagnosis or emergency support.
11. Engineering Philosophy
The technical direction should optimize for a small team building a serious MVP. The ideal architecture 
is simple enough to implement but disciplined enough to scale. Clean architecture, modular monolith 
design, service layer, repository pattern, and strong validation are preferred.
--- PAGE 10 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 1
Draft v1.0 | Executive Summary, Project Context & Product Vision
Principle Meaning for Blumetara
Modular Monolith Keep one deployable backend while separating domains 
internally.
Clean Architecture Keep API routes, business logic, repositories, and 
infrastructure concerns separate.
Repository Pattern Avoid placing direct database logic throughout the codebase.
Service Layer Place business rules in services, not route handlers.
SOLID Make modules easier to modify, test, and extend.
Secure by Default Assume health data is sensitive and protect it from day one.
API First Design backend contracts clearly so Flutter and admin 
dashboard can move faster.
AI as a Service Layer Treat LLM calls, prompts, RAG, and OCR as controlled 
backend services, not random frontend calls.
11.1 AI-Assisted Development Standard
AI tools such as ChatGPT, Claude, Gemini, Cursor, Copilot, and other assistants can be used for 
scaffolding, code generation, tests, documentation, and debugging. However, all AI-generated code must 
be reviewed. The architecture should not be whatever the AI generated in one prompt. It should follow 
the agreed system design and engineering standards.
12. System Design Summary
The supplied diagrams describe a system with client apps, Cloudflare, AWS entry layer, FastAPI 
backend, service layer, data access layer, MongoDB Atlas, AWS S3, vector database, external LLM 
providers, Firebase, payment gateway, background services, CI/CD, and security best practices. This is a 
strong starting architecture for an MVP if implemented in a controlled way.
12.1 Layered Architecture Summary
Layer Components Purpose
Client Layer Flutter mobile app, React admin 
dashboard User and admin interfaces
Edge Layer Cloudflare, DNS, CDN, DDoS protection, 
SSL/TLS Protect and route traffic
AWS Entry Layer Route53, WAF, ALB/API Gateway Managed entry into backend
Backend Layer FastAPI modular monolith Core business logic and APIs
Service Layer AI, RAG, OCR, storage, notifications, 
analytics, payment Reusable business capabilities
Data Layer Repository layer, schemas, MongoDB 
models Controlled database access
Storage Layer MongoDB Atlas, S3, vector database Structured data, files, embeddings
External Services Gemini/OpenAI, Firebase, 
Stripe/Razorpay AI, auth, push, payments
Async Layer Celery, Redis, scheduled tasks, SES, FCM Background jobs and notifications
DevOps Layer Docker, GitHub Actions, ECR, 
deployment automation Build, test, deploy
12.2 Architecture Recommendation
For MVP, the recommended backend deployment target should be selected based on budget and 
developer comfort. EC2 is flexible and familiar but requires more server management. AWS App 
Runner is simpler for containers but can cost more depending on usage. ECS is powerful but may be 
--- PAGE 11 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 1
Draft v1.0 | Executive Summary, Project Context & Product Vision
overkill initially. A practical path is to start with EC2 or App Runner, use Docker from day one, and keep 
the deployment easy to migrate.
13. Data and AI Philosophy
Blumetara is a data-centered AI application. The quality of TARA's responses depends on how well the 
system captures, structures, retrieves, and protects user data. The app should separate raw files, 
structured metadata, embeddings, chat messages, and user profile data.
13.1 Data Storage Rules
 Store PDFs, images, profile photos, voice files, and documents in AWS S3.
 Store metadata, ownership, status, extracted text references, and processing state in MongoDB.
 Store embeddings and report chunks in MongoDB Atlas Vector Search or a dedicated vector database.
 Never send unnecessary personal data to LLM providers.
 Keep audit logs for sensitive actions such as report access, admin actions, and account changes.
 Use user-specific data boundaries so one user's report chunks cannot leak into another user's chat 
context.
13.2 AI Flow Summary
21. User uploads a health report.
22. Backend validates the file and stores it in S3.
23. MongoDB stores report metadata and processing status.
24. OCR extracts text from the report.
25. Text is cleaned and divided into chunks.
26. Embeddings are generated for each chunk.
27. Chunks and embeddings are stored in the vector database.
28. User asks TARA a question.
29. Backend retrieves relevant chunks using similarity search.
30. Prompt builder combines user question, profile, safety rules, and retrieved context.
31. LLM generates a response.
32. Response is formatted, saved, and returned to the user.
14. Security and Trust Baseline
Blumetara handles sensitive health-related data. Even if the MVP is not yet a regulated clinical system, 
the engineering team must treat privacy and security seriously from the first release. Users must trust 
the platform with reports, prescriptions, goals, reminders, and possibly family data in future versions.
14.1 MVP Security Requirements
 Firebase authentication for user identity.
 JWT verification in FastAPI for every protected endpoint.
 Role-based access control for users, admins, support, and future doctors.
 HTTPS everywhere.
 Encrypted storage where supported.
--- PAGE 12 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 1
Draft v1.0 | Executive Summary, Project Context & Product Vision
 Secrets stored in AWS Secrets Manager or secure environment variables, not in code.
 Input validation for all API payloads.
 File validation for uploads.
 Rate limiting for AI and auth-sensitive endpoints.
 Audit logs for admin and sensitive actions.
 Clear medical disclaimers and safety boundaries in AI responses.
14.2 Trust Requirements
Trust is not only technical. It is also product design. TARA should explain uncertainty, avoid 
overconfident medical claims, encourage users to consult professionals, and present information in a 
calm and responsible tone. The user should always understand that the system is an assistant, not a 
doctor.
15. Commercial and Delivery Context
The current commercial planning suggests an MVP development value around INR 2.2 lakhs, Version 1 
around INR 1.6 lakhs, and Version 2 around INR 2.0 lakhs, excluding third-party cloud, API, domain, app 
store, and external service costs. A 10-12 week timeline and 30-day post-delivery bug warranty are part 
of the working expectation. Optional maintenance can be positioned as INR 15,000 to INR 25,000 per 
month depending on scope.
Commercial Item Baseline Direction
MVP Build INR 2.2 lakhs
Version 1 INR 1.6 lakhs
Version 2 INR 2.0 lakhs
Third-party costs Excluded from development fee
Timeline 10-12 weeks for MVP
Warranty 30-day bug-fix warranty after delivery
Maintenance Optional AMC: INR 15,000-25,000/month
15.1 Pricing Justification
The client is paying for complete delivery: requirements, architecture, UI implementation, backend 
engineering, AI integration, database design, file handling, deployment, testing, documentation, and 
handover. AI tools may reduce manual typing time, but they do not remove the engineering 
responsibility or business value of the system.
16. Success Criteria
The MVP should be judged by whether it proves the core product promise with acceptable reliability, 
not by whether it includes every possible future healthcare feature.
Area Success Criteria
User Experience A user can onboard, create profile, upload report, chat with 
TARA, set reminders, and view dashboard without confusion.
AI Quality TARA can answer report-based questions using retrieved 
context and safe language.
Data Handling Reports are stored in S3, metadata is stored in MongoDB, and 
embeddings support retrieval.

expansion.

20. Detailed Product Language and Terminology
A shared vocabulary is necessary because Blumetara combines healthcare language, AI language, cloud 
architecture, and product management. Future developers and AI assistants should use the same terms 
consistently across documentation, code, UI copy, and client communication.
Term Meaning in Blumetara
TARA The in-app AI health co-pilot that guides, reminds, explains, 
and summarizes.
Health Profile
Structured user information such as age range, goals, 
conditions, preferences, medications, and relevant lifestyle 
details.
Health Report Uploaded medical document such as blood report, 
prescription, scan result, or lab PDF/image.
Report Chunk A smaller text segment extracted from a health report and 
prepared for vector search.
RAG Retrieval-Augmented Generation, where TARA retrieves 
relevant user-specific context before answering.
Goal Meter A user-facing progress indicator for goals such as water 
intake, weight, steps, calories, BP, or diabetes tracking.
Nudge A helpful reminder or suggestion generated from goals, 
habits, or missing activity.
Daily Summary A structured end-of-day recap of medicines, water, goals, logs, 
and relevant AI notes.
BUH ID Potential Blumetara user health identifier or internal account 
identifier; should be defined carefully before production use.

24. Product Tone, UX, and Trust Principles
Healthcare UX must feel calm, trustworthy, and clear. Blumetara should not use fear-based language or 
overconfident medical claims. The app should guide users toward better understanding and 
consistency, not panic.
 Use simple language for health explanations.
 Show uncertainty when AI is not sure.
 Do not hide disclaimers in small text only; include them naturally in high-risk answers.
 Use calm visual design, readable typography, and clear action buttons.
 Avoid dark patterns in subscriptions, reminders, or health warnings.
 Make report upload and report deletion understandable.
 Give users control over notifications and health data.
 Design admin tools so staff cannot casually access sensitive data without purpose.
24.1 Example TARA Response Tone
Safe response style
I can help you understand what this value usually means, but I cannot diagnose you. Based on the report you 
uploaded, this marker appears above the reference range. It would be best to discuss it with a qualified doctor, 
especially if you have symptoms or an existing condition.

26. Operational Workflow Preview
The product should be designed not only for users but also for operation after launch. A working MVP 
must have a basic process for bug reports, failed OCR jobs, AI issues, payment problems, and user 
support.
26.1 Example User Workflow
33. User signs up using Firebase authentication.
34. User completes basic health profile.
35. User uploads a blood report PDF or image.
36. Backend stores the file in S3 and saves metadata.
37. Background job extracts text using OCR.
38. Backend chunks the extracted report and stores embeddings.
39. User asks TARA what the report means.
40. TARA retrieves relevant chunks and explains in simple language.
41. User sets medicine and water reminders.
42. User sets a personal goal.
43. At the end of the day, TARA summarizes progress and missing actions.
26.2 Example Admin Workflow
44. Admin logs into the dashboard.
45. Admin views user count, report processing status, AI usage, and payment status.
46. Admin checks failed OCR jobs or support escalations.
47. Admin reviews system health and API usage trends.
48. Admin can disable abusive accounts or investigate suspicious activity through audit logs.
--- PAGE 18 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 1
Draft v1.0 | Executive Summary, Project Context & Product Vision
49. Admin does not casually view health data unless permissions and support workflow justify it.

Every future volume should be written so a new engineer could build from it. This means the 
documentation must be specific, structured, and implementation-ready. Vague statements such as “use 
AI” or “store data securely” are not enough.

28. Development Readiness Checklist
Before development begins, the following items should be completed or explicitly accepted as 
assumptions. This checklist prevents starting implementation with missing foundations.
 Confirm final MVP feature list and mark all future features as out of scope.
 Confirm client budget and third-party cost responsibility.
 Confirm preferred cloud region and data residency expectations.
 Confirm whether app is India-only initially or global-ready.
 Confirm whether Apple App Store and Google Play release are included.
 Confirm UI/UX design responsibility and whether Figma screens are required.
 Confirm LLM provider preference and expected monthly AI usage budget.
 Confirm OCR provider preference and expected report volume.
 Confirm legal disclaimer text with client.
 Confirm payment gateway: Razorpay, Stripe, or both.
 Confirm support and maintenance scope after handover.
 Confirm ownership of code repository, cloud accounts, API keys, and domain.
29. Volume 1 Final Recommendations
The strongest path for Blumetara is to keep the first release narrow but polished. The app should do a 
few things very well: understand uploaded reports, chat with context, remind users, track goals, and 
summarize daily health activity. That is enough to prove whether users want a personal health co-pilot.
--- PAGE 19 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 1
Draft v1.0 | Executive Summary, Project Context & Product Vision
Do not build every item from the BT Quick notes in the MVP. The notes are valuable as product vision, 
but they should be converted into phased roadmap items. Trying to include food analysis, nutrition 
tracking, fitness app reading, 24x7 vitals, SOS alerts, family monitoring, medical risk prediction, hospital 
APIs, pharmacy APIs, insurance APIs, and wearables in the first version would create unacceptable risk.
The engineering foundation should still prepare for these future features. That is why the modular 
monolith, clean architecture, service layer, repository pattern, S3 file storage, MongoDB metadata 
model, vector search, Firebase notifications, and AI orchestrator are important. They allow a practical 
MVP today without blocking growth tomorrow.

1. Product Vision
1.1 Vision Statement
Blumetara AI is envisioned as a personal health co-pilot that helps individuals organize, understand, and 
act on their everyday health information. The product does not attempt to replace doctors or provide 
clinical diagnosis. Instead, it gives users a structured place to store health reports, maintain goals, receive 
reminders, ask health-related questions, and get personalized explanations based on their own health 
profile and uploaded documents.
The long-term product vision is to become a trusted digital health companion that sits between the user 
and the complexity of modern healthcare information. Many users receive blood reports, prescriptions, 
fitness data, diet suggestions, and doctor instructions, but they struggle to connect these pieces into a 
practical daily routine. Blumetara AI solves this gap by combining personal health memory, AI 
explanation, reminders, nudges, and dashboard-based tracking.
One-Line Product Definition
Blumetara AI is an AI-powered personal healthcare companion where TARA AI helps users remember, understand, 
and act on their health information.
1.2 Mission Statement
The mission of Blumetara AI is to make personal health management more understandable, consistent, 
and actionable by combining AI, reminders, document intelligence, and goal-based coaching in a secure 
mobile-first platform.
 Help users understand their own health documents in simple language.
 Help users maintain consistency with medicines, water intake, and health goals.
 Provide personalized responses using the user health profile, reports, goals, and past interactions.
 Create a foundation for future integrations with wearables, doctors, pharmacies, hospitals, and family care 
workflows.
 Keep the MVP simple enough to build, but strong enough to scale into a serious digital healthcare platform.
1.3 Product North Star
The north-star product direction is user trust. In a healthcare-related product, trust is more important 
than novelty. Blumetara should not behave like a random chatbot that gives generic answers. It must 
behave like a careful assistant that knows what it can and cannot do, keeps track of user context, explains 
information clearly, and recommends consulting healthcare professionals whenever the situation 
requires clinical judgment.
North-Star Principle Meaning for Blumetara AI
Trust before speed Fast responses are useful, but safe, clear, and context-aware 
responses matter more.
Personalization before generic advice TARA should use user profile, reports, goals, and reminders 
when relevant.
Action before information overload The product should convert health data into useful daily 
actions.
MVP before overengineering Build a focused first version rather than trying to ship every 
possible healthcare feature.
Safety before medical ambition The MVP must avoid diagnosis, emergency claims, or regulated 
medical-device positioning.
--- PAGE 27 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 2
Draft v1.0 | Product Vision & Business Requirements
1.4 Strategic Product Positioning
Blumetara AI should be positioned as a personal health organization and AI explanation platform rather 
than as a medical diagnosis platform. This distinction is essential for product safety, legal clarity, user 
expectation management, and MVP delivery. The app can help users understand reports, remember 
medication, track goals, and summarize their health day. It should not claim to detect disease, replace 
doctors, prescribe medication, or provide emergency care.
Blumetara Should Be Blumetara Should Not Be
Health co-pilot Doctor replacement
Report explainer Clinical diagnostic device
Medication reminder Prescription authority
Goal and habit coach Guaranteed treatment plan
Personal health memory Hospital-grade EHR system in MVP
AI-assisted education tool Emergency response system in MVP
--- PAGE 28 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 2
Draft v1.0 | Product Vision & Business Requirements
2. Business Problem
2.1 User Pain Points
The central problem is not that users lack health information. The problem is that health information is 
scattered, hard to understand, and difficult to convert into daily discipline. Users may have PDFs of blood 
reports, images of prescriptions, notes from doctors, fitness data, diet goals, and medicine schedules, but 
these are usually stored across WhatsApp, email, paper files, gallery folders, fitness apps, and memory.
Pain Point User Experience Product Opportunity
Medical reports are confusing
Users see values, ranges, and medical 
terms but do not understand what they 
mean.
Report upload, OCR, AI explanation, 
summary, and question-answering.
Health data is scattered
Reports, prescriptions, goals, and 
reminders live in separate apps or offline 
files.
Single health profile and document 
storage layer.
Users forget medicines Manual reminders are inconsistent and 
not linked to health goals.
Medicine reminder module with future 
stock monitoring.
Users lack daily accountability They set goals but do not get useful 
nudges or progress feedback.
Goal tracker, goal meter, nudges, daily 
summary.
Health advice is generic Most chatbots do not know the user 
profile or history.
TARA responses grounded in user profile 
and stored health memory.
Family care is manual One person may manage health data for 
parents or family members.
Future family account monitoring and 
admin/family view.
2.2 Business Opportunity
The business opportunity is to create a consumer health platform that starts with everyday health 
management and gradually expands into a broader healthcare ecosystem. The MVP should validate 
whether users will upload reports, ask health questions, set goals, and use reminders consistently. If that 
behavior is validated, later versions can introduce subscriptions, family plans, nutrition, wearable 
integrations, doctor dashboards, and healthcare partner integrations.
 Short-term opportunity: build an AI health assistant MVP for early users.
 Medium-term opportunity: monetize through paid plans, family plans, and advanced insights.
 Long-term opportunity: become a personal health operating system connected to wearables, hospitals, 
pharmacies, insurance, and doctors.
 Strategic opportunity: create defensibility through personalized health memory, not just generic chatbot 
access.
2.3 Why AI Matters Here
AI is valuable in Blumetara because healthcare information is text-heavy, context-heavy, and confusing 
for normal users. However, the AI must be carefully bounded. TARA should explain, summarize, organize, 
and personalize. It should not make unsafe claims. The strongest value is not simply using an LLM; the 
strongest value is combining user profile, health reports, goals, reminders, and previous interactions into 
a controlled AI experience.
AI Capability Business Value Safety Boundary
Report summarization Users quickly understand what a report 
contains.
Must state that interpretation is 
educational, not diagnosis.
Question answering over reports Users can ask specific questions about 
uploaded documents.
Answers should cite or reference the 
relevant report context where possible.

3. Target Users and Personas
3.1 Primary Target Users
The initial product should focus on individuals who want to manage their own health and families who 
help manage health for parents or dependents. Doctors and institutions should be treated as future 
stakeholders, not primary MVP users. The MVP should avoid trying to become a full clinical workflow 
product immediately.
User Segment Need MVP Priority
Health-conscious individual Track goals, understand reports, 
reminders, AI questions. High
Chronic-condition aware user Monitor diabetes, BP, weight, medicine 
routines. High, but no diagnosis claims
Family caregiver Track family member reports and 
reminders. Medium for MVP, higher for V1
Fitness-focused user Workout, food, calorie, wearable data. Medium; V1 feature set
Doctor/health professional Review patient data and insights. Future
Admin/operator Manage users, monitor content, view 
usage. Required in MVP but minimal

3.6 User Prioritization
The MVP should prioritize users who can validate the core behavior: upload reports, ask questions, set 
health goals, and use reminders. If the first version tries to satisfy doctors, hospitals, pharmacies, wearable 
integrations, nutrition tracking, and family management all at once, delivery risk becomes too high. The 
correct first step is to prove that users find value in TARA AI as a personal health memory and assistant.

Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 2

4. TARA AI Product Concept
4.1 What is TARA AI?
TARA AI is the in-app AI agent inside Blumetara. It should be experienced by users as a health caretaker, 
coach, guide, explainer, and accountability partner. It is not a standalone chatbot pasted into the app; it is 
the intelligence layer that connects the user profile, health reports, goals, reminders, conversations, and 
daily summaries.
TARA AI Definition
TARA AI is the personalized assistant inside Blumetara that remembers user health context, explains reports, 
answers questions, tracks goals, and nudges users toward healthier routines.
4.2 TARA AI Roles
Role Description Example User Value
Caretaker Maintains user health memory and 
reminds users about important routines.
Medicine reminder, water reminder, 
follow-up reminders.
Coach Helps users stay consistent with goals. Weight loss goal progress, BP monitoring 
goal, calorie target reminders.
Guide Explains medical reports and health data 
in simpler language.
Blood report summary and basic 
explanation of terms.
Analyst Summarizes daily, weekly, or monthly 
progress.
End-of-day summary and goal gap 
details.
Personalized Assistant Uses user profile and prior context to 
make answers more relevant.
Responses based on age, goals, reports, 
diet preference, activity level.
4.3 TARA AI Boundaries
TARA must have strict boundaries from day one. Because the product is healthcare-related, unsafe AI 
behavior can damage user trust and create legal risk. The app should consistently communicate that it 
provides education, reminders, organization, and general wellness support, not diagnosis or emergency 
medical care.
Allowed in MVP Avoid in MVP
Explain uploaded reports in simple language. Diagnose disease from a report.
Suggest general questions to ask a doctor. Prescribe medicines or change dosage.
Remind users to take medicines already entered by them. Recommend starting/stopping medicine.
Track goals and summarize progress. Guarantee health outcomes.
Encourage professional consultation when risk is unclear. Handle emergencies as an emergency service.
4.4 TARA AI Personality
TARA should feel calm, supportive, clear, and responsible. It should not be overly dramatic, fear-inducing, 
robotic, or blindly confident. The tone should be similar to a careful health coach who explains 
information in practical language and repeatedly reminds users to consult qualified professionals for 
medical decisions.
 Friendly but not casual in medical-risk contexts.
 Clear and simple without hiding uncertainty.
 Action-oriented: what should the user do next?
 Conservative: when uncertain, recommend professional consultation.
--- PAGE 33 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 2
Draft v1.0 | Product Vision & Business Requirements
 Personalized: refer to user goals, reminders, and uploaded information when relevant.
 Privacy-aware: reassure users that health data is sensitive and handled carefully.
4.5 Product Defensibility Through Memory
Generic LLM access is not a strong business moat. Anyone can open a chatbot and ask health questions. 
Blumetara becomes valuable when it builds structured personal context over time: reports, reminders, 
goals, medicine schedules, progress logs, and summaries. TARA should become useful because it knows 
the user history inside Blumetara, not because it has a better generic answer than every public chatbot.

Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 2

5. Value Proposition
5.1 Core Value Proposition
Blumetara AI gives users one place to store health information, understand reports, ask personalized 
health questions, track goals, and receive reminders. The user value is not just one feature; it is the 
integration of health memory, AI explanation, routine building, and progress tracking.
User Need Blumetara Promise Feature Support
I want to understand my reports. TARA explains reports in simple terms. Report upload, OCR, RAG, AI chat.
I forget health routines. Blumetara reminds me at the right time. Medicine reminders, water reminders, 
goal reminders.
I want to improve my health. The app tracks my goals and progress. Goal meter, dashboards, daily 
summaries.
I want personalized answers. Answers use my profile and health 
history.
Health profile, report memory, 
conversation memory.
I want family support. Future versions let family members 
monitor each other. Family accounts and admin/family views.
5.2 Value by Stakeholder
Stakeholder Value
End User Better understanding, better routine consistency, simplified 
health organization.
Family Member Future ability to monitor dependents and reduce manual 
follow-up burden.
Client/Business Owner AI-powered healthcare product with subscription and 
expansion potential.
Developer Team Clear modular product with realistic MVP scope and future 
technical roadmap.
Investor/Future Partner Scalable health platform vision with AI, data, subscriptions, 
and integrations.
5.3 Differentiation Strategy
Blumetara should not compete only as another AI chatbot. Its differentiation should come from combining 
document memory, health profile, reminders, goal tracking, and future family/wearable integrations. The 
product should be positioned as a personal health operating layer, not a generic Q&A bot.
Competitor Type Typical Strength Blumetara Differentiation
Generic AI chatbots Broad knowledge and natural 
conversation.
Personal health memory, report 
grounding, reminders, goals.
Reminder apps Simple alarms and notifications. Health-context-aware reminders and 
summaries.
Fitness apps Activity and nutrition tracking. Health reports + AI explanation + 
medical context.
Document storage apps Store files safely. AI reads, summarizes, and answers from 
stored reports.
Hospital portals Clinical records and appointments. Consumer-friendly day-to-day health co-
pilot experience.

6. Business Requirements
6.1 Business Requirement Categories
Business requirements define what the product must achieve for users and the business. They are not yet 
low-level technical requirements. Later volumes will convert these into system architecture, database 
schemas, API contracts, UI designs, and implementation tasks.
Category Requirement Summary
BR-01 User Onboarding Users must be able to create accounts, sign in, and complete a 
basic health profile.
BR-02 Health Memory Users must be able to store health reports and key health 
information securely.
BR-03 AI Assistance Users must be able to chat with TARA and receive personalized 
responses.
BR-04 Report Intelligence Uploaded reports must be processed for OCR, summarization, 
and report-based Q&A.
BR-05 Habit Support Users must be able to set reminders for medicines, water, and 
basic goals.
BR-06 Goal Tracking Users must be able to define and track health-related goals.
BR-07 Daily Summary Users must receive a basic end-of-day summary based on app 
activity.
BR-08 Admin Operations Admins must be able to view users, content, reports, usage, and 
system indicators.
BR-09 Monetization The platform must support free and paid tiers either in MVP or 
as a near-term extension.
BR-10 Safety The platform must avoid diagnosis claims and include medical 
disclaimers and escalation guidance.
6.2 Detailed Business Requirements
ID Requirement Description Priority
BR-01 Account Creation and 
Authentication
The product must allow users to 
register, sign in, and access 
their own private health 
workspace using secure 
authentication. Firebase 
Authentication is the expected

7. Free vs Paid Model
7.1 Business Logic of Freemium
A freemium model is appropriate because users need to experience the value of TARA AI before paying. 
However, AI usage, OCR, image analysis, and storage create real infrastructure cost. The free plan should 
provide enough value to attract users while keeping usage limits controlled. The paid plan should unlock 
frequency, personalization, family support, deeper insights, and premium convenience.
Pricing Principle
Do not make the free plan useless. Make it useful enough to build trust, but limited enough that consistent users 
naturally upgrade.
7.2 Suggested Free vs Paid Feature Matrix
Feature Free Plan Paid Plan
AI Chat Limited daily chats, e.g., 5 per day. Higher daily chats, e.g., 20 per day or more 
depending on cost.
Medicine Reminder One medicine or one reminder schedule. Multiple reminders plus future stock 
monitor.
Water Reminder Limited reminder options. Multiple reminder schedules and 
personalization.
Goals One active goal. Up to five or more active goals.
Goal Nudging Basic goal reminders. Goal-oriented nudging and analyzer.
Daily Summary Basic daily summary. Richer daily summary with 
recommendations and gaps.
Healthy Recipes Basic suggestions. Personalized recipes based on health profile 
and goals.
Workout Plans General workout plans. Dedicated workout plans based on health 
profile.
Insights Monthly or limited insight view. Weekly and monthly insights with goal-gap 
details.
Food Analyzer Limited image analysis, e.g., one per day. Higher limits, e.g., ten per day.
Nutrition Tracking Not available or basic. Available with history and goal linkage.
Report Upload Limited uploads and basic analyzer. More uploads, report guide, and advanced 
summary.
Fitness App Tracking Basic future integration. Advanced tracking and insights.
Family Accounts Single account. Family admin account can monitor family 
members.
Ads Ad-supported. Ad-free.
Support Email support. Priority email/callback support.
7.3 Feature Limits and Cost Control
The main cost drivers are LLM calls, OCR processing, embeddings, vector search, file storage, notification 
volume, and database usage. Usage limits should be designed early because they influence the backend 
schema and API authorization logic. Even if payment is not fully launched in the MVP, the product should 
be architected with plan-based limits from the beginning.
Cost Driver Why It Matters Control Mechanism
LLM calls Each chat and summary may consume 
tokens.
Daily quotas, model routing, response 
length limits, caching.
OCR Report and image processing can be 
expensive.
Upload limits, async processing, file-size 
limits.
Embeddings Every report chunk requires embedding 
generation.
Chunk size control, duplicate detection, 
paid upload limits.
Storage PDFs, images, food photos, voice files S3 lifecycle policy, file type limits, quotas 
--- PAGE 39 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 2
Draft v1.0 | Product Vision & Business Requirements
increase S3 cost. by plan.
Notifications Large user base increases scheduled jobs 
and push volume.
Batch processing, scheduler efficiency, 
paid feature boundaries.
Analytics Detailed analytics can increase storage 
and processing.
Retention policy and aggregation 
strategy.
7.4 Subscription Readiness in MVP
The MVP does not need a complex billing system on day one, but it should include a subscription-ready 
data model and feature gating strategy. If the app is built without plan awareness, adding subscriptions 
later may require significant refactoring across backend, mobile app, admin dashboard, and AI usage 
limits.
 Create a subscription or plan field for each user.
 Centralize feature-limit checks in backend services.
 Track AI usage, report uploads, image analysis, and reminders by user and plan.
 Allow admin override for testing, beta users, or promotional access.
 Do not hardcode limits directly into Flutter screens only; backend must enforce them.

8. User Journeys
8.1 New User Onboarding Journey
16. User installs or opens Blumetara mobile app.
17. User creates account using email, phone, or social login depending on Firebase configuration.
18. User completes basic profile setup and optional health profile details.
19. App introduces TARA AI and explains safety boundaries.
20. User is prompted to upload a health report, create a goal, or set a reminder.
21. Home dashboard shows next recommended action.
22. TARA uses the profile context in future responses.
8.2 Health Report Upload Journey
23. User chooses Upload Health Report.
24. User uploads PDF or image from device.
25. Backend validates file type, file size, and user plan limits.
26. File is stored in S3 and metadata is stored in MongoDB.
27. OCR/document parsing extracts text from the report.
28. Text is chunked and embedded for vector search.
29. TARA generates a simple report summary.
30. User can ask questions about the uploaded report.
31. TARA answers using retrieved report context and safety disclaimers.
8.3 AI Chat Journey
32. User opens TARA AI chat.
33. User asks a health-related question.
34. Backend checks user authentication, plan limits, and safety category.
35. System retrieves user profile, relevant reports, goals, reminders, and recent context.
36. RAG retrieves relevant report chunks when needed.
37. Prompt builder creates a controlled prompt for the LLM.
38. LLM returns a response.
39. Response is checked/formatted with medical safety boundaries.
40. Chat message is saved to the conversation history.
41. User receives a clear, personalized answer.
8.4 Reminder Journey
42. User creates medicine, water, or goal reminder.
43. Backend stores reminder schedule and notification preferences.
44. Scheduler or worker checks due reminders.
45. Push notification is sent through Firebase Cloud Messaging.
46. User marks reminder as done, skipped, or snoozed.
47. Progress is saved and included in daily summary.
8.5 Goal Tracking Journey
48. User creates a health goal such as weight loss, BP monitoring, calorie target, or diabetes tracking.
--- PAGE 41 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 2
Draft v1.0 | Product Vision & Business Requirements
49. User sets target, frequency, and reminder preferences.
50. App records progress entries or linked activity data.
51. Dashboard shows progress and goal meter.
52. TARA provides motivational and practical nudges.
53. Daily/weekly summaries explain progress and gaps.
8.6 Admin Journey
54. Admin logs into the React/Next.js dashboard.
55. Admin views user counts, active users, reports uploaded, AI usage, and notification status.
56. Admin can inspect support-level metadata without exposing unnecessary private medical content.
57. Admin monitors failed OCR jobs, API errors, payment status, and system health.
58. Admin exports or reviews high-level analytics for business decisions.

9. MVP Scope and Feature Prioritization
9.1 MVP Objective
The MVP objective is to validate the core Blumetara hypothesis: users will trust and repeatedly use an AI 
health co-pilot that remembers their profile, explains their reports, and helps them maintain daily health 
routines. The MVP must not attempt to become a complete hospital, pharmacy, insurance, wearable, and 
family-care ecosystem immediately.
9.2 MVP Must-Have Scope
MVP Feature Purpose Business Reason
Authentication Allow secure account access. Required for personal health data.
User/Health Profile Capture personalization context. Necessary for TARA personalization.
AI Chat Core TARA experience. Main product differentiator.
Report Upload Store user health reports. Foundation of health memory.
OCR + RAG Basics Enable report analysis and Q&A. Key AI value beyond generic chatbot.
Medicine Reminder Improve routine consistency. High practical value and low complexity.
Water Reminder Support simple habit formation. Easy feature with daily engagement.
Goal Tracking Let users set and monitor health goals. Creates long-term engagement.
Basic Dashboard Show user status and quick actions. Improves usability and retention.
Notifications Deliver reminders and nudges. Required for habit features.
Admin Dashboard Give operator visibility. Required for client/business operations.
9.3 MVP Should-Have Scope
Feature Reason Fallback if Time is Limited
Daily Summary Creates emotional closure and habit 
feedback.
Start with rule-based summary before 
AI-generated summary.
Basic Subscription Flag Prepares for monetization. Use free/pro flags without full payment 
integration.
Basic Analytics Helps founder understand usage. Track only core events initially.
Email Notifications Useful backup channel. Push-only in MVP if timeline is tight.
Healthy Recipe Suggestions Nice engagement feature. Move to V1 if personalization is weak.
9.4 Not MVP
Feature Why Not MVP Suggested Phase
Hospital APIs Requires partnerships, compliance, and 
clinical workflows. V2/V3
Pharmacy APIs Requires pharmacy integrations and 
medicine commerce logic. V2
Insurance APIs High complexity and regulatory/business 
dependencies. V3
Advanced Risk Prediction Could create clinical liability and 
requires validation. Future after expert review
Voice Assistant Useful but not essential for core 
validation. V2
Full Wearable Integration Requires platform permissions and data 
normalization. V2
Doctor Dashboard Different product surface and workflow. V2/V3
AI Agents with Autonomy Risky before core AI safety is mature. Future
--- PAGE 43 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 2
Draft v1.0 | Product Vision & Business Requirements
9.5 MVP Quality Bar
MVP does not mean low quality. It means controlled scope. The MVP can have fewer features, but the 
features it ships should be reliable, secure, understandable, and maintainable. Users are more likely to 
trust a simple product that works well than a large feature list that behaves unpredictably.
 Every feature must have clear empty states, error states, and loading states.
 Report processing must show status: uploaded, processing, ready, failed.
 AI responses must include safety boundaries and uncertainty handling.
 Reminder delivery should be testable and auditable.
 Admin dashboard must show operational visibility, not just decorative charts.
 Privacy and security must be included from day one.
--- PAGE 44 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 2

10. Monetization Strategy
10.1 Revenue Model Options
The most realistic initial revenue model is a freemium subscription. The free plan introduces users to 
TARA AI and basic reminders. The paid plan unlocks higher limits, advanced personalization, more report 
uploads, deeper insights, nutrition features, family accounts, and priority support. Enterprise, doctor, 
hospital, pharmacy, and insurance partnerships should be treated as future revenue models after 
consumer validation.
Revenue Model Fit for MVP Notes
Freemium Subscription High Best initial model. Allows user 
acquisition and paid upgrade path.
Family Plan Medium Strong future value for caregivers and 
parents.
Doctor Dashboard Subscription Future Requires professional workflow and 
compliance review.
Hospital Partnerships Future Requires sales cycle, integration, and 
trust.
Pharmacy Referral/Integration Future Potential but must avoid unsafe 
medication commerce behavior.
Insurance Partnerships Future High complexity; not MVP.
Ads Possible for free tier Must be handled carefully because 
healthcare context is sensitive.
10.2 Pricing Philosophy
Pricing should reflect value, cost, and trust. If AI usage costs are significant, paid plans should be designed 
around usage intensity. Heavy users who upload many reports, use image analysis, and ask many AI 
questions should pay more than light users. However, healthcare-related apps must be careful not to make 
essential safety information inaccessible.
 Free plan should allow basic personal health organization.
 Paid plan should monetize convenience, frequency, advanced insights, family monitoring, and 
personalization.
 LLM and OCR limits should be tied to plan economics.
 Annual plans can reduce churn and improve cash flow.
 Beta phase can offer discounted pricing in exchange for feedback.
10.3 Payment Gateway Strategy
The system design diagrams include Stripe and Razorpay as payment gateway options. The choice 
depends on launch geography and business registration. If launching first in India, Razorpay may be more 
practical. If targeting international users or Canada/US later, Stripe becomes important. The backend 
should abstract payment provider logic so that future providers can be added without rewriting 
subscription logic.
Gateway Strength Consideration
Razorpay Strong India support and local payment 
methods. Best if launch market is India.
Stripe Strong international SaaS subscription 
support. Best if expanding globally.
Both Maximum flexibility. Adds complexity; should be introduced

only when needed.

11. Success Metrics
11.1 MVP Success Definition
The MVP is successful if it proves that users understand the value, trust the AI enough to upload health 
information, return to the app for reminders or chat, and find report explanations useful. Technical 
completion alone is not success. Success requires product behavior and trust.
Success Area Metric Target Direction
Activation Percentage of new users completing 
health profile. Increase
Report Adoption Percentage of users uploading at least 
one report. Increase
AI Engagement Average TARA chats per active user per 
week. Increase with cost control
Reminder Use Percentage of users creating 
medicine/water reminders. Increase
Goal Tracking Percentage of users creating at least one 
goal. Increase
Retention Users returning after 7 and 30 days. Increase
Trust Low rate of unsafe AI feedback or 
complaints. Keep very low
Monetization Free-to-paid conversion after value 
discovery. Increase
Operational Reliability Failed OCR jobs, failed notifications, 
backend errors. Decrease
11.2 Product Analytics Events
Product analytics should be implemented from the MVP stage. Without event tracking, the team will not 
know which features are valuable. Analytics must avoid storing unnecessary sensitive medical content. 
Track behavior metadata, not private health details, unless strictly required and consented.
Event Name Trigger Purpose
user_signed_up User completes account creation. Measure acquisition.
profile_completed User completes health profile. Measure activation.
report_uploaded User uploads report. Measure health memory adoption.
report_processed OCR/RAG processing completes. Measure system reliability.
tara_chat_started User starts AI chat. Measure AI engagement.
goal_created User creates goal. Measure commitment.
reminder_created User creates reminder. Measure habit-feature adoption.
reminder_completed User marks reminder done. Measure routine success.
daily_summary_viewed User opens daily summary. Measure insight consumption.
upgrade_clicked User clicks upgrade. Measure monetization intent.

Average API response time Poor speed reduces trust. Lower
AI response latency Long waits reduce chat engagement. Lower
OCR failure rate Report analysis depends on extraction. Lower
Notification delivery success Reminders are core value. Higher
Crash-free sessions Mobile trust depends on stability. Higher
Support tickets per 100 users Shows UX and reliability issues. Lower
AI safety incident count Healthcare AI must be safe. Near zero

12. Risks, Assumptions, and Constraints
12.1 Business Risks
Risk Impact Mitigation
MVP scope becomes too large Delays, poor quality, unfinished product. Strictly separate MVP, V1, and V2.
Users do not trust AI with health data Low adoption. Clear privacy messaging, safe responses, 
strong UX, transparency.
AI costs become high Paid plans may not cover operational 
cost.
Usage limits, model routing, caching, 
quotas.
Client expects medical diagnosis Legal and product safety risk. Define product as health co-pilot, not 
doctor replacement.
Free plan overuse Infrastructure cost with no revenue. Plan limits and abuse monitoring.
Payment adoption is low Weak monetization. Improve paid value, family plan, insights, 
priority support.
12.2 Product Risks
Risk Impact Mitigation
TARA gives generic responses Product feels like basic chatbot. Use profile, reports, goals, and memory 
in context builder.
Report parsing is inaccurate Wrong or confusing summaries. OCR confidence, user review, 
disclaimers, robust parsing.
Reminder fatigue Users disable notifications. Allow schedule control and smart limits.
Too many features confuse users Low activation and retention. Guide onboarding toward one first 
action.
Admin dashboard overbuilt Time wasted on low-value features. Keep admin MVP operational and simple.
12.3 Technical Constraints Affecting Business
Business requirements must respect technical realities. AI healthcare products require careful design 
around latency, cost, data privacy, provider limits, and security. Features like food image analysis, 
wearable integration, family monitoring, and clinical risk prediction should be phased rather than 
bundled into the MVP.
Constraint Business Meaning
LLM rate limits and costs Free plan and chat limits are necessary.
OCR accuracy limitations Report analysis must allow uncertainty and manual review.
Healthcare data sensitivity Security work cannot be postponed.
Mobile notification dependency Reminder reliability depends on OS permissions and FCM 
delivery behavior.
Third-party APIs Hospital/pharmacy/insurance integrations require partnerships 
and legal review.
App store policies Health claims must be careful and compliant with platform 
guidelines.
12.4 Assumptions
 The first release targets consumer users, not hospitals or doctors.
 Existing LLMs will be used; Blumetara will not train its own foundational model in MVP.
 The platform will store files in object storage and metadata in the database.
 The MVP will use plan-based limits or be designed so plan-based limits can be added easily.
 Users will voluntarily provide health information and accept privacy terms before using AI features.
 The MVP will not claim to diagnose, prescribe, or replace professional medical advice.

13. Acceptance Criteria
13.1 Business Acceptance Criteria for MVP
Area Acceptance Criteria
Onboarding A new user can create an account, complete profile setup, and 
understand what TARA can and cannot do.
AI Chat A user can ask TARA questions and receive safe, personalized, 
understandable answers.
Report Upload A user can upload a PDF/image report, see processing status, 
and later view report summary.
Report Q&A A user can ask questions about an uploaded report and receive 
answers based on report context.
Reminders A user can create medicine and water reminders and receive 
push notifications.
Goals A user can create and update a basic health goal and view 
progress.
Daily Summary A user can receive or view a basic summary of reminders, 
goals, and daily activity.
Admin An admin can view users, report uploads, basic analytics, and 
operational status.
Safety The app clearly avoids medical diagnosis claims and uses 
disclaimers where appropriate.
Monetization Readiness The system has subscription-ready structure or feature gating 
foundation.
13.2 Product Review Checklist
 Does the user understand the value within the first three minutes?
 Can the user complete one meaningful action immediately: upload report, ask TARA, create goal, or set 
reminder?
 Does every AI response feel safe and appropriately bounded?
 Is the MVP focused, or has it become overloaded with V1/V2 features?
 Can the business explain why someone would upgrade to paid?
 Can the admin understand usage and operational health?
 Can future developers understand why features were included or excluded?
13.3 Business Definition of Done
A feature is not complete merely because code exists. A product feature is complete when it satisfies user 
need, business purpose, technical reliability, and safety expectations. For Blumetara, this is especially 
important because AI and health data are involved.
Definition of Done Item Requirement
User flow complete User can complete the task without developer assistance.
Error handling complete The app handles validation errors, failed uploads, failed AI 
calls, and empty states.
Admin visibility present Important operational events are visible to admin or logs.
Analytics event tracked Core product actions are tracked in privacy-conscious analytics.
Safety reviewed AI or health-related output has disclaimers and boundaries.
Documentation updated Product and technical documentation reflect the implemented 
behavior.

15. Instructions for Later Volumes
15.1 Impact on Volume 3 - MVP Scope
Volume 3 should convert the business requirements into a strict MVP scope document. It should define 
must-have, should-have, could-have, and future features with feature acceptance criteria, development 
effort, risk, dependencies, and sprint mapping.
15.2 Impact on Volume 4 - System Architecture
Volume 4 should ensure the architecture supports TARA AI, report memory, reminders, goals, admin 
visibility, subscriptions, and future integrations without overengineering the MVP. The modular monolith 
should remain the preferred backend model unless clear scaling requirements prove otherwise.
15.3 Impact on Volume 5 - Database Design
Volume 5 should design data models around user profile, health reports, conversations, reminders, goals, 
subscriptions, analytics events, and audit logs. Database design must support plan limits and future family 
accounts even if not fully implemented in MVP.
15.4 Impact on Volume 6 - AI/RAG/OCR
The AI volume must implement TARA as a bounded health assistant with user context, report context, 
prompt safety, medical disclaimers, model routing, and cost control. It should treat RAG and OCR as core 
product features, not optional add-ons.
15.5 Impact on Commercial Proposal
The commercial proposal should explain that pricing is based on product strategy, architecture, AI 
integration, cloud setup, testing, deployment, documentation, and maintenance - not merely typing code. It 
--- PAGE 52 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 2
Draft v1.0 | Product Vision & Business Requirements
should also clearly separate development cost from third-party costs such as AWS, MongoDB Atlas, 
Firebase, LLM APIs, payment gateway fees, domains, and app store accounts.
16. Volume 2 Closing Summary
Volume 2 defines Blumetara AI as a focused AI health co-pilot product centered on TARA AI. The business 
foundation is clear: help users remember health information, understand reports, maintain daily routines, 
track goals, and eventually upgrade to advanced paid features. The MVP must validate trust, report usage, 
AI engagement, reminders, and goal tracking. Later versions can expand into food analysis, nutrition, 
family accounts, wearables, doctor workflows, and third-party healthcare integrations.
Next Recommended Volume
Volume 3 should be the MVP Scope & Feature Specification. It should convert this business strategy into a buildable 
feature list with priorities, acceptance criteria, dependencies, and sprint-ready requirements.

delivery blueprint. It defines what should be built first, what should be deliberately postponed, how 
features should be accepted, and how the team should avoid scope creep.
Core Scope Rule
The MVP should prove that users trust and repeatedly use TARA AI to store reports, ask personalized health 
questions, track goals, and follow reminders. Anything that does not validate this hypothesis should be deferred 
unless it is required for safety, authentication, storage, or basic operations.

1. MVP Scope Philosophy
1.1 What MVP Means for Blumetara AI
For Blumetara AI, MVP does not mean a rough prototype, a demo-only chatbot, or a low-quality app. It 
means a deliberately limited first production version that proves the core value proposition while 
maintaining strong engineering discipline. The MVP should be small enough to complete within the target 
delivery window, but professional enough that it can be extended into Version 1 and Version 2 without 
being rebuilt from scratch.
The MVP should answer one strategic question: will users find value in an AI health co-pilot that 
remembers their profile, stores their reports, explains their health information, and helps them follow 
daily routines? If the answer is yes, the platform can expand toward nutrition tracking, wearable 
integration, family monitoring, pharmacy APIs, hospital APIs, insurance workflows, and advanced AI 
agents.
MVP Is MVP Is Not
A controlled first release with production foundations. A half-built demo with no maintainability plan.
A validation tool for core user behavior. A complete healthcare ecosystem.
A platform foundation that supports later expansion. A throwaway prototype to be rewritten later.
A focused set of high-value features. Every feature from the pitch deck implemented at once.
A safe AI assistant with clear boundaries. A diagnostic medical device or doctor replacement.
1.2 Why Scope Control Matters
Blumetara AI has a large long-term vision. The uploaded notes mention AI chat, report analysis, medicine 
reminders, stock monitoring, water reminders, goals, nudging, goal meters, daily summaries, recipes, 
workout plans, weekly/monthly insights, food analysis, nutrition tracking, fitness app reading, family 
accounts, ads, premium support, and integrations. That vision is strong, but building all of it in the first 
release would create delivery risk, quality risk, safety risk, and cost risk.
 The first release must be small enough to complete, test, and deploy properly.
 A healthcare-related product must prioritize trust and safety over feature volume.
 AI features require careful prompting, grounding, logging, and fallback behavior.
 Every additional feature adds database, API, UI, testing, security, and maintenance work.
 A focused MVP gives the client a working product faster and creates a cleaner path for paid future versions.
Founder/Client Positioning
Do not present deferred features as failures. Present them as roadmap discipline. A serious software team does not 
build all possible features in the first version; it builds the right first version and then scales based on evidence.

2. Product Hypothesis and Validation Goals
2.1 Core Product Hypothesis
Core Hypothesis
Users will repeatedly use Blumetara AI if TARA can safely explain their health reports, remember their health 
profile, help them track goals, and remind them about important daily routines.
This hypothesis should drive the MVP. Features that directly test this hypothesis should be prioritized. 
Features that are interesting but do not directly test this behavior should move to MVP+ or Version 1.
2.2 Validation Questions
Question How MVP Tests It Metric
Will users upload health reports? Provide report upload, metadata storage, 
and AI summary. Report uploads per active user.
Will users ask TARA health questions? Provide AI chat grounded in profile and 
reports. Chats per user per week.
Do users value personalized responses? Use profile, goals, and report context in 
prompts. Repeat chat usage and feedback ratings.
Do reminders create engagement? Medicine, water, and goal reminders 
with push notifications. Reminder completion rate.
Do goals create retention? Goal creation, progress logging, and 
dashboard progress. Goals created and updated per user.
Can admin operate the product? Provide basic admin dashboard and 
usage visibility.
Support resolution and operational 
visibility.
2.3 MVP Success Metrics
Metric Category MVP Metric Target Direction
Activation Percentage of users completing profile 
setup. Increase
Report Usage Number of reports uploaded per active 
user. Increase
AI Engagement Number of TARA conversations per 
active user. Increase
Retention Users returning after 7 days and 30 days. Increase
Reminder Utility Medicine/water/goal reminders marked 
completed. Increase
AI Safety Unsafe or overconfident medical 
responses. Decrease
Reliability Failed OCR jobs, failed uploads, 
notification failures. Decrease
Cost Control Average AI cost per active user. Stable and understood
2.4 What the MVP Must Prove
 Users understand the purpose of TARA AI after onboarding.
 Users can securely create an account and manage a health profile.
 Users can upload health reports and receive a useful summary.
 TARA can answer report-related questions using retrieved context.
 Users can create and receive medicine, water, and goal reminders.
 Users can see progress on a simple health dashboard.
 Admins can monitor basic usage, users, reports, and system health.
--- PAGE 58 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 3
Draft v1.0 | MVP Scope Finalization & Delivery Blueprint
 The product can be deployed, maintained, and extended without major rewrites.
2.5 What the MVP Does Not Need to Prove
 It does not need to prove clinical diagnosis accuracy.
 It does not need direct hospital, pharmacy, or insurance integrations.
 It does not need full wearable synchronization.
 It does not need an autonomous medical agent.
 It does not need full family-account management if timeline is tight.
 It does not need food image analysis and nutrition history in the first release unless the client explicitly 
funds MVP+.

3. MVP Boundary Definition
3.1 MVP Feature Boundary
The MVP boundary defines the minimum feature set required to deliver a coherent product. A coherent 
MVP is not just a collection of screens. It must contain a complete user loop: user creates profile, uploads 
data or creates goals, asks TARA questions, receives reminders, views progress, and returns again.
Layer MVP Boundary
Mobile App
Flutter app with authentication, onboarding, dashboard, TARA 
chat, report upload, reminders, goals, profile, notifications, and 
settings.
Admin Dashboard
Basic React/Next.js dashboard for user visibility, report/job 
monitoring, AI usage summary, and manual support 
operations.
Backend
FastAPI modular monolith with auth validation, user/profile 
services, chat service, reports service, reminders service, 
notification service, goals service, admin service, and analytics 
events.
Database
MongoDB Atlas collections for users, profiles, conversations, 
messages, health reports, report chunks, goals, reminders, 
notifications, audit logs, subscriptions/plan flags.
File Storage AWS S3 for PDFs, images, and report assets. MongoDB stores 
metadata only.
AI TARA chat using LLM provider, prompt builder, safety layer, 
report context retrieval, and structured response formatting.
RAG/OCR Basic OCR for uploaded reports, chunking, embeddings, vector 
storage/search, and context retrieval.
Notifications Firebase Cloud Messaging for reminders and app nudges.
Payments
Plan-aware architecture and optional Razorpay/Stripe 
integration depending on commercial decision. Full payment 
automation may be MVP+.
3.2 MVP User Loop
17. User signs up and completes a basic health profile.
18. User uploads a health report or creates a goal/reminder.
19. System stores files in S3 and metadata in MongoDB.
20. OCR extracts report text and the RAG pipeline prepares searchable chunks.
21. User asks TARA a question about health, reports, goals, or routine.
22. TARA builds context from profile, reports, goals, and prior conversation.
23. TARA responds with clear, safe, educational guidance.
24. System sends reminders and tracks completion.
25. Dashboard shows progress and next actions.
26. User returns because TARA and reminders create repeated value.
3.3 MVP Technical Boundary
Decision Area MVP Decision Why
Architecture Modular monolith. Simpler delivery, easier debugging, 
enough scalability for early stage.
Backend FastAPI. Strong Python ecosystem for AI, APIs, 
async tasks, and ML-adjacent services.
Database MongoDB Atlas. Flexible schema for profiles, reports, 
logs, goals, and AI conversations.

Storage S3 for files, MongoDB for metadata. Avoid storing large PDFs/images inside 
the database.
Authentication Firebase Auth with backend token 
verification. Faster secure user identity setup.
Notifications Firebase Cloud Messaging. Suitable for mobile push reminders.
AI Provider Gemini/OpenAI initially. Use existing LLMs; do not build a custom

4. MoSCoW Prioritization
MoSCoW prioritization classifies features as Must Have, Should Have, Could Have, and Won't Have in 
MVP. This prevents every stakeholder request from being treated as equally urgent.

User and Health Profile Required for personalization. Must
TARA AI Chat Core product experience. Must

context. Must
Medicine Reminder High-value everyday utility. Must
Water Reminder Simple habit feature and daily 
engagement driver. Must
Goal Tracking Core personalized coaching loop. Must
Notifications Required for reminders and nudges. Must
Basic Dashboard Gives user overview and next actions. Must
Basic Admin Dashboard Required for operations and client 
visibility. Must
Audit Logging Required for sensitive app operations. Must
4.2 Should Have Features
Feature Reason Fallback
Daily Summary Strong retention feature. Start with rule-based summary if AI 
summary is delayed.
Basic Subscription Flag Needed for future monetization. Create plan field even if payment is 
manual initially.
Basic Analytics Events Needed for business learning. Track only signup, chat, upload, 
reminder, goal events.
Report Summary PDF/View Improves report feature experience. Show AI-generated summary inside app 
only.
Email Notifications Useful backup for account and reports. Use push-only first if timeline is tight.

Healthy Recipes Nice engagement, but not core 
report/chat validation.

database.
Food Image Analyzer Interesting AI feature, but cost and 
accuracy risk. Move to V1/MVP+.

5.1 MVP Dependency Map
The most important dependency chain is profile -> reports -> OCR/RAG -> TARA chat -> 
dashboard/summary. Authentication must come first because almost every feature depends on the user 
identity. File storage must be stable before OCR and RAG. Notifications must be stable before reminders. 
Admin visibility should be developed in parallel with backend events and audit logs.
Dependency Chain Features Affected Risk if Ignored
--- PAGE 64 ---
