Authentication -> User ID Profile, reports, chat, reminders, goals, 
subscriptions. Data ownership and privacy break.
S3 Upload -> Report Metadata OCR, RAG, report summary, admin 
report view. Files become untraceable or insecure.
OCR -> Chunking -> Embeddings Report Q&A, summary, search. TARA cannot answer report-specific 
questions.
Prompt Builder -> Safety Layer AI chat, report Q&A, daily summary. Unsafe or generic AI responses.
Reminder Store -> Scheduler -> FCM Medicine, water, goals. Users do not receive reminders.
Event Logs -> Admin Analytics Admin dashboard, metrics, debugging. Client cannot monitor product usage.

6. Detailed MVP Feature Specifications
This section provides build-ready scope definitions for MVP features. Later volumes will convert these into 
database schemas, API contracts, screen designs, and implementation tasks.
F01 - Authentication and Account Access
Item Decision
Priority P0 - Must Have
Phase MVP
Primary Owner Backend + Flutter
Objective Allow users to securely create accounts, sign in, sign out, and 
access only their own data.
Included in MVP
 Firebase Authentication for user identity.
 Backend JWT/token verification for protected FastAPI routes.
 Basic sign up, login, logout, password reset or provider-based recovery depending on Firebase setup.
 User record creation in MongoDB after first sign-in.
 Basic role support: user and admin.
Excluded from MVP
 Complex multi-organization auth.
 Doctor-specific account workflow.
 Enterprise SSO.
 Advanced family permissions in MVP.
Acceptance Criteria
 Unauthenticated users cannot access protected APIs.
 User can sign up and sign in successfully.
 Backend maps Firebase user ID to MongoDB user record.
 Admin routes cannot be accessed by normal users.
 Invalid or expired tokens return safe errors.
F02-F03 - User and Health Profile
Item Decision
Priority P0 - Must Have
Phase MVP
Primary Owner Flutter + Backend
Objective Collect enough user context for TARA personalization without 
creating excessive onboarding friction.
Included in MVP
 Basic personal profile fields such as name, age range/date of birth, gender if user chooses to provide it, 
height, weight, and preferences.
 Health context fields such as goals, conditions user voluntarily enters, allergies, medications, and lifestyle 
preferences.
 Profile edit screen.
 Consent/safety note explaining that the app is not a doctor.
--- PAGE 66 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 3
Draft v1.0 | MVP Scope Finalization & Delivery Blueprint
 Backend validation for sensitive fields.
Excluded from MVP
 Full clinical health record.
 Doctor-verified diagnosis model.
 Government health ID integration.
 Complex family-member profiles in first MVP.
Acceptance Criteria
 User can complete onboarding without entering every optional field.
 Profile can be updated.
 TARA can access allowed profile fields for personalization.
 Sensitive fields are not exposed in admin views unnecessarily.
 Profile data is tied to authenticated user only.
F04-F05 - TARA AI Chat
Item Decision
Priority P0 - Must Have
Phase MVP
Primary Owner AI + Backend + Flutter
Objective Deliver the core TARA AI experience: personalized, safe, 
context-aware health Q&A and guidance.
Included in MVP
 Chat UI in Flutter.
 Conversation and message storage.
 LLM integration using Gemini/OpenAI/Claude-compatible provider abstraction.
 Prompt builder that includes profile, goals, and relevant report context.
 Safety system prompt and medical disclaimer behavior.
 Basic rate limits and plan limits.
 Error fallback when LLM fails.
Excluded from MVP
 Autonomous AI agent execution.
 Medical diagnosis.
 Prescription changes.
 Emergency triage as a certified service.
 Unlimited free chat usage.
Acceptance Criteria
 User can send and receive messages.
 Chat history persists.
 Responses use user profile/report context when relevant.
 TARA avoids diagnosis/prescription language.
 LLM failures produce helpful non-technical fallback messages.
 Chat usage can be counted per user for future plan limits.

F06 - Health Report Upload and Storage
Item Decision
Priority P0 - Must Have
Phase MVP
Primary Owner Backend + Cloud + Flutter
Objective Allow users to upload health reports as PDFs or images and 
store them securely for future AI retrieval.
Included in MVP
 Upload PDF/image from mobile app.
 File type and size validation.
 S3 object storage.
 MongoDB metadata record.
 Upload status: uploaded, processing, ready, failed.
 Basic report list and report detail view.
Excluded from MVP

 Manual doctor review workflow.
 Complex document classification beyond basic report type.
 Hospital system import.
Acceptance Criteria

 Unsupported files are rejected safely.

 User can see uploaded reports in app.
 Users cannot access other users' files.
 Failed uploads or processing jobs show understandable status.

Included in MVP

 Chunk extracted text into retrieval-friendly sections.
 Generate embeddings.
 Store vectors and chunk metadata.
 Retrieve top relevant chunks for user questions.
 Pass retrieved context to prompt builder.
 Basic report summary generation.

Excluded from MVP

7. Explicit Non-MVP Features
This section is intentionally strict. Clear exclusions protect the project from uncontrolled expansion. A 
feature excluded from MVP is not rejected forever; it is simply moved to a later phase.
Excluded Feature Reason for Exclusion Future Requirement Before Building
Food and prescription analyzer by image
High AI accuracy and safety risk; requires 
image processing, nutrition logic, and 
medical guardrails.
V1 scope, safety design, cost limits, 
validation dataset.
Nutrition tracking
Requires food database, logging UX, 
calorie/macronutrient logic, and long-term 
charts.
V1 data model and UX design.
Dedicated workout plans Useful but requires careful personalization 
and risk disclaimers. V1 workout rules and safety boundaries.
Medicine stock monitor Requires inventory UX and repeated 
medicine tracking. V1 medicine module expansion.
Family account monitoring Requires permissions, consent, privacy, and 
role design. V1 identity and authorization design.
24x7 heart rate/BP/oxygen/glucose analyzer Requires wearable/device integration and 
possibly medical regulatory review.
V2 wearable architecture and compliance 
review.
SOS alerts to relatives Emergency-related feature with serious 
reliability expectations.
V2 safety/legal review and high-availability 
notification plan.
Hospital APIs Requires partner APIs, contracts, security 
reviews, and healthcare data standards. V2/V3 partnership strategy.
Pharmacy APIs
Requires commerce or stock integration, 
partner dependencies, and prescription 
safety.
V2 pharmacy partnership.
Insurance APIs Requires complex business and compliance 
integrations. V3 enterprise roadmap.
Specialized medical LLMs Potentially useful but cost, availability, and 
safety validation must be studied.
AI evaluation, legal review, and budget 
approval.
Custom LLM training Unnecessary for MVP and too costly. Long-term research only if data and 
business scale justify it.
7.1 Language for Client Discussions
When discussing exclusions with the client, avoid saying "we cannot build this." Instead, say: "This is a 
strong roadmap feature, but including it in MVP will increase timeline, cost, testing, and safety risk. The 
recommended approach is to build the foundation now and schedule this for Version 1 or Version 2."
Scope Communication Template
This feature is valuable, but it is not required to validate the MVP. We will design the system so the feature can be 
added later without major rework, but we should not include it in the first delivery unless timeline and budget are 
revised.

8. MVP+ and Version 1 Scope
MVP+ is the bridge between the first release and Version 1. These features are attractive and commercially 
useful, but they should be treated as separate milestones after the core MVP is stable.
8.1 MVP+ Candidate Features
Feature Why It Matters Build Condition
Healthy Recipes Creates daily engagement and supports 
lifestyle positioning. Add after profile and AI chat are stable.
Basic Workout Plan Supports goal coaching and paid-plan 
value. Start with safe template-based plans.
AI Daily Summary Improves retention and perceived 
intelligence. Use after event logging is stable.
Razorpay/Stripe Payments Enables subscription revenue. Add when plan limits are finalized.
Email Support Flow Improves operational support. Add if client needs support process in 
launch.
8.2 Version 1 Feature Set
Version 1 Feature Description Dependency
Food Image Analyzer User uploads food image and receives 
estimated food/nutrition explanation. Image upload, AI vision, usage limits.
Nutrition Tracking Food logs, calories, macros, and nutrition 
summaries. Food model and dashboard expansion.
Dedicated Workout Plans Workout suggestions based on profile 
and goals. Health profile and safety rule set.
Weekly and Monthly Insights Goal gap details, reminder trends, and 
report history summary. Analytics events and summary service.
Medicine Stock Monitor Track medicine remaining quantity and 
refill alerts. Medicine data model expansion.
Family Accounts Admin account can monitor family 
members with consent.
Role-based permissions and privacy 
model.
Priority Support Paid-plan support workflow. Admin dashboard and support processes.
8.3 Version 1 Business Goal
Version 1 should convert the MVP from a useful personal health assistant into a stronger subscription 
product. The main business goal is to create enough paid-plan value that users understand why premium 
exists. Version 1 should focus on increased personalization, more limits, family support, and recurring 
insights rather than adding unrelated features.

9. Version 2 and Long-Term Scope
Version 2 is where Blumetara AI can begin evolving from a personal health management app into a 
broader healthcare ecosystem. These features are powerful but require stronger architecture, compliance 
review, partnerships, and operational maturity.
Long-Term Feature Strategic Value Prerequisites
Wearable Integration Automated activity, heart rate, sleep, and 
health metric tracking.
Apple Health/Google Fit integration, 
permissions, data normalization.
Voice AI More natural interaction and accessibility. Speech-to-text, text-to-speech, privacy 
controls.
Doctor Dashboard Allows professionals to review patient 
summaries.
Consent model, role-based access, legal 
review.
Hospital APIs Connect clinical data sources. Partnerships, healthcare standards, security 
review.
Pharmacy APIs Medication refill and availability 
workflows.
Pharmacy partnerships and prescription 
safety.
Insurance APIs Claims, wellness plans, or policy 
integrations. Enterprise partnerships and compliance.
AI Agents Multi-step assistance such as reminder 
planning and report comparison.
Mature safety layer, tool permissions, audit 
logs.
Predictive Health Analytics Early warning insights from long-term data. Validated models, expert review, regulatory 
clarity.
9.1 Long-Term Architecture Implication
Even though these features are not in MVP, the MVP must avoid architectural decisions that make them 
impossible later. The most important foundations are clean user identity, strong data ownership, modular 
backend services, extensible database collections, event logging, and audit trails. The MVP should be 
simple, but not careless.

11. Acceptance Criteria and Definition of Done
11.1 MVP Acceptance Criteria
Area Acceptance Criteria
Authentication Users and admins can sign in securely; unauthorized access is 
blocked.
Profile Users can create, view, and update profile and health profile 
information.
AI Chat TARA responds to user questions, uses relevant profile/report 
context, and follows safety boundaries.
Report Upload Users can upload supported PDF/image reports; files are stored 
in S3 and metadata appears in app.
OCR/RAG Uploaded reports are processed into text/chunks/embeddings 
and can be used in report Q&A.
Reminders Medicine and water reminders can be created and push 
notifications are delivered in tested conditions.
Goals Users can create goals, update progress, and see status on 
dashboard.
Dashboard Dashboard summarizes reports, goals, reminders, and TARA 
entry point.
Admin Admin can view users, usage, reports/job status, and key 
operational metrics.
Security Users cannot access each other's data. Sensitive endpoints 
require authentication.
Deployment Application is deployed to the selected AWS environment and 
basic monitoring is active.
Documentation Handover documentation explains setup, environment 
variables, deployment, and core workflows.
11.2 Definition of Done
 Feature is implemented in frontend and backend where applicable.
 API validation and error handling are complete.
 Database persistence is tested.
 User ownership and authorization rules are enforced.
 Basic unit/integration tests are written for critical paths.
 Manual QA checklist is passed.
 Admin visibility exists for operationally important workflows.
 Logs are available for debugging failures.
 Feature has no known high-severity bug.
 Client can understand and demo the feature.
 Documentation is updated.

12. Sprint Delivery Blueprint
The MVP is estimated as a 10-12 week delivery. The sprint plan below assumes disciplined scope control 
and limited rework. If the client adds major features such as nutrition tracking, family accounts, or 
payment automation, timeline and cost must be revised.
Sprint Focus Primary Deliverables
Sprint 0 Requirements and architecture setup
Confirm scope, finalize workflows, create 
repositories, environments, design system, 
initial backlog.
Sprint 1 Foundation FastAPI skeleton, Flutter skeleton, Firebase 
Auth setup, MongoDB connection, basic CI.
Sprint 2 Authentication and profile
Signup/login, user record, profile 
onboarding, protected routes, user 
ownership model.
Sprint 3 Reports and storage S3 upload, report metadata, report 
list/detail, file validation, upload status.
Sprint 4 OCR processing OCR/text extraction worker, processing 
status, error handling, report text storage.
Sprint 5 RAG foundation Chunking, embeddings, vector search, 
report summary generation.
Sprint 6 TARA AI chat Chat UI, conversation APIs, prompt builder, 
LLM integration, safety layer.
Sprint 7 Goals and reminders Goal CRUD, medicine/water reminders, 
scheduler, notification integration.
Sprint 8 Dashboard and daily summary User dashboard, progress cards, upcoming 
reminders, summary logic.
Sprint 9 Admin dashboard Admin login, users, reports/jobs, usage 
cards, audit log view.
Sprint 10 Testing and hardening QA, bug fixes, rate limits, security review, 
performance checks.
Sprint 11 Deployment and handover Production deployment, docs, client demo, 
training, warranty start.
12.1 Delivery Milestones
Milestone Completion Signal
M1 - Scope Lock Client signs off MVP scope and exclusions.
M2 - Technical Foundation Auth, database, storage, and CI/CD foundations are running.
M3 - Core AI Loop Report upload -> OCR -> RAG -> TARA answer works end-to-end.
M4 - Routine Loop Goals, reminders, notifications, and dashboard work end-to-
end.
M5 - Admin Visibility Admin can monitor users, reports, AI usage, and failures.
M6 - Production Release App is deployed, tested, documented, and handed over.

13. Scope Creep Controls
Scope creep is one of the largest risks for this project because the product vision is broad and exciting. The 
following controls should be used during every client discussion.
13.1 Change Request Policy
27. Every new feature request must be written down clearly.
28. Classify the request as MVP, MVP+, V1, V2, or future research.
29. Estimate impact on timeline, cost, testing, and safety.
30. Decide whether it replaces another feature or increases scope.
31. Do not start building until the client approves the scope impact.
32. Maintain a change log so there is no confusion later.
13.2 Scope Impact Matrix
Client Request Type Likely Impact Recommended Response
Small UI copy change Low Accept within sprint if no design impact.
Additional field in profile Low/Medium Accept if database and privacy impact is 
minimal.
New reminder type Medium Evaluate scheduler, notification, UI, and 
testing impact.
Food analyzer High Move to MVP+ or revise quote/timeline.
Family accounts High Move to V1 unless already included in 
paid scope.
Wearables Very High Move to V2 with separate architecture 
design.
Doctor dashboard Very High Separate product module and quote.
Medical risk prediction Critical Requires expert validation and legal 
review.
13.3 Approved Scope Language
Client-Friendly Scope Statement
For the MVP, we will focus on the features required to validate TARA AI as a personal health co-pilot: profile, 
reports, AI chat, OCR/RAG, reminders, goals, dashboard, notifications, and admin visibility. Additional features such 
as food analysis, family monitoring, wearables, and hospital APIs are part of the roadmap and can be scheduled 
after MVP stabilization.

14.1 Safety Risk Mitigation
 Always position TARA as educational and supportive, not diagnostic.
 Add medical disclaimer in onboarding and relevant AI responses.
 Detect emergency-like language and direct users to local emergency services or qualified professionals.
 Avoid dosage changes, prescription recommendations, or disease diagnosis.
 Log AI safety failures during testing and improve prompts before launch.
 Keep human review optional for edge cases in future versions, not as a fake promise in MVP.

to develop and operate. The MVP should avoid premature microservices but should maintain clean internal boundaries so 
future scaling is possible.

1. Architecture Overview and Design Goals
Blumetara AI should be designed as a secure, AI-powered personal health platform centered around the TARA AI 
Health Co-Pilot. The MVP architecture must support authentication, health profile management, report upload, 
OCR extraction, RAG-based question answering, reminders, goals, notifications, admin visibility, and basic 
subscription readiness. The platform should be production-minded but not overengineered.
Architecture Goal Meaning for Blumetara MVP Consequence
Maintainability The codebase should be understandable by a 
small team and future developers.
Use modular monolith, feature modules, 
service layer, repository layer, and 
consistent naming.
Security The product handles sensitive health-related 
data.
Use Firebase Auth/JWT, HTTPS, RBAC, 
encrypted storage, input validation, rate 
limits, audit logs, and secure secrets.
Scalability The MVP should not block future growth.
Keep modules separable, add queues for 
background tasks, store files in S3, and use 
managed databases.
Cost Control Startup cloud and AI costs should be 
predictable.
Avoid Kubernetes/microservices early, use 
managed services carefully, cap AI usage, 
cache where safe.
AI Safety TARA must guide users responsibly without 
claiming diagnosis.
Use system prompts, medical disclaimers, 
risk detection, emergency escalation, and 
source-aware report answers.
Core Architecture Statement
Blumetara AI MVP should be a FastAPI modular monolith deployed on AWS, consumed by Flutter and React clients, storing 
operational data in MongoDB Atlas, storing files in S3, using Firebase for auth/notifications, and routing AI work through a 
dedicated AI Orchestrator with OCR and RAG services.

3. Architecture Principles
Principle Rule Reason
Modular monolith first
Do not split MVP into microservices unless a 
module has a proven scaling or ownership 
need.
Microservices increase deployment, 
observability, networking, testing, and 
debugging complexity.
Clean boundaries
Every feature module should expose routes, 
schemas, services, repositories, and models 
cleanly.
Prevents spaghetti code and makes future 
extraction possible.
API-first design Flutter and admin dashboard should 
consume documented REST APIs.
Keeps frontend/backend contracts clear and 
testable.
Secure by default No endpoint should trust client input or 
unverified identity.
Healthcare-related data requires stronger 
protection than a casual consumer app.
Async where required
Long-running OCR, embedding, report 
processing, notifications, and emails should 
not block user requests.
Improves user experience and backend 
reliability.
Observable from day one
Every important request, error, AI call, 
upload, and background job should be 
logged.
Debuggability is essential for production 
support and maintenance.
These principles should be treated as guardrails during development. When an implementation decision conflicts 
with a principle, the team should document the reason and whether it is temporary or permanent.

Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 4

4. End-to-End Request Flow
The architecture can be understood through a normal user flow. A user opens the Flutter app, authenticates 
through Firebase, receives a token, and calls the FastAPI backend through the protected edge and entry layers. 
The backend validates the token, checks authorization, routes the request to the correct module, executes 
business logic through services, persists data through repositories, and calls external providers only through 
abstraction layers.
Step Flow System Responsibility
1 User opens Flutter app or admin opens 
React dashboard.
Client initializes auth state, API client, 
notification token, and app configuration.
2 Request travels through Cloudflare and AWS 
entry layer.
DNS, CDN, TLS, WAF, DDoS protection, and 
load balancing protect and route traffic.
3 FastAPI receives request.
Middleware validates request, logs 
metadata, applies rate limits, and routes to 
module endpoint.
4 Module calls service layer.
Service enforces business rules, 
authorization checks, and transaction-like 
orchestration.
5 Repository interacts with data stores.
MongoDB handles structured metadata; S3 
handles files; vector DB handles 
embeddings/chunks.
6 External services are called if required.
Firebase, LLM provider, OCR provider, 
payment gateway, email, or future third-
party health APIs.
7 Response returned to client. API returns normalized JSON with 
success/error state; UI updates accordingly.
8 Async jobs continue in background.
Celery/worker handles reminders, report 
processing, notifications, emails, summaries, 
and analytics events.
Key Flow Rule
The client should never call LLM providers, S3 privileged APIs, payment providers, or internal admin operations directly. 
The backend is the trust boundary and orchestration layer.
--- PAGE 93 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 4
Draft v1.0 | Complete System Architecture
5. Client Layer - Flutter App and React Admin Dashboard
The client layer is the user-facing part of Blumetara AI. It consists of a Flutter mobile app for users and a 
React/Next.js-style admin dashboard for operational staff. The clients must remain thin enough that sensitive 
business logic, authorization decisions, AI prompting, storage access, and payment verification stay on the 
backend.
5.1 Responsibilities
 Provide user-facing screens and workflows.
 Collect user inputs and files safely.
 Display AI responses, health profile information, reminders, reports, goals, and dashboard summaries.
 Use Firebase authentication state and backend-issued API contracts.
 Receive push notifications through Firebase Cloud Messaging.
 Avoid storing sensitive data permanently on device unless explicitly required and encrypted.
5.2 Key Components
Component Role in Architecture MVP Implementation Guidance
Flutter Mobile App Primary application for patients and individual 
users.
Feature-based architecture with auth, 
dashboard, chat, reports, goals, reminders, 
notifications, profile, and subscription screens.
React Admin Dashboard Operational web dashboard for admin and 
support use.
Start with user management, analytics, report 
visibility, AI usage monitoring, notification 
controls, and audit log views.
API Client Client-side communication wrapper.
Centralize base URL, token handling, retries, 
request IDs, error formatting, and response 
parsing.
Local Cache Temporary data for performance and offline 
tolerance.
Cache non-sensitive view data carefully; avoid 
long-term local medical storage in MVP.
5.3 Architecture Decisions
Thin-client rule
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Business logic must stay in FastAPI, not Flutter/React.
Why this is recommended Keeps security and maintainability strong.
Tradeoffs More API calls may be needed compared to local-heavy logic.
Implementation note Use UI state only for presentation, not final authorization or medical 
decision rules.
Single backend contract
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Both clients should consume stable REST APIs.
Why this is recommended Reduces duplicate backend logic and simplifies testing.
Tradeoffs Admin may need special endpoints and RBAC.
Implementation note Create /api/v1/mobile and /api/v1/admin groups only if needed for 
clarity.
5.4 Risks and Controls
Risk Impact Control
Token leakage Compromised device could expose auth token. User data risk.
UI/Backend mismatch Screens may assume features not supported by 
API. Broken UX.
Admin over-permission Admin dashboard can become dangerous. Data privacy risk.

6. Edge and Entry Layer - Cloudflare, Route 53, WAF, Load Balancer
The edge and entry layer protects and routes inbound traffic before it reaches the FastAPI backend. For the MVP, 
the architecture can use Cloudflare for DNS/CDN/DDoS/TLS and AWS entry services such as Route 53, WAF, and 
Application Load Balancer depending on deployment choices. The diagram includes both Cloudflare and AWS 
entry components; in implementation, the team should avoid duplicating services unnecessarily unless there is a 
clear reason.
6.1 Responsibilities
 Manage domain routing and TLS.
 Protect APIs against common malicious traffic.
 Apply WAF rules and request-size limits.
 Route traffic to backend compute.
 Provide a stable public endpoint for mobile app and admin dashboard.
 Support future horizontal scaling.
6.2 Key Components
Component Role in Architecture MVP Implementation Guidance
Cloudflare DNS, CDN, DDoS protection, SSL/TLS, edge 
caching for static assets.
Use for domain, frontend protection, basic WAF 
rules, and static asset acceleration.
Route 53 AWS DNS service. Use only if AWS-native DNS is preferred; avoid 
duplicate DNS ownership confusion.
AWS WAF Web Application Firewall. Apply managed rules for bots, common attacks, 
and malicious payloads.
Application Load Balancer / API Gateway Routes traffic to backend instances or 
containers.
Use ALB for container/EC2/ECS deployment; API 
Gateway if serverless/API management is 
preferred.
6.3 Architecture Decisions
Cloudflare plus AWS edge
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Use Cloudflare at the outer edge and AWS ALB/WAF for backend 
routing when needed.
Why this is recommended Layered protection and flexible DNS/CDN.
Tradeoffs Can increase configuration complexity and SSL certificate confusion.
Implementation note Document the final DNS/TLS ownership clearly before deployment.
ALB over API Gateway for MVP
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision If FastAPI runs on EC2/ECS/App Runner, ALB is straightforward.
Why this is recommended Works well for long-running backend and WebSocket-like future 
needs.
Tradeoffs API Gateway gives richer API management but adds limits and 
pricing considerations.
Implementation note Choose based on compute target in deployment volume.
6.4 Risks and Controls
Risk Impact Control
Misconfigured TLS App may fail or expose insecure traffic. Security and availability issue.
WAF false positives Legitimate requests may be blocked. Bad user experience.
Large file uploads Health reports may exceed gateway limits. Upload failures.

7. FastAPI Modular Monolith
The FastAPI backend is the core application layer. It should be built as a modular monolith: one deployable 
backend application with clear internal modules. This gives the MVP speed and simplicity while keeping future 
microservice extraction possible. The backend owns business rules, authorization, AI orchestration, data 
consistency, payment verification, file storage coordination, and admin operations.
7.1 Responsibilities
 Expose REST APIs for mobile and admin clients.
 Validate Firebase JWTs and enforce role-based permissions.
 Coordinate business workflows across modules.
 Call service layer for AI, storage, OCR, notifications, payments, analytics, and audit logs.
 Normalize errors and responses.
 Provide consistent logging and observability.
7.2 Key Components
Component Role in Architecture MVP Implementation Guidance
API Routers FastAPI route groups for each domain module. Use /api/v1/auth, /users, /profiles, /reports, /chat, 
/goals, /reminders, /admin.
Schemas/DTOs Pydantic request and response validation. Never pass raw MongoDB documents directly to 
clients.
Domain Services Business logic layer. Keep endpoints thin; services enforce rules and 
call repositories/providers.
Repositories Data access abstraction. Keep MongoDB queries isolated and testable.
Middleware Cross-cutting request processing. Auth, request ID, logging, rate limiting, CORS, 
exception handling.
7.3 Architecture Decisions
Modular monolith
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision One deployable backend with module boundaries.
Why this is recommended Best balance for MVP cost, speed, and maintainability.
Tradeoffs Requires discipline to avoid modules becoming tightly coupled.
Implementation note Create feature folders and explicit service/repository contracts.
FastAPI
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Python backend framework optimized for APIs and AI integrations.
Why this is recommended Strong typing, async support, Pydantic validation, Python AI 
ecosystem.
Tradeoffs Requires careful async/sync dependency management.
Implementation note Use FastAPI dependency injection and structured project layout.
7.4 Risks and Controls
Risk Impact Control
Spaghetti module coupling Future scaling becomes painful. High maintenance cost.
Blocking long jobs OCR or embeddings may slow API requests. Timeouts and poor UX.
Weak validation Bad data enters database. Data quality/security risk.
7.5 Future Evolution
 Extract high-load modules into separate services later if necessary.

8. Backend Domain Modules
The backend should be divided by business capability. Each module should own its route handlers, schemas, 
service, repository, and tests. Cross-module dependencies should go through service interfaces rather than direct 
database access across module boundaries.
Module Purpose Implementation Boundary
Authentication Validates Firebase tokens, user onboarding, 
role assignment, session-related backend rules.
Firebase Auth, JWT middleware, user 
repository, RBAC service.
User Profile Stores personal profile, health profile, 
preferences, notification settings.
Profile service, health-profile schema, settings 
API.
AI Chat Handles TARA conversations, chat messages, 
prompt orchestration, AI response storage.
Conversation service, message repository, AI 
orchestrator.
Health Reports
Uploads metadata, controls S3 file flow, triggers 
OCR/RAG processing, displays report 
summaries.
Report service, storage service, OCR jobs, vector 
chunks.
Goals Tracks goals such as weight, water, calories, BP 
monitoring, diabetes monitoring.
Goal service, progress logs, dashboard 
aggregation.
Medicine Stores medicine schedules and basic adherence 
logs.
Medicine service, reminder scheduler, 
notification service.
Reminders General reminder engine for water, medicine, 
goals, summaries.
Reminder service, Celery tasks, FCM 
integration.
Nutrition Food logging and later image analysis/nutrition 
tracking.
MVP can include basic shell or defer advanced 
analysis.
Workout Workout plans based on profile. Defer advanced personalization to V1 if MVP 
scope is tight.
Subscription Plan limits, entitlements, payment status. Plan service, Stripe/Razorpay provider, usage 
limits.
Admin User management, content controls, 
operational dashboards. Admin APIs, audit logs, analytics summaries.
Analytics Usage metrics, AI cost metrics, report 
processing metrics. Analytics service and event collection.
Module Boundary Rule
A module may depend on shared infrastructure such as database connection, auth context, logging, and settings. It should 
not directly manipulate another module's collections unless that access is intentionally wrapped through a service or 
repository interface.

9. Service Layer
The service layer contains reusable internal services that are not tied to a single user-facing module. These 
services encapsulate infrastructure integrations and cross-cutting business operations such as AI orchestration, 
OCR, RAG, file storage, notifications, payments, email, analytics, user activity tracking, and audit logging.
9.1 Responsibilities
 Provide clean abstractions over external providers.
 Prevent route handlers from containing provider-specific logic.
 Enable provider replacement later.
 Centralize retries, timeouts, error mapping, cost controls, and logs.
 Support testing through mocks and fake providers.
9.2 Key Components
Component Role in Architecture MVP Implementation Guidance
AI Orchestrator Service Routes AI tasks to Gemini/OpenAI and applies 
prompt, context, safety, and logging. All LLM calls must go through this service.
RAG Service Chunk retrieval, vector similarity search, 
context selection. Used by chat and report Q&A.
OCR Service Extracts text from PDFs/images/prescriptions. Can use Google Vision, AWS Textract, or 
another provider behind an interface.
File/Storage Service S3 presigned upload/download, metadata 
linking, file validation. Never expose permanent public S3 object URLs.
Notification Service FCM push, reminder notifications, in-app 
notifications. Centralize device tokens and delivery results.
Payment Service Stripe/Razorpay payment and subscription 
events. Verify webhooks server-side.
Audit Log Service Records sensitive operations. Required for admin actions, report access, AI 
calls, and data changes.
9.3 Architecture Decisions
Provider abstraction
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Wrap every external provider behind internal service interfaces.
Why this is recommended Prevents vendor lock-in and improves testing.
Tradeoffs Takes extra upfront code.
Implementation note Define provider interface and concrete implementation.
Centralized AI orchestration
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision No module calls LLM directly.
Why this is recommended Improves safety, logging, cost control, and prompt consistency.
Tradeoffs AI service can become a bottleneck if poorly designed.
Implementation note Use internal methods per task type: chat, report summary, goal 
insight, daily summary.
9.4 Risks and Controls
Risk Impact Control
Provider outage LLM/OCR/payment/Firebase may fail. Feature degradation.
Cost runaway AI calls may grow unexpectedly. Budget risk.
Secrets leakage External API keys exposed. Critical security issue.

10. Data Access Layer
The data access layer separates business logic from database implementation. It should provide repositories that 
hide MongoDB query details from services. This is especially important because the MVP uses MongoDB Atlas for 
flexible document storage while also relying on S3 and vector search for files and embeddings.
10.1 Responsibilities
 Abstract MongoDB queries from business services.
 Centralize indexes, projection rules, pagination, soft delete, and ownership filters.
 Prevent accidental cross-user data exposure.
 Make database logic testable.
 Support future migration or module extraction.
10.2 Key Components
Component Role in Architecture MVP Implementation Guidance
Repository Classes One repository per aggregate or collection 
group.
UserRepository, ReportRepository, 
ConversationRepository, GoalRepository, 
ReminderRepository, SubscriptionRepository.
Models/Schemas Database model definitions and API schemas. Separate internal DB model from API response 
model.
Query Helpers Pagination, filters, sorting, ownership checks. Standardize list endpoints and admin searches.
Transaction-like Orchestration MongoDB session usage where needed. Use carefully for multi-collection consistency.
10.3 Architecture Decisions
Repository pattern
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Services do not call MongoDB directly.
Why this is recommended Improves maintainability and testability.
Tradeoffs Can feel verbose in small projects.
Implementation note Use repositories for all non-trivial persistence.
Soft delete for sensitive records
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Do not immediately hard-delete important records unless required.
Why this is recommended Supports auditability and recovery.
Tradeoffs Retention policies must be defined.
Implementation note Use deleted_at and status fields with privacy-aware deletion later.
10.4 Risks and Controls
Risk Impact Control
Ownership bugs User may see another user's data. Severe privacy issue.
Unindexed queries Slow dashboards and history pages. Performance issue.
Schema drift MongoDB flexibility can become chaos. Maintenance issue.
10.5 Future Evolution
 Introduce read models for dashboards.
 Add caching layer for frequently used profile and plan data.
 Use MongoDB change streams or event logs for analytics later.

11. Data Stores - MongoDB Atlas, AWS S3, Vector Database
Blumetara AI should use separate storage systems for separate data types. MongoDB Atlas stores application 
metadata and flexible domain documents. AWS S3 stores large files such as medical reports and images. A vector 
database or MongoDB Atlas Vector Search stores embeddings and report chunks for RAG. The architecture should 
never store large PDFs directly in MongoDB.
11.1 Responsibilities
 Store structured and semi-structured user data.
 Store large medical files securely outside the database.
 Store embeddings and chunks for report-aware AI responses.
 Support auditability, backups, and future analytics.
 Maintain data ownership boundaries.
11.2 Key Components
Component Role in Architecture MVP Implementation Guidance
MongoDB Atlas Primary operational database. Users, profiles, conversations, messages, goals, 
reminders, subscriptions, metadata, audit logs.
AWS S3 Object storage for files. Health reports, profile images, prescription 
images, food images, voice files, documents.
Vector Database / Atlas Vector Search Embeddings and chunks. Report chunks, document embeddings, 
metadata, retrieval indexes.
Backups Recovery and continuity. MongoDB backups, S3 versioning/backups, 
retention policy.
11.3 Architecture Decisions
Metadata in MongoDB, files in S3
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Store only file metadata and S3 keys in MongoDB.
Why this is recommended Scales better and avoids database bloat.
Tradeoffs Requires coordinated deletion and access management.
Implementation note Use storage service to link files and metadata.
Vector search beside operational DB
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Use Atlas Vector Search initially if it simplifies stack.
Why this is recommended Fewer systems to manage.
Tradeoffs Dedicated vector DB may scale better later.
Implementation note Choose based on cost and early performance needs.
11.4 Risks and Controls
Risk Impact Control
File access leakage Public or long-lived file URLs expose medical 
docs. Critical privacy issue.
Embedding data leakage Retrieved chunks may expose wrong user data. Critical privacy issue.
Backup gaps Data loss on failure. Business risk.
11.5 Future Evolution
 Move analytics to a warehouse later.
 Split vector search to Pinecone/Weaviate/OpenSearch if scale demands.

External services accelerate development but create dependency, privacy, security, and cost considerations. The

supports authentication and push messaging. LLM providers power TARA AI. Stripe/Razorpay support payments.

12.1 Responsibilities

13. AI/RAG Integration Layer
The AI/RAG layer is the intelligence center of Blumetara AI. It should let TARA answer questions using user 
profile, health history, report chunks, goals, and recent conversation context. However, it must operate with 
medical safety limits. TARA should explain, summarize, remind, and guide; it should not claim to diagnose, 
prescribe, or replace a medical professional.
13.1 Responsibilities
 Understand user query intent.
 Retrieve relevant profile/report/goal context.
 Build safe prompts for the selected LLM.
 Generate source-aware answers where report context is used.
 Store conversation history and summaries.
 Apply safety rules and escalation messaging.
13.2 Key Components
Component Role in Architecture MVP Implementation Guidance
Query Understanding Classifies user intent.
General health question, report question, goal 
question, reminder request, emergency/risk 
query.
Similarity Search Retrieves relevant chunks. Filter by user/report scope before ranking.
Prompt Builder
Combines system prompt, user profile, 
retrieved chunks, chat summary, and current 
query.
Keep prompt consistent and auditable.
LLM Gateway Calls Gemini/OpenAI/Claude. Handle timeout, retries, logging, and usage 
tracking.
Safety Layer Detects red flags and constrains responses. Emergency symptoms should trigger medical 
escalation advice.
13.3 Architecture Decisions
RAG for reports
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Use report chunks to answer document-specific questions.
Why this is recommended Reduces hallucination and improves personalization.
Tradeoffs OCR errors and chunk quality can affect answers.
Implementation note Show limitations and source snippets when possible.
Conversation summary memory
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Use summaries rather than sending entire chat every time.
Why this is recommended Controls token cost and improves relevance.
Tradeoffs Summaries can miss details.
Implementation note Keep key facts separately in profile/health memory.
13.4 Risks and Controls
Risk Impact Control
Hallucinated medical advice User may trust unsafe answer. High safety risk.
Prompt injection in uploaded files Report text may contain malicious instructions. AI safety/security risk.
Wrong-user retrieval RAG may retrieve another user's chunks. Critical privacy breach.

14. Background and Async Processing
Background workers handle tasks that should not block user-facing requests. In Blumetara AI, report processing, 
OCR, embeddings, scheduled reminders, daily summaries, email delivery, notification retries, and analytics 
aggregation are natural background jobs. The MVP can use Celery with Redis as broker/cache, or a managed 
alternative if deployment simplicity is preferred.
14.1 Responsibilities
 Run long-running tasks outside request-response path.
 Schedule reminders and summaries.
 Process report uploads into OCR text and embeddings.
 Retry transient provider failures.
 Record job status for user feedback.
 Reduce API timeouts and improve responsiveness.
14.2 Key Components
Component Role in Architecture MVP Implementation Guidance
Celery Worker Background job processor. Use for OCR, embeddings, reminders, daily 
summaries, emails, notification retries.
Redis Broker/cache. Use as Celery broker initially and cache later 
where safe.
Scheduler Periodic jobs. Medicine reminders, water reminders, daily 
summaries, analytics rollups.
Job Status Collection Tracks async processing state. Report processing: uploaded, queued, 
processing, completed, failed.
Dead Letter Handling Failed jobs that need admin attention. Manual retry or automated retry policies.
14.3 Architecture Decisions
Async report processing
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Return immediately after upload and process in background.
Why this is recommended Better UX and reliability.
Tradeoffs Requires status UI and retry handling.
Implementation note Create report_processing_status field and job logs.
Scheduled notifications
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Use backend scheduler rather than relying only on client alarms.
Why this is recommended Central control and multi-device support.
Tradeoffs Requires timezone correctness.
Implementation note Store user timezone and quiet hours.
14.4 Risks and Controls
Risk Impact Control
Timezone mistakes Reminders fire at wrong time. Trust issue.
Duplicate notifications Users get repeated alerts. Bad UX.
Worker outage Reports/reminders stop processing. Operational issue.
14.5 Future Evolution
 Move to managed queues like SQS/EventBridge if AWS-native architecture is preferred.

15. CI/CD and Release Architecture
CI/CD should make development safer and repeatable. The diagrams include GitHub, GitHub Actions, Docker 
build, push to ECR, and deploy to AWS. The MVP should implement a simple but reliable pipeline that runs 
linting, tests, Docker build, image push, and deployment to a staging/production environment.
15.1 Responsibilities
 Ensure every code change can be built and tested.
 Produce reproducible Docker images.
 Separate development, staging, and production environments.
 Protect production deployment through approvals.
 Support rollback.
 Avoid manual deployment mistakes.
15.2 Key Components
Component Role in Architecture MVP Implementation Guidance
GitHub Repository Source control. Separate repos or mono-repo depending on 
team preference; enforce branch protection.
GitHub Actions CI/CD automation. Run lint, tests, build, image push, deploy.
Docker Container packaging. Dockerize FastAPI backend and worker.
ECR Container registry. Store versioned backend images.
AWS Deployment Target EC2/App Runner/ECS. Choose simple target for MVP; document 
deployment flow.
15.3 Architecture Decisions
Docker-first backend
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Package backend consistently across local/staging/prod.
Why this is recommended Reduces environment mismatch.
Tradeoffs Requires Docker discipline and secrets separation.
Implementation note Use env vars and secrets manager, not hardcoded config.
Staging before production
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Deploy to staging before client demos/production.
Why this is recommended Catches mistakes early.
Tradeoffs Takes extra setup.
Implementation note Use separate MongoDB/S3/Firebase config for staging.
15.4 Risks and Controls
Risk Impact Control
Broken deployment Production outage. Availability risk.
Secrets in repo API keys leak. Critical risk.
No tests in pipeline Bugs ship easily. Quality risk.

 Add blue/green deployments if user base grows.
 Add automated database migration checks and deployment approvals.

16. Security Architecture
Security must be built into every layer because Blumetara AI handles health-related data and AI-generated 
guidance. The MVP should implement a realistic security baseline: Firebase Auth, JWT verification, RBAC, HTTPS, 
input validation, rate limiting, encrypted storage, private S3 objects, secure secrets, audit logs, and prompt-
injection defenses.
16.1 Responsibilities
 Authenticate every protected request.
 Authorize access at object level.
 Protect files and health data.
 Validate inputs and uploads.
 Limit abuse and AI cost attacks.
 Record sensitive actions.
 Prevent prompt injection and RAG data leakage.
16.2 Key Components
Component Role in Architecture MVP Implementation Guidance
JWT Authentication Backend validates Firebase token. Use middleware/dependencies for protected 
routes.
RBAC Role-based access control. Roles: user, admin, support, doctor/future.
Input Validation Pydantic and file validation. Reject malformed requests and dangerous 
uploads.
Rate Limiting Protect APIs and AI calls. Per-user and per-IP limits.
Encryption At rest and in transit. HTTPS, MongoDB Atlas encryption, S3 
encryption.
Audit Logs Track sensitive operations. Admin actions, report access, AI calls, payment 
changes.
16.3 Architecture Decisions
Object-level authorization
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Every report/chat/goal query must verify ownership.
Why this is recommended Prevents cross-user data exposure.
Tradeoffs Adds query complexity.
Implementation note Use auth context and repository filters.
Private S3 with presigned URLs
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Files are never public.
Why this is recommended Protects medical documents.
Tradeoffs Requires backend-managed upload/download flow.
Implementation note Use short expiry and content-type restrictions.
16.4 Risks and Controls
Risk Impact Control
Broken access control User accesses another user's health data. Critical privacy failure.
Prompt injection Uploaded docs override AI behavior. AI safety risk.
AI abuse Users consume excessive tokens. Cost risk.

17. Observability and Operations
A production app must be observable. The MVP should include structured logs, request IDs, error tracking, 
metrics, background job visibility, AI usage tracking, and basic admin/system health views. CloudWatch can be 
the starting point, with future expansion to dedicated observability tools if needed.
17.1 Responsibilities
 Track API health and errors.
 Monitor AI cost and latency.
 Monitor background jobs and notification delivery.
 Support debugging of user issues.
 Detect failures before users report them.
 Provide operational visibility to admin/support roles.
17.2 Key Components
Component Role in Architecture MVP Implementation Guidance
Structured Logs JSON or consistent application logs. Include request_id, user_id hash, endpoint, 
status, latency, error type.
CloudWatch AWS logs and metrics. Start with backend/worker logs, alarms, 
CPU/memory, error rates.
AI Usage Logs Token/cost/provider/task tracking. Needed for subscription limits and cost 
monitoring.
Job Metrics Worker queue length, job success/failure. Required for OCR/reminder reliability.
Admin Health View Operational dashboard. Show active users, report processing status, AI 
usage, failures.
17.3 Architecture Decisions
Request ID everywhere
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Propagate request ID from edge to logs.
Why this is recommended Makes debugging easier.
Tradeoffs Requires middleware and log formatting.
Implementation note Return request_id in error responses.
AI cost observability
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Track every AI call.
Why this is recommended Prevents surprise bills.
Tradeoffs Adds logging/privacy considerations.
Implementation note Store minimal prompt metadata, not unnecessary sensitive content.
17.4 Risks and Controls

No logs Bugs are hard to debug. Maintenance risk.
Sensitive logs Health data may leak into logs. Privacy risk.
No alerts Failures go unnoticed. Reliability risk.

18. Scalability Architecture
The MVP should be simple today but capable of scaling tomorrow. This means avoiding premature microservices 
while preparing clear seams: stateless backend containers, externalized storage, background queues, managed 
databases, module boundaries, rate limits, and provider abstractions. Scaling should happen in stages based on 
real usage data.
18.1 Responsibilities
 Support early users without overengineering.
 Allow horizontal scaling of backend and workers.
 Prevent database and AI cost bottlenecks.
 Prepare for future module extraction.
 Scale file and vector processing independently.
18.2 Key Components
Component Role in Architecture MVP Implementation Guidance
Stateless Backend Multiple backend instances can run behind 
load balancer.
Store sessions in Firebase/client tokens, not 
local memory.
Worker Scaling Increase worker count for reports/reminders. Separate queues by job type later.
MongoDB Scaling Indexes, read/write optimization, backups. Design indexes and pagination early.
S3 Scaling Object storage scales automatically. Use lifecycle policies and private access.
AI Scaling Usage limits, provider routing, caching. Track costs by user and task.
18.3 Architecture Decisions
Scale by bottleneck
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Do not scale every layer at once.
Why this is recommended Cost-efficient and evidence-driven.
Tradeoffs Requires metrics.
Implementation note Use observability to decide scaling work.
Microservice extraction later
Aspect Architecture Decision
Decision Only extract modules when load/team complexity justifies.
Why this is recommended Avoids premature complexity.
Tradeoffs Requires clean module boundaries now.
Implementation note Candidate future services: AI, notifications, reports, payments.
18.4 Risks and Controls
Risk Impact Control
Database hot spots Slow dashboards or chat histories. Performance issue.
AI latency Chat feels slow. UX issue.
Worker backlog Reports process slowly. Trust issue.
18.5 Future Evolution
 Move AI orchestration to separate service at high load.
 Introduce Redis caching for plan/profile/config.
 Add analytics warehouse for reporting.
 Use ECS/Kubernetes only when operational maturity justifies it.

ID Decision Status Rationale
ADR-001 Use Modular Monolith for MVP Accepted
Microservices are unnecessary for 
current team size and feature 
maturity. Modular monolith gives 
delivery speed and future 
extraction path.
ADR-002 Use FastAPI as backend 
framework Accepted
Python is strong for AI

Centralizes prompts, safety,

abstraction.

API requests.

high without clinical validation 
and compliance review.

20. Failure Scenarios and Recovery
Failure Scenario Impact Recovery Strategy
LLM provider timeout User chat request fails or delays. Return friendly retry message, log event, 
optionally retry with fallback provider.
OCR provider fails Report remains unprocessed. Mark report status as failed, allow retry, notify 
user/admin.
Worker down Reminders and report processing stop. CloudWatch alert, restart worker, process 
queued jobs.
MongoDB unavailable Most app functions fail. Show maintenance message, retry backoff, 
restore service with provider support.
S3 upload fails Report/image cannot be saved. Retry upload, validate file size/type, show clear 
error.
Firebase notification failure Reminder not delivered. Record delivery failure, retry where 
appropriate, show in-app notification.
Payment webhook failure Subscription status not updated. Verify webhook retries, idempotency keys, 
manual admin reconciliation.
Cross-user access bug Data privacy incident.
Immediately disable affected endpoint, audit 
logs, patch ownership checks, notify 
stakeholders as required.
Recovery Principle
Every critical workflow should have an observable status. Users and admins should know whether a report is uploaded, 
queued, processing, completed, failed, or retrying. Silent failures destroy trust.

21. Implementation Sequencing
Architecture should be implemented in a controlled order. Do not begin AI complexity before identity, data 
ownership, file storage, logging, and module boundaries are stable.
Phase Architecture Work Expected Output
Phase 0 Repository setup, environment config, Docker 
baseline, coding standards.
Runnable backend skeleton and frontend 
placeholders.
Phase 1 Firebase Auth integration, JWT middleware, 
user/profile module.
Authenticated user identity and secure profile 
storage.
Phase 2 MongoDB repositories, base models, audit 
logging, error handling. Reliable data access pattern.
Phase 3 S3 storage service and health report upload 
metadata. Secure report upload pipeline.
Phase 4 Background worker, report processing status, 
OCR service stub/implementation. Async report processing foundation.
Phase 5 Chunking, embeddings, vector search, RAG 
service. Report-aware retrieval pipeline.
Phase 6 AI Orchestrator and chat module. TARA chat with profile/report context.
Phase 7 Goals, medicine/water reminders, notification 
service. Habit and reminder MVP.
Phase 8 Admin dashboard, analytics, monitoring, CI/CD 
hardening. Operational MVP ready for client review.

22. Architecture Acceptance Checklist
Area Acceptance Criteria
Authentication All protected APIs validate Firebase JWT and map to internal user 
record.
Authorization Every user-owned resource query filters by authenticated user and 
family/role permissions where applicable.
Module Boundaries Routes call services; services call repositories/providers; routes do 
not contain provider logic.
File Storage Files are private in S3; MongoDB stores metadata only; presigned 
URLs expire quickly.
AI Safety LLM calls go through AI Orchestrator; prompts include safety rules 
and no diagnosis/doctor replacement claim.
RAG Security Vector search filters by user/report metadata before returning 
chunks.
Async Jobs OCR, embeddings, reminders, daily summaries, and notifications 
run through workers/schedulers.
Observability Structured logs, request IDs, errors, job status, and AI usage are 
recorded.
CI/CD Backend builds and deploys through repeatable pipeline, not 
manual command history.
Secrets No secrets in client apps or repository; provider keys stored in 
environment/secrets manager.
Admin Admin actions are RBAC-protected and audit logged.
Scalability Backend is stateless and can run multiple instances behind load 
balancer.
Volume 4 Completion Standard
This architecture is acceptable when a developer can look at the system diagrams, module responsibilities, service 
boundaries, data store responsibilities, and decision records and understand exactly how the MVP should be assembled 
without guessing the system shape.

1. Backend Executive Summary
The Blumetara AI backend is the trust boundary and orchestration layer of the product. It should never be treated as a 
simple API wrapper around the mobile app. It owns authentication verification, authorization, health profile logic, AI 
workflow orchestration, file storage access, report processing, reminders, notifications, subscriptions, admin visibility, 
and auditability.
The recommended backend architecture is a FastAPI modular monolith. This gives the project the speed and simplicity 
required for an MVP while still enforcing clean boundaries between product domains. Each module should have its 
own routes, schemas, services, repositories, and tests. Shared infrastructure concerns should live in dedicated service 
abstractions rather than leaking into modules.
Backend Area Recommended Approach Reason
API Framework FastAPI
High performance, Python-native, async 
support, automatic OpenAPI generation, strong 
fit for AI workflows.
Architecture Style Modular monolith Avoids microservice complexity while 
preserving future separation boundaries.
Business Logic Service layer Keeps routes thin and makes logic testable.
Data Access Repository pattern Prevents database logic from spreading across 
services.
Validation Pydantic schemas Ensures consistent request/response validation 
and type safety.
Auth Firebase token verification + backend RBAC Delegates identity while keeping authorization 
rules inside backend.
Async Jobs Celery/RQ/worker style processing
Moves OCR, embeddings, reminders, 
summaries, emails, and notifications out of 
request path.
Observability Structured logs + request IDs + metrics Makes production debugging and maintenance 
possible.
Non-Negotiable Backend Rule
No client should directly control sensitive operations. All file upload permissions, report access, AI context selection, 
payment verification, admin access, and notification sends must be mediated by the backend.
--- PAGE 128 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 5
Draft v1.0 | Backend Architecture & Module Design
2. Backend Principles
Principle Backend Rule
Routes stay thin Route handlers should parse requests, call services, and return responses. 
They should not contain heavy business logic.
Services own business logic A service should decide whether an operation is allowed, which 
repositories to call, and which external services are needed.
Repositories own persistence MongoDB query logic, indexes, filters, pagination, and data access should 
live behind repositories.
External APIs are abstracted Firebase, LLMs, S3, OCR, payments, email, and analytics should be 
accessed through dedicated internal services.
Errors are normalized The backend should return predictable errors with codes, messages, 
request IDs, and safe details.
Security is central Authentication, RBAC, input validation, rate limiting, audit logs, and 
secrets management must be built from the beginning.
AI is orchestrated, not scattered All LLM calls should go through an AI Orchestrator so prompts, costs, 
safety, model choice, and logging are controlled.
Async by default for heavy work OCR, embeddings, report parsing, daily summaries, bulk notifications, 
and reminders should be background tasks.
Decision 2.1 - Modular Monolith Over Microservices
Aspect Backend Decision
Decision Use a modular monolith for MVP backend implementation.
Why
The project needs speed, clarity, low DevOps overhead, and 
maintainability. A modular monolith supports clean boundaries without 
introducing distributed system complexity.
Tradeoffs
Microservices can scale independently but require service discovery, 
networking, distributed tracing, multiple deployments, event contracts, 
and operational maturity.
Guardrails Keep each module isolated internally so future extraction is possible if 
usage grows.
Decision 2.2 - Backend Owns AI Safety
Aspect Backend Decision
Decision Route all AI calls through backend AI services, never directly from Flutter 
or the admin dashboard.
Why Healthcare-adjacent AI needs central control over prompts, context, data 
access, risk checks, disclaimers, and audit logs.
Tradeoffs Adds backend workload and latency, but protects safety and privacy.
Guardrails Use AIOrchestratorService, PromptBuilder, RAGService, 
SafetyGuardrailService, and AIUsageLogger.
--- PAGE 129 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 5
Draft v1.0 | Backend Architecture & Module Design
3. Modular Monolith Strategy
A modular monolith is a single deployable backend application whose internal codebase is separated into clear 
business modules. For Blumetara, this is ideal because the MVP requires multiple features but the team should not 
carry the operational burden of many services. The system should be packaged and deployed as one backend 
application, but internally it should feel like a group of well-defined modules.
Module Boundary Owns Should Not Own
Auth Identity verification, token decoding, role 
checks, auth dependencies. User health profile business logic.
Users/Profile User profile, preferences, health baseline 
metadata. Raw report processing or LLM prompts.
AI Chat Conversation creation, messages, AI response 
orchestration. OCR extraction pipeline details.
Health Reports File metadata, report processing status, 
extracted text, report summaries.
Payment verification or admin role 
management.
Goals Goal definitions, progress logs, goal summaries. Notification delivery infrastructure.
Reminders Medicine/water reminder scheduling and state. Firebase provider implementation details.
Notifications Notification templates, delivery tracking, push 
integration. Goal business rules.
Subscriptions Plans, entitlements, payment status. Clinical or health guidance logic.
Admin Administrative views, moderation, operational 
actions.
Regular user flows unless through controlled 
service calls.
Future Extraction Rule
A module should only become a separate microservice when there is a clear scaling, security, team ownership, or 
deployment reason. Possible future candidates are AI Orchestrator, Notification Service, Payment Service, and Report 
Processing Service.
--- PAGE 130 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 5
Draft v1.0 | Backend Architecture & Module Design
4. Layered Architecture
The backend should be layered so that each concern has a clear place. This prevents the common MVP failure where 
route files become huge and impossible to maintain.
Layer Contains Responsibility Example
API Layer FastAPI routes and dependencies
HTTP contract, request parsing, 
response mapping, dependency 
injection.
POST /api/v1/reports/upload
Schema Layer Pydantic models
Validate request bodies, query 
parameters, and response 
structures.
ReportUploadResponse, 
GoalCreateRequest
Service Layer Business services
Business rules, orchestration, 
authorization checks, external 
service calls.
HealthReportService.process_repo
rt
Repository Layer Database access classes Queries, inserts, updates, 
pagination, aggregation, indexes.
HealthReportRepository.find_by_u
ser
Infrastructure Services External provider wrappers Firebase, S3, LLM, OCR, email, 
payment, analytics.
StorageService.generate_presigned
_url
Worker Layer Background tasks Long-running work and scheduled 
jobs. process_report_ocr_job
Core Layer Config/security/logging/errors Reusable framework-level utilities. settings, auth_dependency, 
exception_handler
4.1 Request Handling Rule
A request should flow from route to schema validation to dependency checks to service method to repository or 
external service call, then back through a response schema. The route should not directly query MongoDB, call LLMs, 
write S3 objects, or send notifications. This rule makes the backend testable and readable.

while allowing shared cross-cutting services. The exact filenames can evolve, but the separation of responsibilities 
should remain.

5.1 Folder Structure Rules
 Every module should contain schemas.py, service.py, repository.py, and optionally routes.py if routes are not 
centralized in api/v1.
 External providers should live under services/ or infrastructure/ and should be injected into modules rather than 
imported everywhere.
 Core security, logging, exception handling, and configuration should be centralized.
 Workers should call service-layer functions where possible instead of duplicating business logic.
 Tests should mirror module boundaries so each module can be validated independently.
--- PAGE 133 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 5
Draft v1.0 | Backend Architecture & Module Design
6. Dependency Injection and Configuration
FastAPI dependency injection should be used to provide authenticated users, role checks, database connections, 
settings, and shared services. Dependency injection prevents hard-coded global state and makes unit testing easier.
Dependency Purpose Implementation Guidance
get_current_user Verify Firebase JWT and return authenticated 
backend user context. Used by all protected user endpoints.
require_admin Verify user has admin role. Used by admin routes and sensitive operations.
get_db Provide MongoDB database/session object. Should reuse connection pool and not 
reconnect per request.
get_storage_service Provide S3 abstraction. Hides AWS implementation details from 
modules.
get_ai_orchestrator Provide AI orchestration service. Centralizes model calls, prompting, RAG, safety, 
and logging.
get_settings Provide environment configuration. Loads from env/secrets, validates required 
settings on startup.
Configuration Rule
No API keys, database URLs, Firebase credentials, or payment secrets should ever be hard-coded. Use environment variables 
locally and AWS Secrets Manager or equivalent secure secret storage in production.
--- PAGE 134 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 5
Draft v1.0 | Backend Architecture & Module Design
7. Request Lifecycle
Stage What Happens Failure Handling
Client request Flutter/Admin sends HTTPS request with token 
and request body. Reject missing token for protected routes.
Edge protection Cloudflare/WAF/load balancer applies TLS, 
basic protection, and routing. Block suspicious traffic before backend.
Middleware Request ID, logging, CORS, rate limit, and body-
size checks are applied.
Return 429 for rate limit, 413 for too-large files, 
400 for malformed request.
Auth dependency Firebase JWT is verified and mapped to 
backend user.
Return 401/403 for invalid token or insufficient 
role.
Schema validation Pydantic validates request input. Return 422 with safe validation details.
Service method Business rules execute. Raise domain-specific errors with safe public 
messages.
Repository/provider call Data access or external service call happens. Use retries, timeouts, and circuit-breaker style 
protection where needed.
Response mapping Return normalized response payload. Never leak stack traces or secrets.
Audit/logging Log business event and technical trace. Ensure logs avoid sensitive medical content 
unless explicitly sanitized.
7.1 Response Envelope Recommendation
For consistency, API responses should follow a predictable structure such as: success, data, error, request_id, and 
timestamp. This improves frontend error handling and debugging. Not every endpoint must wrap responses if the team 
prefers pure REST, but consistency is critical.

Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 5
Draft v1.0 | Backend Architecture & Module Design
8. Authentication Module
The Authentication Module verifies identity and attaches a safe user context to every protected operation. Firebase can 
handle identity creation and token issuance, but the backend must still verify tokens, map users to internal records, 
and enforce roles.
8.1 Responsibilities
 Verify Firebase ID tokens.
 Create or sync backend user records after first login.
 Expose current-user context.
 Support role-based access checks for user, admin, doctor, and support roles.
 Protect all sensitive APIs through dependencies.
8.2 Candidate API Endpoints
Endpoint Method Purpose
 /api/v1/auth/me GET Return authenticated user context.
/api/v1/auth/sync POST Create/sync backend user after Firebase login.
/api/v1/auth/logout POST Optional server-side logout marker or token 
revocation integration.
/api/v1/auth/roles GET Admin-only role inspection endpoint.
8.3 Internal Services and Repositories
Class / Component Responsibility Notes
AuthService Verifies token and maps identity to backend 
user. Should not store raw tokens.
UserContext Typed object containing user_id, firebase_uid, 
roles, and plan. Injected into protected routes.
AuthRepository Stores backend user auth metadata. Keeps app-specific roles separate from Firebase 
identity when needed.
8.4 Data Dependencies
Collection / Store Usage
users Backend user identity and status.
profiles User profile completion state.
audit_logs Login/sync/admin auth events.
8.5 Risks and Controls
Risk Control
Trusting frontend role claims Always enforce role checks on backend.
Token replay or stale roles Check status/roles from backend when needed.
Account deletion complexity Design soft deletion and data retention policy early.
8.6 Acceptance Criteria
 Protected routes reject invalid tokens.
 Backend user record is created/synced after login.
 Admin endpoints reject non-admin users.
 Auth errors are standardized and do not leak internals.
--- PAGE 136 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 5
Draft v1.0 | Backend Architecture & Module Design
9. User and Profile Module
The User and Profile Module manages core personal information, health profile inputs, preferences, and onboarding 
completion. This module provides the context that TARA AI uses for personalization while avoiding uncontrolled 
medical claims.
9.1 Responsibilities
 Manage profile creation and updates.
 Store health baseline information such as age range, gender if collected, height, weight, lifestyle preferences, 
conditions, allergies, medications, and goals.
 Control privacy preferences and notification preferences.
 Expose profile context to AI and dashboard services through safe read methods.
9.2 Candidate API Endpoints
Endpoint Method Purpose
/api/v1/users/me GET Return current user account summary.
/api/v1/profile GET Return user profile.
/api/v1/profile PUT Update profile.
/api/v1/profile/health PUT Update health profile fields.
/api/v1/profile/preferences PUT Update app preferences.
9.3 Internal Services and Repositories
Class / Component Responsibility Notes
UserService Account-level operations and status checks. No raw AI prompting here.
ProfileService Profile and health baseline updates. Validates sensitive fields carefully.
ProfileRepository MongoDB persistence for profile documents. Should support partial updates.
9.4 Data Dependencies
Collection / Store Usage
users Account identity and status.
profiles Personal and health profile data.
audit_logs Profile updates and consent-related changes.
9.5 Risks and Controls
Risk Control
Over-collection of sensitive data Collect only MVP-required fields.
Incorrect AI personalization Separate user-stated facts from AI-inferred summaries.
Privacy issues Use consent, clear data policies, and audit logs.
9.6 Acceptance Criteria
 User can complete onboarding.
 Profile can be updated safely.
 AI context builder can retrieve profile summary.
 Sensitive updates are auditable.

Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 5

10. AI Chat Module
The AI Chat Module manages conversations between users and TARA AI. It stores conversation metadata and messages 
while delegating LLM selection, RAG retrieval, prompt construction, safety checks, and usage logging to AI 
infrastructure services.
10.1 Responsibilities
 Create conversations.
 Store user and assistant messages.
 Call AI Orchestrator for safe responses.
 Use user profile and report context when appropriate.
 Track AI usage by user and subscription plan.
 Apply chat limits for free and paid tiers.
10.2 Candidate API Endpoints
Endpoint Method Purpose
/api/v1/chat/conversations POST Create a conversation.
/api/v1/chat/conversations GET List user conversations.
/api/v1/chat/conversations/{id} GET Get conversation and messages.
/api/v1/chat/conversations/{id}/messages POST Send user message and receive TARA response.
/api/v1/chat/usage GET Return chat usage and limits.
10.3 Internal Services and Repositories
Class / Component Responsibility Notes
AIChatService Owns chat flow and message persistence. Calls AIOrchestratorService.
ConversationRepository CRUD for conversations. Enforces user ownership.
MessageRepository Stores messages and metadata. Avoid storing excessive hidden prompt data.
EntitlementService Checks plan limits. Used before AI call.
10.4 Data Dependencies
Collection / Store Usage
conversations Conversation metadata.
messages User/assistant messages.
profiles Health context.
report_chunks/vector DB RAG context.
subscriptions Plan limits and entitlements.
ai_usage_logs Token/cost/provider tracking.
10.5 Risks and Controls
Risk Control
Medical hallucination Use safety prompts, disclaimers, and context grounding.
Cost explosion Limit free chats, log token usage, cap contexts.
Prompt injection Sanitize retrieved text and apply system hierarchy.
Data leakage Always filter RAG by user_id and access permissions.
10.6 Acceptance Criteria
 User can create and continue chat.
 Responses use user context only with authorization.
 Usage limits are enforced.
 Every AI call is logged with provider/model/token estimate.
--- PAGE 138 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 5
Draft v1.0 | Backend Architecture & Module Design
11. Health Report Module
The Health Report Module manages report uploads, S3 metadata, OCR processing status, extracted text, summaries, and 
report-level access control. It should not directly expose raw S3 objects without controlled signed URLs.
11.1 Responsibilities
 Create report upload records.
 Validate file type and size.
 Generate S3 upload/download access securely.
 Trigger OCR and chunking background jobs.
 Store processing status and extracted metadata.
 Expose report summaries and report-specific Q&A entry points.
11.2 Candidate API Endpoints
Endpoint Method Purpose
/api/v1/reports GET List user reports.
/api/v1/reports/upload-url POST Create report record and signed upload URL.
/api/v1/reports/{id} GET Get report details.
/api/v1/reports/{id}/process POST Trigger/retry processing.
/api/v1/reports/{id}/summary GET Get AI-generated report summary.
/api/v1/reports/{id} DELETE Delete or archive report.
11.3 Internal Services and Repositories
Class / Component Responsibility Notes
HealthReportService Coordinates report lifecycle. Owns status transitions.
StorageService S3 signed URL and object operations. Avoid public buckets.
OCRService Extracts text from PDFs/images. Can run sync for tiny files or async for normal 
reports.
RAGService Chunks text and creates embeddings. Stores chunks with report/user metadata.
HealthReportRepository Stores report metadata and statuses. Never stores large PDFs in MongoDB.
11.4 Data Dependencies
Collection / Store Usage
health_reports File metadata, status, summary.
report_chunks Extracted chunks and metadata.
vector database Embeddings for retrieval.
S3 Actual PDFs/images.
audit_logs Upload/download/delete events.
11.5 Risks and Controls
Risk Control
Malicious files Validate MIME, size, extension, and scan if possible.
OCR failure Store failed status and allow retry.
Wrong-user access Always enforce owner check before signed URL generation.
Large processing jobs Use background workers and status polling.
11.6 Acceptance Criteria
 User can upload reports securely.
 Report processing status is visible.
 Failed processing can be retried.
 Report data is available to RAG only for owning user.
