19. Background Jobs and Async Processing
The backend should not block user requests for heavy or scheduled work. Report OCR, embedding creation, report 
summaries, daily summaries, reminder delivery, email sending, analytics aggregation, and notification retries should 
run through background workers.
Job Type Trigger Worker Responsibility User Experience
Report processing User uploads report. Run OCR, extract text, chunk, 
embed, summarize, update status.
User sees processing status and 
receives notification when ready.
Reminder delivery Scheduled next_run_at. Send push/in-app notification and 
create delivery log.
User receives reminder at 
configured time.
Daily summary Scheduled evening job. Summarize goals, logs, reminders, 
and profile context.
User receives 10 PM style daily 
summary if enabled.
AI usage aggregation Periodic job. Aggregate token estimates and 
costs. Admin sees usage dashboard.
Email sending Business event. Send transactional email with 
retries.
User receives 
account/payment/support emails.
Cleanup/archive Scheduled maintenance.
Clean expired signed URL 
metadata, old failed jobs, invalid 
device tokens.
System remains stable and clean.
Worker Rule
Background workers should call service-layer methods or shared functions rather than duplicating business logic. 
Duplication between API routes and workers is one of the fastest ways to create inconsistent behavior.
--- PAGE 147 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 5
Draft v1.0 | Backend Architecture & Module Design
20. Validation and Error Handling
Healthcare-adjacent applications need strict input validation and safe error reporting. Errors should help developers 
debug while not exposing secrets, stack traces, provider payloads, raw medical content, or internal infrastructure 
details to users.
Error Type HTTP Status Example Client Message Style
ValidationError 422 Invalid goal target value. Clear field-level explanation.
AuthenticationError 401 Missing or invalid token. Please sign in again.
AuthorizationError 403 User tries to access another user 
report.
You do not have permission for 
this action.
NotFoundError 404 Report ID does not exist for user. Requested item was not found.
ConflictError 409 Duplicate active plan transition. This action conflicts with current 
state.
RateLimitError 429 Too many AI chat requests. Limit reached. Try again later or 
upgrade plan.
ProviderError 502/503 LLM/OCR/payment provider 
unavailable.
Service temporarily unavailable. 
Please try again.
InternalError 500 Unexpected unhandled bug. Something went wrong. Use 
request ID for support.
20.1 Error Response Shape
Recommended error responses should include code, message, request_id, and optional safe details. They should not 
include Python stack traces, raw exception objects, provider secrets, database queries, or raw LLM prompts.
--- PAGE 148 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 5
Draft v1.0 | Backend Architecture & Module Design
21. Security Controls
Control Backend Implementation Why It Matters
JWT verification Verify Firebase token on every protected 
request. Prevents unauthenticated data access.
RBAC Role checks for admin, support, doctor, and 
user capabilities. Prevents privilege escalation.
Ownership checks Every user-owned record query filters by 
user_id. Prevents cross-user data leaks.
Input validation Pydantic schemas plus business validation. Prevents invalid data and injection attempts.
Rate limiting Apply per-user/IP limits to chat, upload, login-
sensitive flows, and admin actions. Controls abuse and AI cost.
File validation Validate MIME, extension, size, and processing 
type. Reduces malicious upload risk.
Secrets management Use environment variables and AWS Secrets 
Manager. Avoids credential leaks.
Audit logs Record sensitive actions. Supports accountability and incident review.
Prompt injection controls Treat user/report text as untrusted and enforce 
system instructions. Protects AI workflows.
Safe logging Avoid raw medical data, tokens, secrets, and 
prompts in normal logs. Protects privacy and compliance readiness.
Medical Safety Boundary
TARA AI should not claim to diagnose, prescribe, or replace a clinician. Backend AI services should apply disclaimers, 
emergency detection, and safe escalation language where relevant.
--- PAGE 149 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 5
Draft v1.0 | Backend Architecture & Module Design
22. Observability and Logging
Observability must be built into the backend from day one. Without logs, request IDs, provider call records, and job 
state tracking, maintenance becomes guesswork.
Signal What to Capture Example Use
Request logs method, path, status, latency, user_id hash, 
request_id. Debug API failures and performance.
Error logs exception type, safe message, stack trace 
internally, request_id. Investigate production bugs.
AI usage logs provider, model, token estimate, latency, cost 
estimate, feature. Control AI costs and plan limits.
Job logs job_id, type, status, retry count, failure reason. Debug OCR/reminder failures.
Audit logs actor, target, action, timestamp, IP/device 
context. Accountability for sensitive actions.
Metrics request count, latency p95, error rate, queue 
depth, worker failures. Production monitoring and scaling decisions.
22.1 Request ID Rule
Every request should receive a request_id that appears in API responses, logs, background job metadata, and support 
troubleshooting. This is a small implementation detail that significantly improves professional support quality.

Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 5

23. Testing Strategy
Test Type What to Test Examples
Unit tests Service methods and pure business logic. Goal score calculation, plan entitlement check, 
prompt context selection.
Repository tests Database query behavior against test MongoDB. Report list by user_id, pagination, soft delete 
filters.
API tests Route behavior with auth and validation. POST /chat rejects free user after limit.
Integration tests Service interactions with mocked providers. Report upload creates S3 URL and report 
record.
Worker tests Background job behavior and retries. OCR failed job updates status and retry count.
Security tests Access control, role checks, ownership checks. User A cannot access User B report.
AI tests Prompt and RAG safety behavior. Retrieved chunks are user-scoped and prompt 
injection is contained.
Testing Rule
The backend is not done just because endpoints return data. It is done when the service rules, authorization checks, failure 
states, background jobs, and critical provider integrations are tested.

25. Backend Definition of Done
The backend should be considered complete for MVP only when the following conditions are satisfied. This checklist 
prevents a demo-only backend from being mistaken for a maintainable production-ready system.
Area Definition of Done
Architecture Modules, services, repositories, schemas, and workers follow the agreed 
folder structure.
Authentication All protected routes verify Firebase tokens and map to backend user 
context.
Authorization User-owned data is always filtered by user_id; admin operations require 
role checks.
Validation All request bodies and responses use Pydantic schemas with clear 
validation rules.
AI All LLM calls go through AIOrchestratorService with logging, safety, and 
usage tracking.
Reports Files are stored in S3; MongoDB stores metadata; processing state is 
tracked.
Async OCR, embeddings, reminders, emails, and summaries use workers or 
background jobs where needed.
Errors Errors are normalized and include request_id without leaking internals.
Observability Request logs, AI usage logs, job logs, and audit logs exist for critical flows.
Testing Critical service, API, security, and worker paths have tests.
Documentation OpenAPI docs, setup instructions, environment variable list, and runbook 
notes are available.
Volume 5 Closing Statement
The backend is the product engine of Blumetara AI. If the backend is clean, secure, testable, and observable, the Flutter app, 
admin dashboard, AI features, and future roadmap can grow safely. If the backend becomes messy, every future feature 
will become slower, riskier, and more expensive.

Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 6
Draft v1.0 | Database Design, Data Modeling & Persistence Strategy
Document Control
Item Details
Document Name Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 6: Database Design, Data 
Modeling & Persistence Strategy
Purpose
Define the canonical data model, collection design, storage boundaries, 
indexing strategy, privacy controls, lifecycle rules, and scaling approach 
for the Blumetara AI MVP and future versions.
Inputs Used Master planning documents, BT Quick product notes, system design 
diagrams, and Volumes 1-5.
Primary Audience
Founder, backend engineers, database engineers, AI/RAG engineers, 
DevOps engineers, QA, security reviewers, and future project handover 
sessions.
Out of Scope Final production migrations, exact cloud billing configuration, official legal 
compliance certification, and medical-device regulatory validation.
How to Use This Volume
This volume is the database blueprint for Blumetara AI. It should be used before backend implementation begins, before 
API contracts are finalized, and before the AI/RAG pipeline is connected to real user data. The purpose is to prevent 
random collection creation, uncontrolled schema drift, missing indexes, weak privacy boundaries, and expensive data 
redesign later.
 Use this volume as the source of truth for MongoDB collection names and ownership.
 Every backend module should read and write only through repositories or dedicated service interfaces.
 Every file upload should store binary files in S3 and only metadata in MongoDB.
 Every AI answer that uses health reports should be traceable to report chunks or user profile context.
 Every sensitive data update should be auditable and protected by role-based access control.
1. Database Executive Summary
Blumetara AI is a health co-pilot platform. Its database must support user identity, health profiles, medical report 
metadata, OCR outputs, vector chunks, AI conversations, reminders, goals, food logs, workout plans, subscriptions, 
notifications, family monitoring, and administrative audit logs. The database cannot be treated as a simple CRUD store. It 
is the memory backbone of TARA AI.
The recommended primary database for the MVP is MongoDB Atlas because the product contains flexible, document-
oriented, rapidly evolving data. Health reports, AI conversations, user preferences, goals, reminders, and profile context 
are not always uniform. MongoDB allows quick iteration while still supporting production-grade indexes, validation, 
encryption, backups, vector search, and scaling when designed carefully.
Core Rule
MongoDB stores structured metadata and application state. AWS S3 stores heavy binary files. Vector search stores searchable 
embeddings. The backend service layer controls all data access. The client app never talks directly to the database.
1.1 Data Store Responsibilities
Store Primary Responsibility Examples Do Not Store
MongoDB Atlas Operational data and metadata
Users, profiles, goals, reminders, 
report metadata, messages, audit 
logs
Large PDFs, images, raw voice files, 
unbounded binary blobs
AWS S3 Object storage for binary assets Reports, prescriptions, food images, 
profile images, voice files
User passwords, plain secrets, 
database indexes
Vector Store Semantic retrieval for RAG Report chunks, embeddings, chunk 
metadata Original full PDFs as binary files
Firebase Auth Authentication identity provider UID, email verification, auth token 
validation Application health profile data
Payment Gateway Payment transaction execution Subscription payment IDs, invoices, 
status callbacks
Full card details or sensitive 
payment credentials
--- PAGE 156 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 6
Draft v1.0 | Database Design, Data Modeling & Persistence Strategy
1.2 Top-Level Data Model
User
  -> Profile
  -> HealthProfile
  -> Conversations -> Messages
  -> HealthReports -> ReportChunks -> Embeddings
  -> Goals -> GoalProgress
  -> Medicines -> Reminders -> Notifications
  -> WaterLogs / FoodLogs / WorkoutPlans
  -> Subscriptions -> Payments
  -> FamilyMembers
  -> AuditLogs
1.3 MVP Database Success Criteria
 User data is isolated by user_id across every user-owned collection.
 Health reports are stored as S3 objects with metadata in MongoDB.
 AI chat has access to user profile context, report chunks, and conversation history without sending unnecessary data to the 
LLM.
 Indexes support common dashboard, reminder, chat, and report queries efficiently.
 Audit logs capture sensitive administrative and health-data operations.
 The schema can support Free and Paid plans without redesign.
 The design can later support family accounts, doctors, wearables, and external healthcare APIs.
2. Database Design Principles
2.1 Document-Oriented Primary Model
Aspect Database Decision
Decision Use MongoDB Atlas as the primary application database.
Rationale
Blumetara data is flexible: health profiles, reports, goals, reminders, AI 
messages, and analytics evolve quickly. MongoDB supports rapid iteration 
and nested documents while still allowing indexes and validation.
Tradeoffs Relational joins are weaker than SQL; complex transactional analytics may 
require additional reporting stores later.
Guardrails
Keep documents bounded. Do not embed unlimited arrays. Use references 
for high-growth child records such as messages, logs, chunks, and 
notifications.
2.2 Metadata in MongoDB, Files in S3
Aspect Database Decision
Decision Store only file metadata in MongoDB and store binaries in S3.
Rationale
Medical reports, images, and voice files can grow large. S3 is cheaper and 
purpose-built for object storage. MongoDB remains performant for 
metadata and queries.
Tradeoffs Requires signed URL flow, bucket security, and object lifecycle 
management.
Guardrails Never expose raw S3 public URLs for private health files. Use pre-signed 
URLs or authenticated proxy access.
2.3 One User ID Across All Collections
Aspect Database Decision
Decision Use user_id as the primary ownership field in every user-owned collection.
Rationale This enables strict authorization, deletion, analytics, and data isolation.
Tradeoffs Every query must include user_id where applicable.
Guardrails Repository methods must enforce user ownership. No endpoint should 
fetch user-owned data using only document ID.
--- PAGE 157 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 6
Draft v1.0 | Database Design, Data Modeling & Persistence Strategy
2.4 Separate High-Growth Collections
Aspect Database Decision
Decision Keep messages, report chunks, logs, notifications, and progress records 
separate from parent objects.
Rationale These records can grow quickly and would create oversized documents if 
embedded.
Tradeoffs More queries are needed to reconstruct complete views.
Guardrails Use pagination, summary fields, and indexes to keep views fast.
2.5 Vector Data Is Search Infrastructure
Aspect Database Decision
Decision Store embeddings in a dedicated vector collection or vector-enabled store.
Rationale RAG requires semantic search over report chunks and profile context. 
Vector search should be optimized independently from normal app CRUD.
Tradeoffs Vector indexes add cost and operational complexity.
Guardrails Store chunk metadata with source report, user_id, sensitivity level, and 
extraction confidence.
2.6 Privacy by Design
Aspect Database Decision
Decision Treat all health data as sensitive even before formal regulatory 
certification.
Rationale The platform stores reports, goals, medicines, and health history. Trust 
depends on privacy protection.
Tradeoffs More audit logging and access controls increase engineering work.
Guardrails Encrypt data in transit and at rest, restrict admin access, log sensitive 
actions, and support account/data deletion.
3. Logical Data Domains
The database is organized into domains that map to backend modules. Each domain has an owning service and a 
repository boundary. This prevents the backend from becoming a random set of collections without ownership.
Domain Collections Owning Backend Module Primary Risks
Identity & Access users, admin_users Auth, Admin Account takeover, weak role checks, 
inconsistent auth identity
Profile & Health Context profiles, health_profiles Users, Profile Sensitive health data leakage, 
incomplete user context
AI Chat conversations, messages AI Chat
Unbounded history, hallucination 
without context, privacy leakage to 
LLM
Reports & RAG health_reports, report_chunks Health Reports, RAG OCR errors, wrong chunk retrieval, 
large file exposure
Goals & Progress goals, goal_progress Goals Incorrect progress metrics, duplicate 
entries
Medication & Reminders medicines, reminders Medicine, Reminders Missed reminders, timezone errors
Lifestyle Tracking water_logs, food_logs, workout_plans Nutrition, Workout Noisy user data, inconsistent units
Notifications notifications Notifications Duplicate notifications, notification 
fatigue
Commercial subscriptions, payments Subscription, Payment Incorrect plan access, payment 
mismatch
Governance audit_logs, app_settings Admin, Audit Missing traceability, unsafe 
configuration changes
Family Accounts family_members Family / Admin Unauthorized family access
3.1 Ownership Rules
 The Auth module owns identity linkage but does not own detailed health profile data.
--- PAGE 158 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 6
Draft v1.0 | Database Design, Data Modeling & Persistence Strategy
 The Profile module owns personal and health context data used by TARA AI.
 The AI Chat module owns conversations and messages but relies on RAG service for report context.
 The Report module owns report metadata and extraction status; the RAG service owns report chunks and embeddings.
 The Reminder module owns scheduling state; the Notification module owns notification delivery logs.
 The Admin module may read operational summaries but should not freely mutate user health records.

extraction state Many per user Critical

configuration Low growth MVP
5. Collection: users
Property Design
Purpose
Stores application-level user identity metadata and links Firebase UID to 
internal user records. This collection is not the password store; Firebase 
Auth handles credential authentication.
Owning Module Authentication Module
PII / PHI Sensitivity High - contains account identifiers and auth metadata
Persistence Type Primary MongoDB collection
Lifecycle Created and updated by application services; retained according to 
product privacy policy and user deletion rules.
5.1 Field Design
Field Type Required Description
_id ObjectId Yes Internal MongoDB user identifier.
firebase_uid String Yes Stable Firebase identity key.
email String Yes Normalized email address.
phone String No Optional verified phone number.
status Enum Yes active, suspended, deleted, pending.
role Enum Yes user, admin, doctor, support where 
applicable.
plan_id String No Current commercial plan reference.
created_at DateTime Yes Account creation timestamp.
updated_at DateTime Yes Last account update timestamp.
--- PAGE 159 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 6
Draft v1.0 | Database Design, Data Modeling & Persistence Strategy
last_login_at DateTime No Last successful login timestamp.
deleted_at DateTime No Soft delete timestamp if account is 
deleted.
5.2 Index Strategy
Index Purpose Notes
unique(firebase_uid) Resolve authenticated user quickly Must be unique.
unique(email) Avoid duplicate accounts Use lowercase normalized email.
status + role Admin filtering Useful for admin dashboard.
5.3 Sample Document Shape
{
  "_id": "ObjectId",

  "email": "user@example.com",
  "status": "active",

  "plan_id": "free",
  "created_at": "2026-07-02T10:00:00Z",
  "updated_at": "2026-07-02T10:00:00Z"
}
5.4 Common Query Patterns
 Find user by Firebase UID during every authenticated request.
 List active users for admin dashboard with pagination.
 Check role and status before allowing sensitive actions.
5.5 Risks and Controls
Risk Control
Duplicate identity records Enforce unique firebase_uid and email indexes.
Deleted users still visible Use status/deleted_at filters in every query.
Role escalation Only admin services can update role fields.

26. Indexing Strategy
Indexes should be designed from query patterns, not from guesswork. Every index has write overhead and storage cost, 
so the MVP should include only indexes that support real product paths: authentication, dashboards, report lists, chat 
history, reminder workers, notification center, subscription checks, and audit review.
Query Path Required Index Reason
Authenticated request user lookup users.firebase_uid unique Every API call needs fast user resolution.
User dashboard profile load profiles.user_id unique, health_profiles.user_id 
unique Dashboard and AI context need quick profile reads.
Conversation list conversations(user_id, last_message_at) Recent chat list.
Message pagination messages(conversation_id, created_at) Chat screen performance.
Report list health_reports(user_id, created_at) Report library.
Report chunks report_chunks(user_id, report_id, chunk_index) Report reconstruction and auditability.
Vector retrieval vector index on embedding with user filter RAG search.
Active goals goals(user_id, status) Dashboard goal cards.
Goal progress trends goal_progress(user_id, goal_id, recorded_at) Charts and insights.
Due reminders reminders(status, next_run_at) Worker efficiency.
Notification center notifications(user_id, created_at) User notification list.
Subscription entitlement subscriptions.user_id unique Feature limit checks.
Audit review audit_logs(target_user_id, created_at) Compliance and support review.
26.1 Index Anti-Patterns
 Do not index every field by default.
 Do not create indexes for admin screens before the admin screen exists.
 Do not create compound indexes in the wrong order; equality fields should usually come before sort/range fields.
 Do not forget user_id in user-owned query paths.
 Do not rely on collection scans for reminder workers or notification dispatch.
27. Vector Search and RAG Data Model
The RAG layer allows TARA AI to answer based on user-specific health reports and profile context. The database must 
make source-aware retrieval possible. A generated answer should be traceable to the relevant chunks that were used. 
This improves trust, debugging, and safety.
RAG Object Stored Fields Purpose
Report Chunk user_id, report_id, chunk_index, chunk_text, 
embedding, metadata Primary retrieval unit for report Q&A.
Chunk Metadata page, section, lab marker, OCR confidence, source 
type Improves filtering and citation logic.
--- PAGE 180 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 6
Draft v1.0 | Database Design, Data Modeling & Persistence Strategy
Embedding Vector array generated from chunk_text Semantic similarity search.
Context Reference message_id, chunk_id, score, report_id Shows what context influenced an AI response.
Report Summary report_id, structured markers, risk flags, generated 
summary Fast dashboard and summary rendering.
27.1 RAG Retrieval Contract
1. Receive user query and authenticated user_id.
2. Classify intent: general health, report Q&A, medication, goal coaching, nutrition, emergency risk, or administrative query.
3. Generate query embedding only for retrieval-relevant intents.
4. Search vector index with strict user_id filtering.
5. Fetch top-k chunks and metadata.
6. Build prompt with minimal necessary profile context, retrieved chunks, safety rules, and disclaimer rules.
7. Store response message with context_refs containing chunk IDs and retrieval scores.
27.2 Retrieval Safety Requirements
 Never retrieve chunks across users.
 Never use report chunks from deleted reports.
 Never present low-confidence OCR text as certain.
 Never allow prompt injection inside report text to override system instructions.
 Always include medical safety disclaimers for diagnosis/treatment-like answers.
28. Data Validation and Schema Governance
MongoDB is flexible, but uncontrolled flexibility is dangerous. Blumetara should use application-level validation with 
Pydantic schemas in FastAPI and optional MongoDB schema validation for critical collections. The backend must validate 
inputs before writing records.
Layer Validation Responsibility Example
Client App User-friendly form validation Required full name, reminder time format.
FastAPI Schemas Strong request validation Goal type enum, allowed units, report upload 
metadata.
Service Layer Business rule validation Free users can create only allowed number of goals.
Repository Layer Ownership and query safety Always query by user_id + document_id.
MongoDB Validation Critical field enforcement Required user_id, status enum, timestamp fields.
28.1 Schema Versioning
 Add schema_version to complex documents such as health_profiles, report extraction summaries, AI analysis results, and 
workout plans.
 Do not break old records when the product evolves.
 Write migration scripts for structural changes.
 Prefer additive changes for MVP unless there is a serious design defect.
28.2 Field Naming Rules
 Use snake_case consistently in backend and database fields.
 Use user_id, report_id, goal_id, and conversation_id consistently.
 Use created_at, updated_at, deleted_at timestamps.
 Use status fields with explicit enums instead of ambiguous booleans.
 Use *_at for timestamps and *_id for identifiers.
--- PAGE 181 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 6
Draft v1.0 | Database Design, Data Modeling & Persistence Strategy
29. Privacy, Security and Data Protection
Blumetara AI handles health-related data. Even if the MVP is not positioned as a certified medical device, the engineering 
standard must treat health information as highly sensitive. The database design should reduce exposure, support 
deletion, support auditability, and avoid unnecessary duplication of sensitive data.
Control Database Implementation
User isolation Every user-owned collection includes user_id and repository methods enforce it.
Encryption at rest Use MongoDB Atlas encryption and S3 server-side encryption.
Encryption in transit Use TLS for database and object-store connections.
Least privilege Backend service uses scoped database credentials; admin access is limited.
Auditability Sensitive admin reads/writes generate audit_logs records.
Deletion support Soft delete first, then physical purge workflows for final deletion.
Data minimization Do not store full AI prompt bodies or unnecessary raw medical text in logs.
Secrets protection Do not store API keys in MongoDB; use AWS Secrets Manager or equivalent.
29.1 User Data Deletion Policy - Engineering View
 Mark user status as deleted and prevent login.
 Revoke active tokens or rely on Firebase disablement where available.
 Delete or anonymize profile, health profile, conversations, messages, reports, chunks, reminders, notifications, and logs 
according to the product privacy policy.
 Delete S3 files associated with the user.
 Preserve minimal legally required payment and audit records only if required and allowed by policy.
 Record deletion completion status without keeping unnecessary sensitive content.
30. Backup, Restore and Disaster Recovery
Database backup is not optional. Medical reports, reminders, goals, subscriptions, and AI history are core user assets. The 
MVP should use MongoDB Atlas backup capabilities and S3 versioning/lifecycle controls where feasible.
Asset Backup Strategy Restore Consideration
MongoDB Atlas Automated backups with point-in-time recovery if 
budget allows Test restore into staging before trusting process.
S3 Reports Versioning and lifecycle rules for private buckets Ensure deleted-user purge rules override normal 
retention when required.
Vector Index Rebuildable from report_chunks and embeddings if 
stored
If external vector DB is used, export metadata and 
IDs.
App Settings Versioned setting changes with audit logs Bad config rollback should be fast.
Secrets Stored in Secrets Manager, not backed up in app DB Recovery requires secure rotation procedure.
30.1 Recovery Objectives
Metric MVP Target Later Target
RPO - Recovery Point Objective 24 hours or better depending on Atlas tier Minutes with point-in-time recovery
RTO - Recovery Time Objective Same business day for MVP Under 1 hour for production scale
Backup Test Frequency Before go-live and after major schema changes Monthly or quarterly restore drills
Criticality Reports, users, subscriptions, reminders All operational and AI data
31. Scaling Strategy by User Count
Stage Database Strategy Key Actions
0-100 users Simple Atlas cluster, essential indexes Validate schema, queries, backups, and RAG 
correctness.
100-1,000 users Add query monitoring and slow query review Tune indexes, add pagination everywhere, verify 
worker queries.
1,000-10,000 users Separate hot collections and review cluster tier Optimize messages, notifications, chunks, and 
--- PAGE 182 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 6
Draft v1.0 | Database Design, Data Modeling & Persistence Strategy
progress logs.
10,000-100,000 users Consider read patterns, archival strategy, cache 
layer
Introduce Redis for hot entitlement/profile/session 
data if needed.
100,000+ users Evaluate sharding, analytics warehouse, service 
split
Shard by user_id if necessary; move analytics to 
separate pipeline.
31.1 Future Sharding Considerations
If Blumetara grows heavily, the likely shard key for most user-owned collections is user_id or a compound key beginning 
with user_id. This keeps user data co-located and supports account-level operations. However, sharding should not be 
introduced too early because it adds operational complexity. First optimize indexes, query patterns, pagination, and 
archival policies.
31.2 Collections Most Likely to Need Scaling Attention
 messages - high write volume from chat usage.
 report_chunks - high growth when users upload many reports.
 notifications - high growth from reminders and nudges.
 goal_progress and water_logs - high write volume from daily tracking.
 audit_logs - high growth from admin and sensitive operations.
32. Implementation Checklist
Phase Database Tasks Exit Criteria
Sprint 0 Finalize collection names, indexes, schema 
conventions, and user_id ownership rule Database design approved before coding begins.
Sprint 1 Create MongoDB connection module, base 
repository, index creation script Backend can connect to dev/staging DB safely.
Sprint 2 Implement users, profiles, health_profiles collections Auth and onboarding flows persist correctly.
Sprint 3 Implement reports metadata and S3 references Reports upload without storing binaries in 
MongoDB.
Sprint 4 Implement report_chunks and vector search 
abstraction Report Q&A can retrieve user-specific chunks.
Sprint 5 Implement conversations and messages Chat history works with pagination and 
context_refs.
Sprint 6 Implement goals, progress, medicines, reminders Dashboard and reminders work reliably.
Sprint 7 Implement notifications, subscriptions, audit_logs Production controls and commercial gates exist.
Pre-Go-Live Run seed data, index verification, backup 
verification, privacy review Database is ready for MVP launch.
32.1 Developer Guardrails
 No direct database calls from route handlers.
 No user-owned query without user_id.
 No unbounded arrays for high-growth data.
 No raw report files inside MongoDB.
 No card data or secrets in MongoDB.
 No sensitive text in application logs or audit metadata.
 No feature entitlement checks in the client only; backend must enforce limits.
33. Volume 6 Closing Summary
The database design for Blumetara AI must support two goals at the same time: fast MVP development and long-term 
startup scalability. MongoDB Atlas gives the flexibility needed for early AI healthcare product iteration, but it must be 
used with discipline. The schema should be module-aligned, privacy-aware, index-driven, and ready for future growth.
--- PAGE 183 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 6
Draft v1.0 | Database Design, Data Modeling & Persistence Strategy
The most important design choices are simple but critical: store binary files in S3, store metadata in MongoDB, keep high-
growth records in separate collections, enforce user ownership on every query, preserve traceability for AI responses, 
and audit sensitive operations. These choices allow TARA AI to become more than a chatbot: it becomes a safe, contextual, 
and maintainable health co-pilot.
Next Volume
Volume 7 should cover AI Architecture: TARA AI Agent, prompt engineering, LLM orchestration, safety guardrails, 
conversation memory, medical disclaimers, provider selection, cost optimization, and AI evaluation strategy.

orchestrated, how user context and reports are used safely, and how AI 
quality, safety, cost, and observability are controlled.
Inputs Used Master planning documents, BT Quick product notes, system design 
diagrams, and Volumes 1-6.
Primary Audience Founder, AI engineers, backend engineers, prompt engineers, product 
team, QA, security reviewers, and future developers.
Out of Scope
Detailed OCR implementation, full vector database schema, certified 
clinical validation, training a proprietary medical LLM, and 
legal/regulatory compliance certification.
How to Use This Volume
This volume is the AI blueprint for Blumetara AI. It should be read before implementing the AI chat module, report Q&A, 
daily summaries, goal coaching, reminder intelligence, nutrition coaching, workout suggestions, and any feature that 
sends data to an LLM provider.
 Use this document to define what TARA AI is allowed to do and what it must refuse or escalate.
 Use this document to design the AI service layer before writing prompts or connecting APIs.
 Use this document to separate product intelligence from medical diagnosis claims.
 Use this document to guide evaluation, logging, cost control, and future AI roadmap decisions.
1. AI Executive Summary
TARA AI is the intelligence layer of Blumetara AI. It is not merely a chatbot. It is a personal health co-pilot that combines 
user profile context, health reports, goals, reminders, lifestyle logs, and carefully controlled LLM outputs to help users 
understand and manage their health routines.
The MVP should use existing LLM providers rather than building or training a custom model. The product value comes 
from orchestration: how the system retrieves the right context, structures prompts, applies safety rules, enforces user 
permissions, stores memory, and converts AI outputs into useful product actions.
Core AI Positioning
Blumetara must position TARA AI as an assistant, explainer, organizer, coach, and health routine companion - not as a doctor, 
diagnostic authority, emergency service, or replacement for professional medical care.
1.1 TARA AI Product Roles
Role What TARA Does MVP Boundary
Caretaker Reminds users about medicines, water, goals, and 
routine tasks.
Allowed if based on user-configured reminders and 
safe templates.
Coach Encourages healthy habits, explains progress gaps, 
and suggests next steps.
Allowed for general wellness and user goals; avoid 
diagnosis claims.
Report Explainer Explains uploaded blood reports, prescriptions, and 
health files in simple language.
Allowed with RAG context and disclaimers; must not 
make definitive diagnosis.
Health Memory Uses profile, past reports, goals, and conversation 
summaries to personalize replies.
Allowed with explicit consent and strict data 
minimization.
Navigator Suggests when a user should consult a doctor or 
seek urgent help.
Allowed as safety escalation; not a triage 
replacement.
Analyzer Summarizes daily/weekly patterns and progress. Allowed for descriptive analytics, not certified 
medical predictions.
1.2 AI Success Criteria
 Responses are personalized using the user profile and relevant report context only when appropriate.

 The AI does not invent medical facts that are not in the user profile, reports, or safe general knowledge.
 The AI clearly distinguishes general wellness information from medical advice.
 The system can explain why an answer was generated, including which report chunks or profile fields were used.
 The AI service is observable: token usage, model selection, latency, failures, and safety events are logged.
 The AI can scale commercially by controlling prompt size, context retrieval, and model routing.
2. Responsible AI Boundaries
Because Blumetara operates in a health context, the AI must be designed with strict boundaries. A health assistant can be 
helpful without pretending to be a medical authority. The safest strategy is to combine personalized context with careful 
language, escalation guidance, and refusal rules for risky requests.
Allowed Conditionally Allowed Not Allowed
Explain a lab marker in simple words. Explain a report finding when the report text is 
available and the answer includes uncertainty. Diagnose a disease definitively.
Remind user to take medicine they added. Suggest doctor consultation based on concerning 
symptoms or report values.
Tell the user to start, stop, or change medication 
dosage.
Create general workout or diet guidance. Personalize workouts based on user profile and 
stated limitations.
Give dangerous plans for medical conditions 
without professional oversight.
Summarize daily progress. Identify trends and encourage follow-up. Predict guaranteed disease outcomes.
Answer general health education questions. Answer using retrieved report chunks and cited 
context.
Handle emergencies as a replacement for 
emergency services.
2.1 Medical Disclaimer Strategy
The AI should not add a heavy disclaimer to every tiny message because that destroys user experience. Instead, 
disclaimers should be risk-sensitive. Low-risk habit coaching can be conversational. Report interpretation, medication 
questions, pregnancy-related questions, chronic disease management, severe symptoms, mental health crisis, or 
emergency-related messages require stronger caution and referral language.
Risk Level Example User Intent AI Behavior
Low How much water should I drink today? Give general guidance, personalize if profile data 
exists, avoid overclaiming.
Medium My cholesterol is high in this report, what does it 
mean?
Explain report value, cite report context, encourage 
doctor follow-up.
High Can I stop this medicine? Refuse direct medication change advice; advise 
consulting doctor.
Emergency I have chest pain and shortness of breath. Strong emergency escalation: contact local 
emergency services immediately.
Crisis I want to harm myself. Crisis response: encourage immediate help, 
emergency contact, local crisis support.
3. TARA AI Agent Architecture
TARA AI should be implemented as an orchestrated backend service, not as prompts scattered across the frontend. The 
mobile app sends user messages to the backend. The backend authenticates the user, builds context, retrieves relevant 
knowledge, selects the right model, applies guardrails, calls the LLM, validates the response, stores the result, and returns 
a formatted answer.
Mobile App / Admin Dashboard
  -> FastAPI AI Chat Endpoint
  -> Auth & Entitlement Check
  -> Intent Classifier
  -> Context Builder
  -> RAG Retriever when needed
  -> Safety Policy Engine
  -> Prompt Builder
  -> Model Router
  -> LLM Provider Client

  -> Message Store + Audit/Event Logs
  -> Response to User
3.1 AI Service Components
Component Responsibility Why It Exists
AI Chat Controller Receives user messages and returns AI responses. Keeps API contract stable for mobile app and admin 
dashboard.
Intent Classifier Classifies the message into report Q&A, goal 
coaching, medication, emergency, nutrition, etc.
Determines whether RAG, tools, refusal, or 
escalation is needed.
Context Builder Loads minimal user profile, health profile, 
conversation summary, and feature-specific context. Personalization without sending unnecessary data.
RAG Retriever Retrieves relevant report chunks and knowledge 
snippets.
Grounds answers in user reports and reduces 
hallucination.
Prompt Builder Constructs provider-specific prompts using 
templates and context. Centralizes prompt logic and makes it testable.
Model Router Chooses Gemini/OpenAI/Claude or cheaper model 
based on task. Controls cost, latency, and quality.
Safety Engine Applies policy rules before and after LLM calls. Prevents unsafe medical claims, emergency 
mishandling, and data leaks.
Response Formatter Formats answer for chat, dashboard card, summary, 
or notification. Keeps UX consistent.
Evaluation Logger Logs quality, safety, latency, token usage, and 
context sources. Enables debugging and continuous improvement.
4. AI Request Lifecycle
1. The user submits a message through the Flutter mobile app or admin-approved interface.
2. FastAPI validates the JWT/Firebase identity and maps it to internal user_id.
3. The AI Chat module checks the user plan, daily usage limit, feature permission, and account status.
4. The Intent Classifier detects whether the query is general health, report Q&A, medication, goal coaching, nutrition, workout, 
emergency, or administrative.
5. The Safety Engine checks for emergency, self-harm, medication-change, diagnosis, or prohibited requests before retrieving 
context.
6. The Context Builder loads only necessary user profile, health profile, active goals, relevant medicines, and conversation 
summary.
7. If report context is needed, the RAG Retriever searches only the authenticated user's report chunks and returns top-ranked 
snippets.
8. The Prompt Builder composes the system instructions, safety rules, user message, retrieved context, and output format 
requirements.
9. The Model Router selects the provider and model based on cost, quality, urgency, and task complexity.
10. The LLM response is parsed and checked by the Response Validator for unsafe claims, missing disclaimers, hallucinated 
source references, and formatting issues.
11. The message, context references, token usage, model metadata, safety flags, and latency are stored.
12. The formatted response is returned to the client app.
4.1 Lifecycle Failure Handling
Failure Point Fallback Behavior User Message Strategy
Auth fails Reject request Ask user to sign in again.
Plan limit reached Block or downgrade Explain daily limit and upgrade option.
RAG retrieval fails Answer only if safe without report context Say report context could not be loaded.
LLM provider timeout Retry once, then fallback model Ask user to try again if all providers fail.
Safety violation Refuse or escalate Use calm, clear safety guidance.
Response validation fails Regenerate with stricter prompt or safe fallback Avoid exposing raw model failure.

5. Intent Classification Design
Intent classification is the routing brain of the AI system. It decides what the user wants and therefore what context, tools, 
and safety policy are required. This can begin as a lightweight rules + LLM classification approach and later evolve into a 
trained classifier if usage justifies it.
Intent Example Required Context Default Action
general_health What does vitamin D do? Minimal profile context if relevant Educational response with disclaimer 
if needed.
report_qa Explain my blood report. Report chunks + health profile RAG-grounded answer.
medication Can I take this tablet twice? Medicines + profile + safety rules Avoid dosage changes; advise 
doctor/pharmacist.
goal_coaching How am I doing with weight loss? Goals + progress + profile Coaching response and next steps.
reminder_management Remind me to drink water at 5 PM. Timezone + reminder permissions Create reminder through backend 
service after confirmation.
nutrition Is this food okay for my goal? Food logs + goals + profile General nutrition guidance.
workout Give me a workout plan. Profile + goals + limitations Safe routine suggestions.
emergency I have severe chest pain. No RAG needed Emergency escalation.
admin_support Why is my report not processed? Report status only Support-style explanation.
5.1 Intent Classifier Output Schema
{
  "intent": "report_qa",
  "risk_level": "medium",
  "requires_rag": true,
  "requires_tool": false,
  "requires_disclaimer": true,
  "requires_emergency_escalation": false,
  "confidence": 0.86,
  "reason": "User asks to explain uploaded blood report values."
}
6. Context Management Strategy
TARA AI should feel personalized, but personalization must be controlled. Sending everything about the user to an LLM 
on every request is expensive, risky, and unnecessary. The correct approach is minimal context loading based on intent.
Context Type Source Collection Use Case Send to LLM?
Basic profile profiles Age, timezone, language, 
height/weight if relevant Only if relevant.
Health profile health_profiles Conditions, allergies, user-confirmed 
health context Only necessary fields.
Conversation summary conversations.summary Long-term chat memory compression Yes for continuity.
Recent messages messages Short-term conversational context Last N messages only.
Report chunks report_chunks/vector store Report Q&A and explanations Top-k relevant chunks only.
Goals goals/goal_progress Goal coaching and dashboards Relevant active goals only.
Medicines medicines/reminders Medication reminders and 
explanations
Names/schedule if user asks; no 
dosage advice.
Food/workout logs food_logs/workout_plans Nutrition and workout 
personalization V1; summarize before sending.
6.1 Context Minimization Rules
 Never send full medical reports when top-k chunks are sufficient.
 Never send the full conversation history after the conversation becomes long; use summaries plus recent messages.
 Never send unrelated profile fields to answer simple general questions.
 Never send family member data unless the user is authorized and the query is about that family member.
 Never place secrets, internal IDs, raw system logs, or admin notes into prompts.

6.2 Memory Types
Memory Type Purpose Storage Update Strategy
Short-term memory Maintain chat continuity Recent messages Updated every message.
Conversation summary Compress long chat history conversations.summary Updated periodically or after long 
exchanges.
Health memory Personal health context health_profiles User-confirmed updates only.
Report memory Uploaded report knowledge health_reports/report_chunks Updated after OCR/RAG processing.
Goal memory Current goals and progress goals/goal_progress Updated by tracking actions.
7. Prompt Engineering Architecture
Prompts should be treated as versioned engineering assets, not random strings inside code. Every prompt should have a 
purpose, template ID, version, input variables, output schema, safety instructions, and test cases.
Prompt Type Purpose Example Output
System Prompt Defines TARA identity, boundaries, tone, safety 
rules. Stable assistant behavior.
Intent Prompt Classifies user intent and risk level. JSON classification object.
RAG Answer Prompt Answers using retrieved chunks and profile context. Grounded user-facing answer.
Report Summary Prompt Summarizes medical report in simple language. Structured report summary.
Goal Coach Prompt Turns goals and progress into coaching advice. Supportive next steps.
Daily Summary Prompt Summarizes user day from logs and reminders. Daily recap and tomorrow suggestions.
Safety Rewrite Prompt Rewrites risky output into safe language. Compliant response.
7.1 Base TARA System Prompt - Draft
You are TARA, the AI health co-pilot inside Blumetara AI.
Your role is to help users understand their health information, organize routines,
track goals, and ask better questions to healthcare professionals.
You are not a doctor. You do not diagnose, prescribe, or replace emergency care.
Use the provided user context and report context only when relevant.
If information is missing, say so clearly.
If symptoms are severe or urgent, recommend immediate medical attention.
For medication changes, dosage changes, or treatment decisions, advise consulting a qualified clinician.
Be clear, calm, practical, and supportive.
7.2 Prompt Template Governance
 Store prompt templates in backend configuration or version-controlled files.
 Assign every production prompt a template_id and version.
 Log template_id and version with each AI response for debugging.
 Do not let frontend clients directly modify system prompts.
 Run regression tests when prompts change.
8. Model Provider Strategy
The MVP should support provider abstraction from the beginning. The product may start with Gemini for cost/speed and 
optionally support OpenAI or Claude for higher-quality responses. The backend should not lock business logic to one 
provider SDK.
Task Type Preferred Model Class Reason Fallback
Intent classification Fast low-cost model Small structured task Rules fallback or another cheap 
model.
General health chat Fast mid-quality model Frequent interactions need low cost 
and latency Alternate LLM provider.
Report explanation Higher-quality reasoning model Needs careful context handling and 
clarity
Retry with stronger model if answer 
fails validation.
Daily summaries Fast model Template-driven summarization Batch retry worker.
Safety-sensitive questions Higher-quality model + strict prompt Higher risk requires better reasoning Safe refusal template if uncertain.

8.1 Provider Abstraction
Aspect AI Architecture Decision
Decision Create an LLMProvider interface and route calls through 
AIOrchestratorService.
Rationale This makes it possible to switch Gemini/OpenAI/Claude without rewriting 
product modules.
Tradeoffs Abstraction adds initial engineering work and requires normalized 
response formats.
Guardrails Keep provider-specific logic inside adapters, not business services.
8.2 Model Router Inputs
 Intent and risk level.
 User plan: free, paid, admin/internal.
 Task complexity: simple, medium, complex.
 Latency target: real-time chat vs background summary.
 Cost budget and daily usage limit.
 Provider availability and recent error rates.
 Need for JSON-structured output.
9. AI Orchestrator Service Design
The AI Orchestrator is the central backend service that coordinates classification, context retrieval, prompt building, 
model routing, safety checks, provider calls, validation, and persistence. It should be implemented as an internal service 
used by the AI chat module, report module, summary jobs, and future agent features.
class AIOrchestratorService:
    async def handle_user_message(user_id, conversation_id, message):
        auth_context = await access_policy.validate_user(user_id)
        entitlement = await plan_service.check_ai_quota(user_id)
        intent = await intent_classifier.classify(message)
        safety_precheck = safety_engine.precheck(intent, message)
        context = await context_builder.build(user_id, intent)
        rag_context = await rag_service.retrieve(user_id, message, intent) if intent.requires_rag else []
        prompt = prompt_builder.build(intent, context, rag_context, message)
        model = model_router.select(intent, entitlement)
        raw_response = await llm_client.generate(model, prompt)
        final_response = await response_validator.validate(raw_response, intent, rag_context)
        await message_repository.save_turn(...)
        await usage_logger.log(...)
        return final_response
9.1 Orchestrator Responsibilities
 Guarantee that every AI call is associated with an authenticated user or trusted backend job.
 Enforce plan limits before spending tokens.
 Prevent cross-user context leakage.
 Apply safety rules before and after generation.
 Normalize provider responses into a single internal response format.
 Log enough metadata for debugging without storing unnecessary sensitive prompt content.

10. Safety Engine Design
The Safety Engine is the policy layer that protects users and the company. It must handle risky health, medication, 
emergency, self-harm, privacy, and prompt-injection scenarios. It should be deterministic where possible and LLM-
assisted only where necessary.
Safety Category Detection Method Required Behavior
Emergency symptoms Rules + classifier Strongly recommend emergency services 
immediately.
Self-harm crisis Rules + classifier Provide supportive crisis escalation, emergency 
help, trusted person.
Medication dosage change Rules + classifier Refuse dosage change guidance and refer to 
doctor/pharmacist.
Diagnosis request Classifier Explain limitations; suggest professional evaluation.
Prompt injection in report Sanitization + prompt rules Treat report text as data, not instructions.
Cross-user data request Access policy Deny and log suspicious access.
Illegal or harmful instructions Safety policy Refuse safely.
10.1 Pre-Generation Safety Checks
 Check emergency keywords and symptom patterns before retrieval.
 Check medication change requests before model routing.
 Check whether the user asks for diagnosis, prognosis, or treatment decisions.
 Check whether the user attempts to override system instructions or access another user's data.
10.2 Post-Generation Safety Checks
 Detect definitive diagnosis language such as “you have X” when not medically verified.
 Detect medication instructions such as changing dosage or stopping medicine.
 Detect hallucinated source references or report values not present in retrieved context.
 Detect missing emergency escalation for high-risk symptoms.
 Detect answer format violations for structured JSON outputs.
11. RAG Usage at the AI Architecture Level
RAG is the mechanism that allows TARA to answer using user-specific reports and stored health context. Volume 8 will 
define the detailed OCR and RAG pipeline. This volume defines when the AI should use RAG and how it should treat 
retrieved context.
When to Use RAG When Not to Use RAG
User asks about an uploaded report. User asks a general educational question with no personal context needed.
User asks why a dashboard health marker changed. User asks to create a simple water reminder.
User asks for history from past reports. User asks a UI/support question.
User asks a personalized question requiring previous data. User asks something unsafe where escalation is required first.
11.1 RAG Answer Rules
 Use retrieved report chunks as context, not as absolute truth if OCR confidence is low.
 Mention uncertainty when report text is unclear or incomplete.
 Do not answer report-specific questions without report context unless clearly stated.
 Do not expose internal chunk IDs to users, but store chunk IDs for traceability.
 When possible, explain values in simple language and recommend doctor follow-up for abnormal or concerning values.

12. Tool and Action Architecture
In future versions, TARA should not only answer questions but also perform safe actions through backend tools. The MVP 
can support limited actions such as creating reminders, summarizing reports, updating goals, and generating daily 
summaries. Tools must be permissioned and auditable.
Tool Action Safety Control MVP Priority
create_reminder Create medicine/water/goal reminder Require authenticated user and 
confirmation High
update_goal Update target or progress Validate ownership and plan limits High
summarize_report Generate report summary Use only user-owned processed report High
generate_daily_summary Summarize day from logs Background job with user opt-in Medium
create_workout_plan Generate workout plan Respect health profile limitations V1
analyze_food_image Analyze food image Use image safety and nutrition 
disclaimer V1
contact_family_alert Notify family contact Strong consent and emergency rules V2
12.1 Tool Execution Rules
 The LLM may suggest a tool call, but backend services must validate the action.
 High-impact actions require explicit user confirmation.
 No tool can access another user's data without relationship authorization.
 Every tool execution should create an audit or event log entry if it changes state.
 Tools must be idempotent where possible to avoid duplicate reminders or notifications.
13. AI Response Formats
Different features need different response formats. A chat answer is conversational. A report summary needs sections. A 
daily summary needs cards. A tool call needs structured JSON. The AI architecture should define canonical formats so the 
frontend can render responses consistently.
Response Type Used For Required Fields
chat_text General conversation message, disclaimer_level, suggested_actions
report_explanation Report Q&A summary, key_points, abnormal_markers, 
recommended_follow_up, sources
goal_coaching Goals progress_summary, gap, next_steps, encouragement
daily_summary End-of-day recap wins, missed_items, health_notes, tomorrow_focus
tool_action Reminder/goal creation action_type, arguments, confirmation_required
safety_escalation Emergency or crisis urgent_message, recommended_action, 
emergency_flag
13.1 Example Report Explanation JSON
{
  "response_type": "report_explanation",
  "disclaimer_level": "medium",
  "summary": "Your report shows a few values outside the usual reference range.",
  "key_points": [
    {"marker": "Vitamin D", "meaning": "Low in the uploaded report", "confidence": "high"}
  ],
  "recommended_follow_up": "Please discuss these findings with a qualified healthcare professional.",
  "sources": [{"report_id": "...", "chunk_id": "...", "score": 0.82}]
}

14. AI Observability and Logging
AI systems are difficult to debug if only final answers are stored. Blumetara should log structured AI metadata without 
unnecessarily storing sensitive raw prompts. Observability helps control cost, diagnose hallucinations, evaluate quality, 
and understand provider failures.
Metric / Event Purpose Storage Location
model_provider Know which provider generated response message metadata / ai_usage_log
model_name Debug cost and quality differences message metadata
prompt_template_id Trace prompt version message metadata
input_tokens/output_tokens Cost tracking usage logs
latency_ms Performance monitoring usage logs / CloudWatch
intent/risk_level Safety and routing analysis message metadata
context_refs Trace RAG sources message metadata
safety_flags Audit risky interactions safety logs / audit logs
provider_error Debug outages error logs
14.1 What Not to Log
 Do not log full raw medical reports inside normal application logs.
 Do not log full prompts with all user health context unless debugging mode is explicitly controlled and protected.
 Do not log API keys, secrets, provider tokens, or internal credentials.
 Do not log other users' data inside a user-specific AI trace.
15. AI Cost Control
AI cost can become one of the largest operating expenses. Cost control must be designed before launch. The easiest way to 
control cost is to limit prompt size, use cheaper models for simpler tasks, cache repeated summaries, and enforce plan-
based quotas.
Cost Driver Control Strategy
Long prompts Use conversation summaries, top-k RAG chunks, and minimal profile 
context.
High-cost models Route simple tasks to cheaper models and reserve stronger models for 
report reasoning.
Repeated summaries Cache report summaries and daily summary outputs where valid.
Free plan abuse Daily chat limits, image/report upload limits, rate limiting.
Retry storms Exponential backoff and circuit breakers for provider failures.
Large document uploads File size limits, background processing, and paid-plan limits.
15.1 Plan-Based AI Limits
Plan AI Chat Limit Report Analysis Advanced Features
Free Limited daily chats Limited uploads/analysis Basic reminders and general 
summaries.
Paid Higher daily chats More reports and deeper guidance Goal nudges, stock monitor, family 
monitoring, nutrition tracking.
Admin/Internal No normal user limits Testing and support only Restricted by admin role and audit 
logs.
16. AI Evaluation Strategy
AI quality cannot be judged only by whether the answer sounds good. Blumetara needs evaluation cases that test 
factuality, safety, personalization, tone, RAG grounding, refusal behavior, and structured output correctness.
Evaluation Dimension What to Test Pass Criteria
Grounding Does report Q&A use retrieved report context? No invented report values.
--- PAGE 194 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 7
Draft v1.0 | AI Architecture, TARA Agent, LLM Orchestration & Safety
Safety Does AI refuse medication changes and escalate 
emergencies? Correct refusal/escalation behavior.
Personalization Does answer use profile only when relevant? Relevant, not creepy or excessive.
Tone Is response supportive and clear? Calm, simple, non-alarming language.
Completeness Does answer address the user question? No major missing parts.
Format Does JSON output parse? Valid schema and required fields.
Cost Was appropriate model selected? No expensive model for simple task.
16.1 Test Set Categories
 Normal wellness questions.
 Report explanation questions with known report chunks.
 Medication dosage-change requests.
 Emergency symptom prompts.
 Prompt injection hidden inside uploaded report text.
 Goal coaching questions with progress data.
 Out-of-scope requests such as legal/financial/diagnostic claims.
 Multi-turn conversations requiring memory.
17. AI Security Threat Model
AI systems introduce new security risks beyond normal application security. TARA must be protected from prompt 
injection, data exfiltration, cross-user leakage, malicious report content, unsafe tool calls, and model output 
manipulation.
Threat Example Mitigation
Prompt injection Uploaded report says: ignore previous instructions. Treat retrieved text as untrusted data and isolate it 
in prompt.
Data exfiltration User asks for another user's reports. Repository-level user_id filtering and access policy.
Tool abuse LLM attempts to create repeated reminders. Backend validation, confirmation, idempotency.
Hallucinated sources AI cites report value not retrieved. Response validator checks source references.
Sensitive logging Full prompt with health data in logs. Structured metadata logging, protected debug mode 
only.
Provider outage LLM API unavailable. Fallback provider, graceful error, background retry.
17.1 Prompt Injection Rule
Critical Rule
All retrieved report text, OCR text, user-uploaded content, and third-party content must be treated as untrusted data. It can 
provide medical content to analyze, but it can never override system instructions, safety policies, access controls, or developer 
rules.
18. Human Handoff and Escalation
TARA should know when not to answer directly. A strong health AI product is not one that answers everything; it is one 
that safely identifies when a human professional, emergency service, support team, or family contact should be involved.
Escalation Type Trigger System Response
Doctor consultation Abnormal report values, chronic disease concerns, 
treatment decisions
Recommend discussing with qualified healthcare 
professional.
Emergency service Severe symptoms such as chest pain, stroke signs, 
breathing difficulty Urgent emergency guidance.
Pharmacist/Doctor Medication dosage, interactions, side effects Avoid direct medical decision; refer to professional.
Support team Upload failure, billing issue, processing stuck Create support-friendly explanation and ticket 
metadata.
Family contact Future SOS or monitoring flows Requires explicit consent and strict authorization.

19. AI Feature Roadmap
Phase AI Features Engineering Requirements
MVP AI chat, report explanation, basic RAG, health profile 
personalization, daily summary, safe reminders
AI orchestrator, prompt templates, RAG retrieval, 
safety engine, usage logs.
MVP+ Food image explanation, deeper goal nudges, weekly 
insights, medicine stock monitor
Image analysis pipeline, richer logs, more templates,

V1 Workout personalization, nutrition tracking, family

Context permissions, family authorization, analytics

V2 Voice AI, wearable integration, SOS alerts, external 
healthcare APIs
Streaming AI, event-driven ingestion, stronger 
compliance and escalation workflows.
Scale Multi-provider model routing, AI evaluation 
dashboard, internal support copilot
Evaluation pipeline, prompt registry, feedback 
loops, cost optimization.
19.1 Features Not Recommended for MVP
 Fully autonomous medical agents that make decisions without user confirmation.
 Certified risk prediction claims.
 Doctor dashboard with clinical decision-making workflows.
 Insurance or hospital API integrations.
 Medication interaction engine unless backed by a trusted medical database and reviewed carefully.
 Emergency SOS automation without legal, consent, and reliability review.
20. Implementation Checklist
Phase AI Engineering Tasks Exit Criteria
Sprint 0 Finalize AI boundaries, safety policy, prompt 
governance, model provider decision AI scope approved before coding.
Sprint 1 Create AI service interfaces, provider adapters, 
prompt template structure Backend can call provider through abstraction.
Sprint 2 Implement intent classifier and plan-based quota 
checks Messages are routed safely and usage is limited.
Sprint 3 Implement context builder and conversation 
memory summary Personalization works without oversized prompts.
Sprint 4 Connect RAG retriever to report chunks Report Q&A uses user-owned retrieved chunks.
Sprint 5 Implement safety precheck and postcheck Unsafe medication/emergency requests are handled 
correctly.
Sprint 6 Implement response schemas and frontend 
rendering contracts
Flutter can render chat, report, summary, and safety 
responses.
Sprint 7 Implement AI usage logs and quality evaluation test 
set Team can debug cost, latency, grounding, and safety.
Pre-Go-Live Run AI regression suite and safety review MVP AI behavior is launch-ready.
20.1 AI Launch Checklist
 All AI endpoints require authentication.
 Free and paid limits are enforced before provider calls.
 Provider API keys are stored in Secrets Manager or secure environment, not source code.
 Every LLM call logs provider, model, latency, token usage, prompt template ID, and safety metadata.
 Emergency and medication-change prompts are tested manually before release.
 Report Q&A never retrieves chunks across users.
 Prompt injection in uploaded documents is tested.
 Users see clear limitation language for medical decisions.
 Admin can monitor AI errors and high-level usage without reading private health content unnecessarily.
--- PAGE 196 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 7
Draft v1.0 | AI Architecture, TARA Agent, LLM Orchestration & Safety
21. Volume 7 Summary
Volume 7 defines the intelligence architecture of Blumetara AI. TARA AI is not just a chat screen. It is an orchestrated AI 
layer that combines intent classification, context building, RAG, prompt engineering, provider routing, safety checks, 
response formatting, evaluation, logging, and cost control.
The most important architectural decision is to keep AI logic inside the backend service layer rather than spreading 
prompts across the mobile app. This gives Blumetara control over safety, privacy, cost, provider switching, and future 
scalability.
Final AI Principle
The MVP should be impressive because it is useful, personalized, and safe - not because it pretends to be a doctor. TARA 
should help users understand, organize, and act responsibly on their health information while encouraging professional care 
whenever decisions become medical.
21.1 Handover Notes for Future Chats or Developers
 Continue Volume 8 with detailed OCR, report processing, chunking, embeddings, vector database, RAG retrieval, and report 
Q&A implementation.
 Do not implement AI calls directly inside Flutter.
 Do not store raw provider API keys in code or MongoDB.
 Do not allow AI-generated medical history to become confirmed profile truth without user confirmation.
 Do not let retrieved report text override TARA system instructions.

Item Details
Document Name Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 8: OCR, RAG Pipeline & Health Report 
Intelligence
Purpose
Define how uploaded health reports are securely stored, processed, converted 
into usable text, embedded, retrieved, and used by TARA AI for grounded health-
report explanations.
Inputs Used Master planning documents, BT Quick product notes, system design diagrams,

and legally binding clinical interpretation.
How to Use This Volume
This volume is the implementation blueprint for the health report intelligence layer. It should be used before building 
report upload, OCR, report summary, report Q&A, vector search, or any feature where TARA answers questions using 
user documents.
 Use this document to separate file storage, OCR processing, vector indexing, and AI answering into clean services.
 Use this document to prevent unsafe report interpretation, hallucinated values, and cross-user data leakage.
 Use this document to define how report chunks, embeddings, and source references should be stored and audited.
 Use this document as the quality checklist for the RAG pipeline before production launch.
1. Executive Summary
Blumetara AI depends on one high-value capability: helping users understand their health documents. The report 
intelligence pipeline converts uploaded files such as blood reports, prescriptions, fitness summaries, and medical 
documents into structured, searchable, retrievable knowledge. TARA AI can then answer user questions using the user's 
own data rather than relying only on general model knowledge.
The recommended MVP pipeline is intentionally practical: upload the file, store it in S3, create metadata in MongoDB, 
extract text through OCR or text parsing, normalize and validate the extracted content, split it into chunks, create 
embeddings, store the chunks in a vector-enabled store, retrieve relevant chunks during chat, build a safe prompt, and 
return a grounded answer with appropriate disclaimers.
Core Pipeline Principle
The uploaded report is the source of context. The LLM is the explainer. MongoDB/S3/vector search provide memory and 
traceability. TARA must never pretend to know what is in a report if the report text was not extracted, retrieved, or verified.
1.1 Pipeline Success Criteria
 Users can upload health reports reliably from the mobile app.
 Files are stored securely in S3 while MongoDB stores metadata only.
 OCR and parsing outputs are traceable to the original report.
 Chunks and embeddings are tied to the correct user_id, report_id, and access scope.
 Report Q&A retrieves the most relevant chunks instead of sending entire reports to the LLM.
 AI responses include uncertainty when OCR confidence or retrieved context is weak.
 No user can retrieve another user's document chunks.
 Processing failures are visible to the user and admin dashboard.
--- PAGE 199 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 8
Draft v1.0 | OCR, RAG Pipeline & Health Report Intelligence
2. End-to-End Pipeline Overview
The pipeline should be designed as a state machine, not as one giant synchronous API call. Uploading a report is user-
facing and should be fast. OCR, chunking, embedding, summary generation, and indexing can run asynchronously so the 
app remains responsive.
User Uploads Report
  -> Mobile App obtains upload permission
  -> Backend validates file metadata and user entitlement
  -> File stored in AWS S3
  -> health_reports document created in MongoDB with status = uploaded
  -> Background worker starts processing
  -> OCR / text extraction
  -> Text normalization and medical section detection
  -> Chunking and metadata enrichment
  -> Embedding generation
  -> Vector store upsert
  -> Optional report summary generation
  -> health_reports status = processed
  -> TARA can answer report-specific questions through RAG
2.1 Pipeline Stages
Stage Input Output Primary Service
Upload validation File name, type, size, user plan Accepted/rejected upload Health Report Service
Object storage Validated file S3 object key + metadata Storage Service
Metadata creation S3 key + user_id health_reports record Report Repository
OCR/text extraction PDF/image file Raw extracted text + confidence OCR Service
Normalization Raw extracted text Cleaned text + sections Report Parser Service
Chunking Normalized text Report chunks with metadata RAG Service
Embedding Chunks Vector embeddings Embedding Service
Indexing Embeddings + metadata Searchable vector records Vector Store Adapter
Summarization Chunks/report text User-facing summary AI Orchestrator
Retrieval User query Top relevant chunks RAG Retriever
Answer generation Query + chunks + profile Grounded AI response TARA AI Service
3. Upload and File Intake Architecture
Health report upload must be designed with security and operational reliability from the beginning. The frontend should 
not send large files through a normal chat endpoint. Instead, the backend should either receive the file through a 
controlled upload endpoint or generate pre-signed S3 upload URLs after validating user permissions and file rules.
3.1 Architecture Decision - S3 for Files, MongoDB for Metadata
Aspect Decision Detail
Decision Store PDFs, images, and medical files in AWS S3. Store only metadata, processing 
status, extracted text references, and chunk references in MongoDB.
Rationale
MongoDB is not designed to be a document file storage system for large binaries. 
S3 is cheaper, durable, scalable, and supports lifecycle policies, encryption, and 
object-level access controls.
Tradeoffs Requires managing S3 keys, signed URLs, object permissions, and cleanup logic. 
Adds one more cloud service to configure.
Guardrails Never expose raw S3 object keys directly as public URLs. Use short-lived signed 
URLs and strict bucket policies.
3.2 Accepted File Types
File Type MVP Support Notes
PDF Yes Most common medical report format. Prefer text 
extraction first, OCR fallback if scanned.
JPG/JPEG Yes Common for photographed prescriptions or reports.
PNG Yes Common image upload format.
HEIC Optional iPhone images; may need conversion before OCR.
DOC/DOCX No for MVP Avoid complexity unless client strongly requires it.
CSV/XLSX No for MVP Could support later for exported fitness or lab data.
--- PAGE 200 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 8
Draft v1.0 | OCR, RAG Pipeline & Health Report Intelligence
3.3 File Validation Rules
 Limit maximum file size based on plan. Example: Free 5 MB, Paid 20 MB in MVP planning.
 Validate MIME type and file extension. Do not trust extension alone.
 Reject executable formats, compressed archives, scripts, and unsupported documents.
 Scan or inspect uploaded files if production security budget allows.
 Generate unique object keys using user_id/report_id rather than user-provided filenames.
 Preserve the original filename only as metadata after sanitization.
 Create audit events for uploads, failed uploads, deletes, and reprocessing actions.
4. Health Report Processing State Machine
A report should move through explicit statuses. This gives the mobile app and admin dashboard a reliable way to display 
progress and diagnose failures.
Status Meaning User Visible Message
uploaded File stored successfully; processing not started. Report uploaded. Processing will start shortly.
queued Background job is queued. Report is waiting for analysis.
processing_ocr OCR/text extraction is running. Extracting text from report.
processing_chunks Text is being cleaned and chunked. Preparing report for AI questions.
processing_embeddings Embeddings are being generated. Indexing report knowledge.
summary_pending Optional summary not generated yet. Generating report summary.
processed Report is ready for AI chat and summary view. Report is ready.
failed Processing failed after retries. We could not process this report. Please try again or 
contact support.
deleted User/admin deleted or soft-deleted report. Report removed.
4.1 Status Transitions
uploaded -> queued -> processing_ocr -> processing_chunks -> processing_embeddings -> summary_pending -> processed
uploaded -> queued -> processing_ocr -> failed
processing_chunks -> failed
processing_embeddings -> failed
processed -> deleted
failed -> queued  # manual or automatic reprocess
Operational Rule
Never mark a report as processed until the raw file, extracted text, chunks, embeddings, and minimum metadata are all 
linked and queryable for that authenticated user.
5. OCR and Text Extraction Strategy
OCR should not be treated as perfect. Medical reports often contain tables, abbreviations, units, reference ranges, 
handwritten prescription content, low-quality scans, and mixed languages. The system must capture confidence, preserve 
original text, and avoid overconfident AI explanations when extraction quality is poor.
Input Type Preferred Extraction Method Fallback
Digital PDF with embedded text PDF text extraction OCR if text extraction returns too little content.
Scanned PDF OCR page by page Manual retry / ask user for clearer file.
Image report OCR on image Image preprocessing then OCR retry.
Prescription image OCR + prescription-specific parser Ask user to confirm medicine names if confidence 
low.
Fitness screenshot OCR + layout parser V1 integration with fitness APIs preferred.
5.1 OCR Provider Options
Provider Strength Weakness MVP Recommendation
Google Vision Strong OCR, easy integration, good 
image support. Cost and vendor dependency. Good MVP option if using Google 
ecosystem.  
AWS Textract Strong document/table extraction, fits May be more complex/costly Strong option for medical report

AWS architecture. depending on use. tables.

stack is AWS. Consider if client chooses Azure later.
Open-source OCR Lower direct cost and local control. Quality and maintenance burden;
