demands it.
5.2 OCR Output Schema
{
  "report_id": "rep_123",
  "user_id": "usr_456",
  "provider": "aws_textract",
  "pages": [
    {
      "page_number": 1,
      "raw_text": "...",
      "confidence_avg": 0.91,
      "blocks": [
        {"type": "line", "text": "Hemoglobin 13.5 g/dL", "confidence": 0.96},
        {"type": "table_cell", "row": 3, "col": 2, "text": "13.5", "confidence": 0.94}
      ]
    }
  ],
  "extraction_status": "completed"
}
6. Medical Text Normalization
After extraction, the text must be normalized before chunking. Normalization improves retrieval quality and reduces 
hallucination. The goal is not to diagnose; the goal is to convert messy document text into a structured representation that 
can be searched and explained safely.
Normalization Task Purpose Example
Whitespace cleanup Remove OCR artifacts and repeated spaces. "Vitamin   D" -> "Vitamin D"
Page boundary tagging Preserve traceability. [Page 2] CBC Results
Section detection Separate CBC, lipid profile, liver function, 
prescription, notes. section_type = lipid_profile
Unit preservation Keep units tied to values. mg/dL, mmol/L, IU/L
Reference range preservation Keep min/max/reference text. Reference: 12-16 g/dL
Abnormal flag capture Extract H/L markers when present. LDL 160 H
Confidence tagging Mark uncertain OCR segments. confidence < 0.70
6.1 Structured Marker Extraction
For MVP, structured marker extraction can be best-effort rather than medically certified. It can identify common lab 
markers and store them as extracted observations. TARA can then explain that these are extracted from the uploaded 
report and should be verified by a doctor.
{
  "marker_name": "Vitamin D",
  "raw_value": "12.7",
  "unit": "ng/mL",
  "reference_range": "30-100",
  "flag": "low",
  "page_number": 1,
  "source_text": "Vitamin D 12.7 ng/mL Reference 30-100",
  "ocr_confidence": 0.93,
  "normalization_confidence": 0.82
}
7. Chunking Strategy
Chunking decides how report text is split before embedding. Poor chunking causes poor retrieval. Medical reports should 
not be split blindly every fixed number of characters if that separates a marker from its unit or reference range. The best 
MVP approach is hybrid chunking: section-aware where possible, token-bounded for model compatibility, with overlap 
only when useful.
--- PAGE 202 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 8
Draft v1.0 | OCR, RAG Pipeline & Health Report Intelligence
Chunking Method Use Case Risk
Fixed-size chunks Fast baseline for all text. Can split tables and separate values from units.
Page-level chunks Useful for traceability. May be too large and noisy.
Section-aware chunks Best for lab sections and prescriptions. Requires reliable section detection.
Marker-level chunks Good for specific lab Q&A. May lose broader report context.
Hybrid chunks Recommended MVP compromise. More implementation effort.
7.1 Recommended Chunk Metadata
{
  "chunk_id": "chk_789",
  "report_id": "rep_123",
  "user_id": "usr_456",
  "family_member_id": null,
  "chunk_index": 12,
  "page_start": 2,
  "page_end": 2,
  "section_type": "lipid_profile",
  "text": "LDL Cholesterol: 160 mg/dL. Reference range: <100 mg/dL. Flag: High.",
  "tokens_estimated": 28,
  "ocr_confidence_avg": 0.94,
  "contains_abnormal_marker": true,
  "created_at": "2026-07-02T00:00:00Z"
}
7.2 Chunk Size Recommendation
Content Type Recommended Chunk Size Overlap
Short lab rows Group related rows into 200-500 tokens. Minimal overlap.
Narrative doctor notes 400-800 tokens. 50-100 token overlap.
Prescription text Keep medicine block together. No overlap unless long.
Full report summary Store separately from chunks. No overlap.
8. Embedding Generation and Vector Storage
Embeddings convert report chunks into vectors so the system can retrieve semantically relevant content for a user query. 
The vector layer must enforce user-level filtering. A query from one user must search only that user's allowed chunks.
8.1 Architecture Decision - Vector Search with Metadata Filters
Aspect Decision Detail
Decision Store each embedding with metadata including user_id, report_id, 
family_member_id, chunk_id, section_type, and processing status.
Rationale Metadata filters are required for privacy, access control, report-specific Q&A, 
and debugging.
Tradeoffs Filtering adds complexity and must be tested carefully to avoid cross-user 
retrieval errors.
Guardrails Every vector query must include user_id and access-scope filters. Never rely 
only on application-side post-filtering.
8.2 Vector Record Schema
{
  "vector_id": "vec_chk_789",
  "embedding": [0.012, -0.044, 0.231],
  "text": "LDL Cholesterol: 160 mg/dL...",
  "metadata": {
    "user_id": "usr_456",
    "report_id": "rep_123",
    "chunk_id": "chk_789",
    "page_start": 2,
    "section_type": "lipid_profile",
    "source": "health_report",
    "visibility": "owner_only"
  }
}
8.3 Embedding Refresh Rules
 Generate embeddings after chunk text is finalized, not before normalization.
--- PAGE 203 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 8
Draft v1.0 | OCR, RAG Pipeline & Health Report Intelligence
 If OCR is reprocessed, invalidate old chunks and old embeddings.
 If a report is deleted, delete or tombstone corresponding chunks and vectors.
 If embedding model changes, create a migration job to re-embed documents gradually.
 Store embedding_model and embedding_version for every vector record.
9. Retrieval Design
Retrieval determines which chunks are given to the LLM. The RAG retriever should combine semantic similarity, 
metadata filters, report selection, recency, confidence, and task-specific rules. The top result is not always the safest 
result; the system should retrieve enough context to answer accurately while keeping prompts small.
Retrieval Factor Why It Matters Implementation Rule
User filter Prevents data leakage. Always filter by authenticated user_id and family 
access scope.
Report filter Allows asking about a selected report. Filter by report_id when user is viewing a report.
Similarity score Finds semantically relevant chunks. Retrieve top-k candidates.
OCR confidence Avoids relying on poor extraction. Down-rank or flag low-confidence chunks.
Section type Improves precision for lab/prescription questions. Boost relevant section categories.
Recency Important for longitudinal reports. Prefer newer reports when question asks current 
state.
Abnormal flag Useful for “what is concerning” questions. Boost abnormal marker chunks but avoid alarmist 
tone.
9.1 Retrieval Output Contract
{
  "query": "Why is my LDL high?",
  "filters": {"user_id": "usr_456", "report_id": "rep_123"},
  "top_k": 5,
  "results": [
    {
      "chunk_id": "chk_789",
      "report_id": "rep_123",
      "score": 0.86,
      "page_start": 2,
      "section_type": "lipid_profile",
      "text": "LDL Cholesterol: 160 mg/dL. Reference range: <100 mg/dL. Flag: High.",
      "ocr_confidence_avg": 0.94
    }
  ]
}
10. Prompt Context Assembly
The prompt builder should not simply paste chunks into a prompt. It should assemble context using a clear hierarchy: 
system safety rules, user intent, minimal user profile, selected report chunks, uncertainty notes, and required output 
format. The prompt should instruct the LLM to answer only from retrieved report context when the question is report-
specific.
SYSTEM:
You are TARA, the health co-pilot in Blumetara. You explain health information but do not diagnose.
USER PROFILE CONTEXT:
Age: 35. Goal: reduce LDL. Known allergies: none provided.
RETRIEVED REPORT CONTEXT:
[Source 1 | Report rep_123 | Page 2 | OCR 0.94]
LDL Cholesterol: 160 mg/dL. Reference range: <100 mg/dL. Flag: High.
USER QUESTION:
Why is my LDL high?
INSTRUCTIONS:
- Explain in simple language.
- Use only the provided report context for report-specific values.
- Do not diagnose.
- Recommend discussing abnormal values with a qualified clinician.
- Mention uncertainty if context is incomplete.
--- PAGE 204 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 8
Draft v1.0 | OCR, RAG Pipeline & Health Report Intelligence
10.1 Context Assembly Rules
 Include source labels in the internal prompt, but present user-friendly wording in the answer.
 Do not include irrelevant chunks merely because they are from the same report.
 Limit total retrieved context based on model token budget and task complexity.
 If no relevant chunks are found, say the report context was not found and ask the user to upload or select the correct report.
 For multiple reports, clearly distinguish which report/date each value came from.
11. Report Summary Generation
Report summaries are useful because users may not know what to ask. After successful processing, the system can 
generate a safe, structured summary. This summary should be stored separately from raw OCR output and clearly 
marked as AI-generated.
Summary Section Purpose Safety Rule
Plain-language overview Explain what type of report it is. Do not claim diagnosis.
Key observations Mention notable extracted items. Tie observations to extracted text and confidence.
Values outside reference range Highlight abnormal flags if present. Avoid panic language; encourage doctor review.
Questions to ask doctor Help user prepare for consultation. Frame as discussion points.
Lifestyle notes General wellness suggestions if relevant. Avoid personalized treatment claims without 
clinician input.
11.1 Summary JSON Schema
{
  "report_id": "rep_123",
  "summary_version": "v1",
  "plain_language_summary": "This appears to be a lipid profile report...",
  "key_observations": [
    {"label": "LDL Cholesterol", "value": "160 mg/dL", "flag": "high", "source_chunk_id": "chk_789"}
  ],
  "doctor_questions": ["What could be contributing to my high LDL?"],
  "disclaimer": "This is an AI explanation, not a medical diagnosis. Please consult a qualified healthcare professional."
}
12. Report Q&A Behavior
Report Q&A is where users ask TARA questions about uploaded reports. This feature is high value but also high risk. The 
AI must stay grounded, communicate uncertainty, and avoid overinterpreting results.
User Question Type RAG Behavior Response Requirement
What does this value mean? Retrieve marker chunk and nearby reference range. Explain marker generally and value in report 
context.
Is this dangerous? Retrieve abnormal markers and risk-related context. Avoid definitive danger claim; advise clinician for 
abnormal/severe concerns.
Compare old and new reports. Retrieve same marker across reports. Show trend with dates and source reports.
What should I do? Retrieve report context and profile goals. Give general next steps and clinician follow-up; no 
medication changes.
Can I ignore this? Retrieve relevant context. Do not tell user to ignore abnormal findings; 
recommend review.
12.1 Grounded Answer Checklist
 Does the answer mention only values that exist in retrieved chunks?
 Does the answer state uncertainty if extraction quality is low?
 Does the answer avoid diagnosis, prescription, or treatment changes?
 Does the answer recommend professional review for abnormal or concerning findings?
 Does the backend store source chunk IDs for traceability?
--- PAGE 205 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 8
Draft v1.0 | OCR, RAG Pipeline & Health Report Intelligence
13. Handling Low OCR Confidence
Low-quality OCR is common in healthcare documents. TARA should never behave as if low-confidence extracted text is 
guaranteed accurate. The UI and AI response should both reflect processing quality.
Confidence Case System Behavior User Experience
High confidence > 0.85 Use chunks normally. Normal report Q&A.
Medium confidence 0.65-0.85 Use with caution flag. Mention that some text may need verification.
Low confidence < 0.65 Avoid specific interpretation unless confirmed. Ask user to upload clearer image or manually 
confirm text.
Missing pages Mark report incomplete. Tell user which pages failed if known.
Unclear prescription name Ask confirmation. Do not guess medicine name confidently.
13.1 Low Confidence Response Template
I can try to help, but the text extraction quality for this part of the report looks unclear.
Please verify the value directly from the original report or upload a clearer image.
I should not confidently interpret a value that may have been misread.
14. Privacy and Access Control for RAG
The most serious RAG security failure is cross-user data leakage. Every part of the pipeline must preserve ownership and 
authorization metadata. Retrieval must filter before results are returned to the prompt builder.
Control Implementation
User ownership Every report, chunk, and vector must include user_id.
Family account scope Use family_member_id and relationship permissions when family monitoring 
exists.
Backend-only retrieval Frontend must never query vector DB directly.
Metadata filters Vector search must filter by user_id/report_id before returning results.
Signed URL protection Report files accessed through short-lived URLs only.
Deletion propagation Deleting a report must remove or tombstone chunks/vectors/summaries.
Audit logging Log report access, AI retrieval, admin access, and reprocessing events.
Non-Negotiable Security Rule
Never rely on the LLM to protect private data. Data isolation must happen before prompt creation through backend 
authentication, authorization, database filters, and vector search metadata filters.
15. Background Workers and Queue Design
Report processing is a background workflow. Celery with Redis is a practical MVP option because the existing system 
design already includes Celery/Redis for scheduled tasks and async jobs. The same infrastructure can process OCR, 
chunking, embeddings, summaries, and retries.
Job Trigger Retry Policy
process_report_ocr Report uploaded Retry 2-3 times with backoff.
normalize_report_text OCR completed Retry if parser fails due to transient error.
create_report_chunks Text normalized Fail fast if no text found.
generate_embeddings Chunks created Retry provider/network failures.
upsert_vectors Embeddings generated Retry DB/vector store failures.
generate_report_summary Vector indexing complete Optional retry; summary can be regenerated later.
cleanup_deleted_report Report deleted Retry until all dependent data removed/tombstoned.
15.1 Idempotency Rules
 Each job should be safe to retry without creating duplicate chunks or duplicate vectors.
 Use report_id + processing_version to group all generated artifacts.
 Before creating chunks, check whether chunks already exist for the current processing version.
 Before vector upsert, use deterministic vector IDs based on chunk_id and embedding_version.
--- PAGE 206 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 8
Draft v1.0 | OCR, RAG Pipeline & Health Report Intelligence
 Use status transitions and locked processing fields to prevent duplicate concurrent processing.
16. Error Handling and Reprocessing
A production system must assume files will fail to process. Reports can be blurry, corrupted, too large, password-
protected, unsupported, or missing pages. The product should provide graceful error messages and internal diagnostic 
details.
Failure Type Internal Handling User Message
Unsupported file Reject before upload or processing. This file type is not supported yet.
File too large Reject based on plan limit. This file is larger than your current upload limit.
OCR timeout Retry background job. Your report is taking longer than expected.
No text extracted Mark failed with reason. We could not read text from this report. Please 
upload a clearer file.
Embedding provider failure Retry and fallback if configured. Report analysis is temporarily delayed.
Vector upsert failure Retry and alert admin if repeated. Report is uploaded but not ready for AI questions 
yet.
16.1 Reprocessing Rules
 Allow admin-triggered reprocessing for failed reports.
 Allow user-triggered retry if the file is still valid and plan permits it.
 Increment processing_version for each full reprocess.
 Mark old chunks/vectors inactive before activating new ones.
 Preserve failure reason, timestamps, and retry count for support investigation.
17. API Design for Report Intelligence
The detailed API volume will define full contracts, but the RAG/OCR pipeline needs a clear API surface. These endpoints 
should be implemented inside the Health Report module and AI Chat module.
Endpoint Purpose Notes
POST /reports/upload-url Create signed upload URL or initiate upload. Validate file type, size, user plan.
POST /reports Create report metadata after upload. Creates health_reports record.
GET /reports List user reports. Return status and summary availability.
GET /reports/{id} Get report metadata/details. Must check ownership.
POST /reports/{id}/process Trigger processing/reprocessing. Admin or allowed user action.
GET /reports/{id}/summary Get AI-generated summary. Only if processed.
POST /chat/report-qa Ask question about selected report. Uses RAG retrieval.
DELETE /reports/{id} Delete or soft-delete report. Must cascade cleanup jobs.
17.1 Report Q&A Request Example
POST /chat/report-qa
{
  "report_id": "rep_123",
  "message": "What does my LDL value mean?",
  "conversation_id": "conv_456"
}
18. Data Model Dependencies
Volume 6 defines the database design in detail. This volume focuses on the relationships required by the RAG and OCR 
pipeline.
Collection Pipeline Responsibility
health_reports Stores report metadata, S3 location, status, processing version, summary refs.
report_pages Optional page-level OCR text and confidence.
report_chunks Stores normalized text chunks, page ranges, section types, and source metadata.
report_observations Optional structured extracted markers such as lab values and units.
conversations Links report Q&A to a user chat session.
--- PAGE 207 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 8
Draft v1.0 | OCR, RAG Pipeline & Health Report Intelligence
messages Stores user and AI messages with context refs and model metadata.
ai_usage_logs Stores token usage, model, prompt version, latency, and errors.
audit_logs Stores report access, processing, delete, admin access, and reprocess events.
18.1 Minimal Required Fields
Entity Required MVP Fields
health_reports _id, user_id, s3_key, original_filename, file_type, status, processing_version, 
created_at, updated_at
report_chunks _id, user_id, report_id, text, chunk_index, page_start, page_end, section_type, 
ocr_confidence_avg, active
vector record vector_id, embedding, text or text_ref, metadata.user_id, metadata.report_id, 
metadata.chunk_id, embedding_model
message metadata message_id, context_refs, model_provider, model_name, prompt_template_id, 
token_usage, safety_flags
19. Observability and Monitoring
The report intelligence pipeline must be observable across file upload, background processing, OCR provider calls, 
embedding calls, vector search, and LLM generation. Without monitoring, debugging report failures becomes extremely 
difficult.
Metric Why It Matters
upload_success_rate Detects frontend/backend/storage upload problems.
ocr_success_rate Measures document extraction reliability.
avg_ocr_latency Controls user wait time and worker capacity.
processing_failure_reason_count Shows top causes of failures.
embedding_latency/cost Tracks AI infrastructure cost.
vector_retrieval_latency Affects chat response time.
no_context_answer_rate Detects retrieval or indexing quality issues.
hallucination_flag_count Indicates answer quality/safety problems.
report_qa_token_usage Controls cost and plan limits.
19.1 Logs to Capture
 Upload request metadata: user_id, file type, size, result, and report_id.
 Processing job events: job name, status, retry count, duration, and error type.
 OCR metadata: provider, confidence distribution, pages processed, and text length.
 Embedding metadata: model, vector count, duration, and cost estimate.
 RAG metadata: query, top_k, chunk IDs, scores, and filters applied.
 LLM metadata: model, prompt template, token usage, latency, and safety flags.
20. Testing Strategy
Testing the report intelligence pipeline requires more than unit tests. It requires test files, OCR quality checks, retrieval 
tests, security tests, and AI answer evaluation.
Test Type What to Verify Example
Unit tests Parser, chunker, status transitions. Chunking does not split lab value from unit.
Integration tests S3 + MongoDB + worker + vector store. Upload report and verify processed state.
Security tests Ownership filters and signed URLs. User A cannot retrieve User B chunks.
OCR tests Text extraction accuracy on sample reports. Known marker appears in extracted text.
Retrieval tests Correct chunks returned for known queries. LDL query returns lipid profile chunk.
AI tests Grounded answer quality and safety. Answer does not invent values.
Failure tests Retry and error messages. Blurry image triggers low-confidence handling.
20.1 Golden Test Dataset
 At least 5 clean digital PDF lab reports.
 At least 5 scanned PDF reports.
--- PAGE 208 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 8
Draft v1.0 | OCR, RAG Pipeline & Health Report Intelligence
 At least 5 mobile-camera report photos with different quality levels.
 At least 3 prescription images.
 At least 3 intentionally corrupted or unsupported files.
 Expected extracted markers and expected retrieval results for each test document.
21. Security Threat Model for RAG/OCR
RAG introduces unique security risks because user documents become prompt context. The system must protect against 
cross-user retrieval, prompt injection inside uploaded documents, malicious files, and accidental disclosure.
Threat Example Mitigation
Cross-user retrieval User receives another user's report context. Mandatory vector metadata filters and access tests.
Prompt injection in document Uploaded report says ignore system prompt. Treat document text as data, not instructions.
Malicious file Uploaded file contains exploit payload. File validation, scanning, sandboxed processing if 
possible.
Oversharing in prompt Too much profile/report data sent to LLM. Context minimization and top-k retrieval.
Admin misuse Admin views sensitive report without reason. RBAC, audit logs, minimum support access.
Deleted data remains retrievable Vectors not removed after delete. Cascade deletion/tombstone worker with 
verification.
21.1 Prompt Injection Rule
Document-as-Data Rule
Text extracted from uploaded reports must be treated as untrusted user-provided data. It must never override system 
prompts, developer instructions, safety rules, privacy filters, or tool permissions.
22. MVP Implementation Sequence
The report intelligence pipeline should be implemented in phases so the team can validate each part before connecting it 
to user-facing AI chat.
1. Create health_reports collection and report upload API.
2. Configure private S3 bucket and signed upload/download strategy.
3. Implement upload validation, metadata creation, and report listing UI.
4. Add Celery/Redis or equivalent background worker setup.
5. Implement OCR/text extraction for PDF and images.
6. Store raw extracted text and processing metadata.
7. Implement normalization and section-aware chunking.
8. Create report_chunks collection and indexes.
9. Generate embeddings and upsert to vector store with user filters.
10. Build RAG retriever and test with known questions.
11. Connect report Q&A to TARA AI with safety prompts.
12. Generate basic report summaries after processing.
13. Add monitoring, error handling, and admin reprocess controls.
14. Run security tests for cross-user isolation and prompt injection.

25. Handover Notes for Future Developers
Future developers should understand that this volume defines the intelligence infrastructure behind the report-analysis 
experience. The most important engineering rule is that AI quality depends on data quality, retrieval quality, and safety 
boundaries. Do not begin by writing prompts. Begin by building secure upload, reliable extraction, traceable chunks, 
vector metadata filters, and a tested retrieval layer.
 Keep report processing asynchronous and observable.
 Keep document files in S3 and metadata in MongoDB.
 Keep vector retrieval behind the backend only.
 Keep prompts versioned and tested.
 Keep report-specific answers grounded in retrieved chunks.
 Keep medical claims conservative and professionally safe.
End of Volume 8
This volume completes the OCR/RAG blueprint. The next volume should define API Documentation in full: endpoint groups, 
request/response schemas, error codes, authentication requirements, validation rules, and example payloads for the entire 
Blumetara MVP.

Contracts

Define backend API contracts for the mobile app, admin dashboard, AI/RAG

How to Use This Volume
This volume is the reference contract between the Blumetara clients and backend. It is not just a list of URLs. It defines 
API behavior, security assumptions, validation expectations, response consistency, pagination, file upload strategy, error 
semantics, and implementation sequencing.
 Use this document before creating FastAPI routers, Pydantic schemas, frontend API clients, and QA test cases.
 Use endpoint groups to keep the modular monolith clean and feature-owned.
 Translate these contracts into OpenAPI/Swagger once implementation begins.
 Treat response formats and error formats as stable contracts after MVP client approval.
1. Executive Summary
Blumetara AI requires a clear API layer because the platform has multiple consumers: the Flutter mobile app, the React 
admin dashboard, background workers, and eventually external healthcare integrations. The API layer must stay 
consistent even as internal modules evolve. This volume defines a REST-first API strategy for the MVP using FastAPI, 
JWT/Firebase authentication, MongoDB-backed resources, S3 file handling, RAG/AI orchestration, and role-based access 
control.
API Design Principle
Every API should be boring, predictable, secure, and testable. The AI experience may feel intelligent, but the API contract must 
remain deterministic: clear inputs, clear outputs, explicit errors, auditable side effects, and strict access control.
1.1 API Success Criteria
 Flutter developers can integrate screens without guessing request and response shapes.
 Admin dashboard developers can manage users, reports, subscriptions, and system visibility through separate admin APIs.
 AI/RAG endpoints are separated from normal CRUD endpoints and include safety, rate limit, and traceability controls.
 File upload APIs do not expose raw cloud storage permissions or public object keys.
 All protected endpoints validate Firebase/JWT identity and enforce user scope or admin role.
 All endpoints return a consistent response envelope and error structure.
 API documentation can be converted to Swagger/OpenAPI and used by QA for test cases.
2. API Architecture Overview
The API layer sits above the service layer of the FastAPI modular monolith. Routers should remain thin. They should 
validate input, verify authentication, call services, and return response DTOs. Business logic belongs in services. Database 
access belongs in repositories. External providers are accessed through adapters or service clients.
Client Request
  -> Cloudflare / WAF / Load Balancer
  -> FastAPI Router
  -> Auth Dependency + Role/Scope Checks
  -> Pydantic Request Schema Validation
--- PAGE 212 ---

  -> Service Layer Business Logic
  -> Repository / External Adapter
  -> Response DTO
  -> Standard API Response Envelope

3. API Standards and Conventions
3.1 Versioning
All public backend routes should use a versioned prefix: /api/v1. This gives the project a migration path if breaking 
changes are required later. Internal worker routes, if any, should not be publicly exposed.
3.2 HTTP Method Rules
Method Usage Rule Example
GET Read-only retrieval. Must not mutate data. GET /api/v1/reports
POST Create a resource or trigger a command. POST /api/v1/goals
PUT Replace a resource when full replacement is 
intended. PUT /api/v1/profile
PATCH Partial update to an existing resource. PATCH /api/v1/goals/{goal_id}
DELETE Soft delete where possible for health data. DELETE /api/v1/reports/{report_id}
3.3 Standard Response Envelope
{
  "success": true,
  "data": { ... },
  "message": "Operation completed successfully",
  "request_id": "req_01HZX...",
  "timestamp": "2026-07-02T17:30:00Z"
}
3.4 Standard Error Envelope
{
  "success": false,
  "error": {
    "code": "VALIDATION_ERROR",
    "message": "Invalid request payload",
    "details": [
      {"field": "email", "issue": "Invalid email format"}
    ]
  },
  "request_id": "req_01HZX...",
  "timestamp": "2026-07-02T17:30:00Z"
}

3.5 Common HTTP Status Codes
Status Meaning Typical Use
200 OK Successful reads or updates.
201 Created New resource created.
202 Accepted Async task accepted, such as report processing.
204 No Content Successful delete/no payload response.
400 Bad Request Malformed or invalid request.
401 Unauthorized Missing/invalid token.
403 Forbidden Authenticated but insufficient permission.
404 Not Found Resource not found or not accessible.
409 Conflict Duplicate or invalid state transition.
422 Validation Error Pydantic validation failure.
429 Too Many Requests Rate limit exceeded.
500 Internal Server Error Unexpected system failure.
503 Service Unavailable External provider unavailable.
4. Authentication and Authorization APIs
Blumetara uses Firebase Authentication for identity and FastAPI for backend authorization. The frontend obtains a 
Firebase ID token. The backend verifies the token, maps the Firebase user to an internal user record, and applies role, 
plan, and resource-scope rules.
POST /api/v1/auth/session
Field Details
Purpose Verify Firebase token, create/update internal user session metadata, and return 
backend-facing user context.
Auth Firebase ID token required
Primary Module Authentication Module
Rate Limit Moderate
Request Example
Headers:
Authorization: Bearer <firebase_id_token>
Body:
{
  "device_id": "ios_abc123",
  "platform": "ios",
  "app_version": "1.0.0"
}
Success Response Example
{
  "success": true,
  "data": {
    "user_id": "usr_123",
    "role": "user",
    "plan": "free",
    "profile_completed": false,
    "entitlements": {"daily_chat_limit": 5, "max_goals": 1}
  }
}

admin.

state. Avoid storing unnecessary sensitive fields.

metrics.
Used by TARA only with user consent and strict 
scope.

9. Goal Tracking APIs
Goals should be modeled generically so the product can support weight loss, water intake, glucose monitoring, BP 
monitoring, step goals, calorie goals, sleep goals, and future health behaviors without creating a new API group for each 
goal type.

block MVP.
Food Image Analyzer V1 Requires AI image processing, cost controls, and 
daily limits.
Nutrition Tracking V1 Needs nutrient database or external API.

14. Admin APIs
Admin APIs must be separated from user APIs and protected with admin role checks. Admin actions must create audit 
logs. The admin dashboard should not access user medical content casually; sensitive report details should require 
explicit privileged support workflow.
Admin Capability MVP Need Notes
User Search Yes Search by email, name, user_id, subscription state.
User Detail Yes Show account status, plan, usage, high-level 
health/report counts.
Report Status Yes Show processing status, failure reason, retry action.
AI Usage Yes Show usage and provider errors, not raw sensitive 
chats by default.
Notifications Optional Manual system announcements later.
Payment Monitoring MVP+ Needed if paid plan launches in MVP.
Audit Logs Yes Required for sensitive operations.

16. Cross-Cutting API Requirements
16.1 Pagination
List endpoints should use cursor-based pagination for scalable resources such as reports, conversations, messages, 
notifications, audit logs, and admin user search.
Query:
GET /api/v1/reports?limit=20&cursor=eyJpZCI6...
Response:
"pagination": {
  "limit": 20,
  "next_cursor": "eyJpZCI6...",
  "has_more": true
--- PAGE 232 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 9
Draft v1.0 | API Documentation & Integration Contracts
}
16.2 Filtering and Sorting
Parameter Usage Example
status Filter by processing/resource status. status=processed
type Filter by resource type. report_type=blood_report
from/to Date range filtering. from=2026-07-01&to=2026-07-31
sort Sort by safe indexed fields. sort=-created_at
q Search query for admin/user-owned resources. q=cholesterol
16.3 Idempotency
Payment creation, webhook handling, report upload confirmation, and reminder creation should support idempotency. 
This prevents duplicate payments, duplicate reminders, and repeated task creation when clients retry requests.
Headers:
Idempotency-Key: idem_01HZXYZ
Applicable endpoints:
POST /subscriptions/checkout
POST /reports/{report_id}/confirm-upload
POST /reminders
POST /medicines/{medicine_id}/logs
16.4 Rate Limiting
Endpoint Class Limit Strategy Reason
Auth/session Moderate per device/IP Prevent automated abuse.
AI chat Plan based + per-minute cap Control cost and abuse.
Report upload Strict per user/day Control storage/OCR costs.
Food image analysis Plan based + daily cap High AI cost feature.
Admin APIs Role based + audit Sensitive operations.
Webhook APIs Signature validation + replay protection Prevent fraud and spoofing.
17. Validation Rules
Validation must happen at the API boundary using Pydantic schemas and again inside service-level business rules where 
required. API validation prevents malformed data; business validation prevents invalid state transitions.
Area Validation Examples
Emails and identifiers Validate format, length, and canonicalization.
Dates and times Use ISO-8601, store UTC internally, preserve user timezone for reminders.
Medical fields Avoid unsupported diagnosis fields; use controlled labels where possible.
Goal targets Validate units, numeric ranges, frequency, and plan limits.
File uploads Validate size, content type, extension, and ownership.
AI prompts Reject empty, abusive, disallowed, prompt-injection, and emergency-risk inputs 
where needed.
Payments Validate plan IDs server-side; never trust client-calculated price.
18. Security and Privacy Requirements
 Every protected route must use a centralized auth dependency.
 Every user-owned resource lookup must include user_id scope in repository queries.
 Admin routes must require role=admin and should create audit logs for sensitive actions.
 Do not return raw S3 object keys to clients except where absolutely necessary; prefer signed URLs with short expiry.
 Do not expose raw LLM prompts, internal system messages, provider keys, or hidden safety instructions.
 Do not allow users to request another user_id in normal user APIs.
 RAG retrieval must filter by user_id, report_id ownership, family account permission, and deletion status.
 Payment webhooks must verify provider signatures and protect against replay attacks.
--- PAGE 233 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 9
Draft v1.0 | API Documentation & Integration Contracts
19. OpenAPI and Swagger Implementation Plan
FastAPI can generate OpenAPI documentation automatically if routers and Pydantic models are defined cleanly. The 
generated docs should be considered a developer tool, while this volume remains the architectural contract.
 Use tags matching modules: Auth, Users, Reports, AI, Goals, Medicines, Reminders, Notifications, Subscriptions, Admin, 
System.
 Define request and response Pydantic models explicitly. Avoid returning raw MongoDB documents.
 Include response_model for every endpoint.
 Document error codes in endpoint docstrings or OpenAPI extensions.
 Hide internal/admin-only docs in production if necessary.
 Export OpenAPI JSON and include it in the developer handover package.
@router.post("/api/v1/goals", response_model=ApiResponse[GoalResponse], tags=["Goals"])
async def create_goal(
    payload: GoalCreateRequest,
    current_user: CurrentUser = Depends(require_user),
    service: GoalService = Depends(get_goal_service),
):
    result = await service.create_goal(user_id=current_user.user_id, payload=payload)
    return ApiResponse(success=True, data=result, message="Goal created")
20. Frontend Integration Guidelines
Client Area Integration Rule
Flutter API Client Use typed service classes for each API group. Do not call HTTP directly from 
widgets.
Token Handling Attach Firebase ID token through interceptor/middleware. Refresh token when 
expired.
Error Display Map standard error codes to friendly user messages.
Report Upload Use pre-signed upload flow and show processing status polling.
AI Chat Stream response later if needed; MVP can use request/response.
Admin Dashboard Use separate admin API client and enforce admin auth state.
Offline Handling Queue only safe local actions. Do not queue payments or AI chat blindly.
21. QA Test Matrix
API Group Critical Test Cases
Auth Valid token, expired token, disabled user, missing token.
Users/Profile Create profile, update profile, missing required fields, unauthorized access.
Reports Upload URL, invalid file type, quota exceeded, confirm upload, process status, 
delete.
AI Chat Free plan limit, report-based answer, no report context, unsafe medical 
question, provider failure.
Goals Create within limit, exceed plan limit, progress update, invalid units.
Reminders Timezone handling, duplicate reminders, disable reminder, FCM token removed.
Payments Create checkout, webhook valid, webhook invalid signature, duplicate webhook.
Admin Non-admin blocked, user search, report retry, audit log created.
22. Implementation Sequence
API implementation should follow dependency order. Authentication and user profile must come before reports and AI. 
Report upload and processing must come before report Q&A. Subscriptions can be implemented after core MVP unless 
paid plan is part of launch.
Phase API Work Reason
Phase 1 System health, auth session, current user, profile 
APIs App bootstrapping and identity foundation.
Phase 2 Health profile, settings, notification token APIs Personalization and reminders foundation.
Phase 3 Report upload, list, detail, status APIs File and metadata foundation.
Phase 4 AI chat and report question APIs Core TARA experience.
--- PAGE 234 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 9
Draft v1.0 | API Documentation & Integration Contracts
Phase 5 Goals, medicines, reminders, progress logs Habit and caretaker capabilities.
Phase 6 Admin user/report/analytics APIs Operational visibility.
Phase 7 Subscriptions/payments/webhooks Monetization and plan limits.
Phase 8 Nutrition/workout APIs MVP+ or V1 expansion.
23. API Backlog
Priority Endpoint Area Decision
P0 Auth, Profile, Reports, AI Chat, Goals, Reminders Required for MVP.
P1 Admin, Analytics, Notifications, Daily Summary Important for operations and product value.
P2 Subscriptions, Payments Required if paid plan launches immediately.
P3 Food Image Analyzer, Nutrition Tracking, Workout 
Generation Move to MVP+ or V1 if timeline is tight.
P4 Wearables, Hospital APIs, Pharmacy APIs, Insurance 
APIs Future V2/enterprise roadmap.
24. Definition of Done for API Layer
 Every implemented endpoint has a Pydantic request model and response model.
 Every protected endpoint validates token, role, plan, and user ownership where applicable.
 Every endpoint has unit/integration tests for success and failure paths.
 Every endpoint returns the standard success/error envelope.
 Every endpoint logs request_id and high-level operational metadata without leaking sensitive data.
 Swagger/OpenAPI docs are generated and reviewed.
 Frontend developers can integrate without asking for hidden response fields.
 QA has a test case list for each endpoint group.
 Admin-sensitive and medical-data-sensitive endpoints create audit logs.
25. Closing Summary
Volume 9 turns the Blumetara AI architecture into practical integration contracts. The mobile app, admin dashboard, 
backend services, AI orchestrator, RAG pipeline, subscription layer, and operations dashboard all depend on stable APIs. 
The API layer should be implemented with discipline: thin routers, strict schemas, centralized authorization, predictable 
responses, and explicit error behavior.
The next volume should focus on Flutter mobile architecture and client implementation, translating these APIs into 
screens, states, navigation flows, token handling, upload flows, chat UX, report views, reminders, notifications, and user 
experience behavior.

Item Details
Document Name Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 10: Flutter Mobile App Architecture & 
UX Delivery Blueprint
Purpose Define how the Blumetara AI mobile app should be designed, organized, 
integrated, tested, and released for the MVP and future versions.

How to Use This Volume
This volume converts the Blumetara product vision into a mobile engineering blueprint. It should be used before the 
Flutter app is implemented. The goal is to avoid a random screen-by-screen build and instead create a maintainable, 
scalable, testable mobile app that can support TARA AI, health reports, goals, reminders, subscriptions, and future 
wearable integrations.
 Use this document to decide the Flutter folder structure, navigation, state management, and feature boundaries.
 Use the screen specifications as the starting point for Figma screens, Flutter widgets, and QA test cases.
 Use the integration guidance to connect the mobile app safely with FastAPI, Firebase Auth, FCM, S3-backed report uploads, 
and AI/RAG APIs.
 Treat this as a blueprint, not a final UI design file. The UI should still be designed visually in Figma or equivalent before final 
implementation.
1. Executive Summary
The Blumetara mobile app is the primary user-facing experience of the platform. Users will interact with TARA AI 
through the mobile app to ask health questions, upload medical reports, track goals, receive medicine and water 
reminders, view personalized health summaries, and monitor progress over time. Because the mobile app will handle 
sensitive health-related information, it must be designed with strong privacy, predictable navigation, secure 
authentication, graceful error handling, and a calm healthcare-oriented user experience.
Mobile Product Principle
The Flutter app should feel like a reliable health companion, not a noisy productivity app. The experience must be simple, 
calm, safe, personalized, and transparent. TARA AI should guide users, but the app must never imply that it replaces 
professional medical care.
1.1 Mobile MVP Success Criteria
 Users can register, log in, and maintain a health profile securely.
 Users can upload health reports and track processing status without confusion.
 Users can chat with TARA AI using profile and report context.
 Users can set goals and view progress in a simple dashboard.
 Users can create medicine and water reminders and receive push notifications.
 Users can understand system states such as loading, processing, failed upload, AI unavailable, and empty data.
 The app supports Android and iOS with a shared Flutter codebase.
 The codebase is modular enough to support V1/V2 features without rewrite.
--- PAGE 237 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 10
Draft v1.0 | Flutter Mobile App Architecture & UX Delivery Blueprint
2. Mobile App Product Role
The mobile app is not just a frontend wrapper around APIs. It is the user experience layer that translates backend 
intelligence into daily behavior. For Blumetara, the mobile app must bring together AI chat, report memory, reminders, 
goals, and daily summaries into one coherent health co-pilot experience.
Responsibility Mobile App Role Backend Role
Authentication Collect login/signup credentials or social login input; 
store token securely.
Verify Firebase token and map user to internal 
account.
Health Profile Collect and display health profile fields through 
guided forms. Persist profile and expose profile-aware AI context.
Report Upload Let user choose PDF/image, validate file type/size, 
show upload/progress status.
Store file in S3, run OCR/RAG processing, persist 
metadata.
TARA Chat Provide conversational UI, message states, 
disclaimers, and source/report references.
Classify intent, build context, call LLM, apply safety 
and return response.
Goals Show goals, progress meters, nudges, and update 
flows. Persist goals/progress and compute analytics.
Reminders Create schedules, permission prompts, and 
local/push notification UX.
Store reminders, schedule worker tasks, send FCM 
notifications.
Subscription Display plan limits, upgrade prompts, entitlement 
state. Validate plan, enforce limits, handle payments.
3. Flutter Architecture Philosophy
The recommended architecture for the Blumetara mobile app is a feature-first clean architecture. Each major feature 
owns its presentation, application/state, domain models, repositories, and data sources. Shared infrastructure such as API 
client, auth token provider, secure storage, error mapping, analytics, theme, and reusable widgets should live in a core 
layer.
Flutter App
  -> Presentation Layer: screens, widgets, navigation, view states
  -> Application Layer: controllers/notifiers, use cases, form state
  -> Domain Layer: entities, value objects, repository contracts
  -> Data Layer: API clients, DTOs, repository implementations, cache
  -> Core Layer: auth, networking, errors, theme, analytics, storage, utilities
3.1 Why Feature-First Clean Architecture
Decision Reason Tradeoff
Feature-first folders Keeps AI chat, reports, goals, reminders, and profile 
isolated and easier to maintain. Requires discipline to avoid duplicated utilities.
Repository abstraction Allows API details to remain outside UI widgets. Adds small upfront complexity.
Typed models/DTOs Reduces integration mistakes and improves 
testability. Requires model maintenance when APIs change.
Central API client Standardizes headers, token refresh, errors, retries, 
and logging.
Must be designed carefully to avoid becoming a God 
object.
Shared design system Keeps healthcare UI consistent and professional. Needs initial effort before screens are built.

5. State Management Strategy
The state management approach should be simple enough for a small team but structured enough for a production app. 
Riverpod is recommended because it supports dependency injection, testability, scoped providers, and clean separation 
between UI and business logic. BLoC is also acceptable, but Riverpod is lighter for this MVP.
Option Pros Cons Recommendation
Riverpod
Great dependency injection, 
testability, async state, less 
boilerplate.
Requires provider discipline and 
naming conventions. Recommended.
BLoC Very explicit events/states, strong for 
large teams. More boilerplate for MVP. Acceptable alternative.
Provider Simple and familiar. Can become messy in larger apps. Avoid for core architecture.
setState only Fast for prototypes. Not maintainable for Blumetara scale. Do not use except tiny local UI state.
5.1 State Types
 Global app state: authentication session, current user, selected family member, feature flags, subscription entitlement.
 Feature state: chat messages, report upload progress, goal list, reminder schedules, medicine stock, notification list.
 Transient UI state: text field focus, tab selection, local animation state, modal visibility.
 Cached state: profile snapshot, dashboard summary, recent conversations, last report processing status.
6. Navigation Architecture
Navigation should be route-based and guarded. The app should prevent unauthenticated users from entering protected 
screens and should route incomplete users to health profile onboarding before enabling TARA personalization. GoRouter 
is recommended because it handles declarative routing, redirects, deep links, nested navigation, and guards well.

7. Design System and UX Principles
Blumetara should use a calm healthcare design language. The app should avoid aggressive red alerts except for truly 
important warning states. It should use approachable copy, clear cards, progress meters, and guided flows. Because users 
may be worried about health reports, the UI must communicate uncertainty and safety clearly.
UX Principle Implementation Guidance
Calm by default Use clean spacing, soft cards, readable typography, and non-alarming colors.
Explain AI boundaries Show clear disclaimer that TARA is not a doctor and does not replace emergency 
care.
Reduce cognitive load Use progressive disclosure. Do not expose all health data at once.
Show progress Report upload, OCR, AI processing, and goal tracking need visible states.
Make failure recoverable Every failed upload/API/AI call should provide a retry path.
Personal but not creepy Use health profile context in helpful ways without overclaiming certainty.
Accessible UI Readable font sizes, contrast, tap targets, semantic labels.
7.1 Core Reusable Components
Component Purpose Used In
HealthMetricCard Show compact health metric or goal progress. Dashboard, Goals, Reports.
TaraMessageBubble Display AI/user messages with status and disclaimer 
support. TARA Chat.
ReportStatusChip Show uploaded/processing/ready/failed state. Reports list and details.
GoalProgressMeter Visual progress against goal target. Goals, Dashboard.
ReminderCard Medicine/water/goal reminder summary with next 
time. Reminders, Dashboard.
SafetyDisclaimerBanner Explain AI safety/medical boundaries. Chat, Reports, Onboarding.
EmptyStateView Friendly empty screens with next action. Reports, Goals, Reminders.
ErrorRetryView Standard failure display with retry. All network screens.
PlanLimitBanner Explain free-plan limit and upgrade path. Chat, Reports, Goals, Food Analyzer future.

9. TARA AI Mobile Experience
TARA AI is the emotional and functional center of Blumetara. The mobile chat interface must make TARA feel helpful, 
safe, and context-aware while clearly showing that AI is not a doctor. The UI should support normal chat, report-specific 
Q&A, daily summaries, goal nudges, and safety escalations.
9.1 Chat Message States
State UI Behavior Backend/Event Source
--- PAGE 243 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 10
Draft v1.0 | Flutter Mobile App Architecture & UX Delivery Blueprint
User composing Text field active, attachment/report context selector 
optional. Local UI state.
Sending User message visible with pending indicator. POST /ai/chat started.
Thinking TARA typing/loading indicator with subtle 
animation. AI orchestrator processing.
Response ready AI answer displayed with optional source/report 
references. POST /ai/chat success.
Safety response TARA refuses diagnosis or directs user to 
doctor/emergency care. Safety engine response.
Rate limited Plan limit or abuse limit banner shown. 429 or entitlement error.
Provider unavailable Retry and fallback message. 503 or AI provider failure.
TARA Safety Copy Rule
Avoid phrases like "You have disease X" or "This is definitely normal." Prefer: "Your report appears to show...", "This may 
indicate...", "Please confirm with a qualified healthcare professional."
10. Report Upload UX
Report upload is one of the most important flows because it creates long-term memory for TARA. The user must 
understand what is happening after a file is uploaded. OCR and RAG processing may take time, so the app should show 
clear status and allow users to leave the screen while processing continues.
Report Upload UX Flow
  Select File
  -> Validate type and size locally
  -> Upload to backend/S3 flow
  -> Backend accepts job
  -> Show processing card
  -> Poll or refresh status
  -> Ready: show summary and Ask TARA button
  -> Failed: show reason and retry/re-upload action
Report Status Meaning Mobile UI
selected User picked a file but upload not started. Preview file name, size, and upload button.
uploading File transfer in progress. Progress bar and cancel option if supported.
uploaded File stored; processing queued. Processing message.
ocr_processing OCR extraction running. Status chip: Extracting text.
embedding_processing Chunking/embedding running. Status chip: Preparing AI memory.
ready Report can be summarized and queried. Show summary, tags, Ask TARA CTA.
failed Upload or processing failed. Show human-readable failure and retry.
11. API Integration Pattern
The Flutter app should not call HTTP directly from widgets. Each feature should use a repository that depends on a 
central API client. DTO mapping should happen in the data layer. Domain entities should be used by UI/application layers.
Widget / Screen
  -> Controller / Notifier
  -> Use Case or Feature Service
  -> Repository Interface
  -> Repository Implementation
  -> API Client
  -> FastAPI Backend
11.1 API Client Responsibilities
 Attach Firebase ID token to protected requests.
 Refresh or re-fetch token when expired.
 Parse standard success/error envelopes.
 Map HTTP errors to user-friendly app errors.
 Apply retry policy only for safe transient failures.
--- PAGE 244 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 10
Draft v1.0 | Flutter Mobile App Architecture & UX Delivery Blueprint
 Attach request IDs to logs where available.
 Avoid logging sensitive health data in debug or production logs.
11.2 Example Repository Contract
abstract class ReportsRepository {
  Future<List<HealthReport>> getReports();
  Future<HealthReportUploadResult> uploadReport(File file);
  Future<HealthReportDetails> getReportDetails(String reportId);
  Future<TaraAnswer> askReportQuestion(String reportId, String question);
}
12. Authentication, Token, and Secure Storage
Firebase Authentication manages user identity. The Flutter app obtains Firebase ID tokens and sends them to FastAPI. 
Sensitive session data should be stored in secure storage. Non-sensitive preferences can be stored in shared preferences. 
The app should handle token expiration and logout cleanly.
Item Storage Notes
Firebase current user Firebase SDK SDK manages auth state.
Firebase ID token In memory; re-fetch from SDK Do not manually persist long-term if SDK can supply 
it.
Refresh/session metadata Firebase SDK / secure storage if needed Avoid custom refresh handling unless required.
Device token for FCM Secure/local storage + backend registration Update backend when token changes.
User preferences SharedPreferences Theme, onboarding complete, non-sensitive flags.
Health data cache Prefer encrypted/local minimal cache Avoid caching raw reports unless explicitly 
required.
Privacy Rule
Do not store raw medical reports, extracted OCR text, AI responses containing sensitive medical data, or access tokens in plain 
local storage. Minimize offline health-data caching during MVP.
13. Notifications and Reminder UX
Notifications are central to medicine reminders, water reminders, goal nudges, daily summaries, and plan events. The 
app must handle notification permission prompts respectfully. Users should understand why notifications are needed 
before the operating system permission dialog appears.
Notification Type Trigger UX Expectation
Medicine reminder Scheduled backend worker / FCM Clear medicine name, dosage, action: mark 
taken/snooze.
Water reminder Configured reminder schedule Lightweight nudge, not alarming.
Goal nudge Goal schedule or gap detection Encouraging progress copy.
Daily summary 10 PM or user-selected summary time Open daily summary screen or TARA summary.
Report ready OCR/RAG processing completed Open report details.
Plan limit Usage limit reached Open subscription screen.
13.1 Notification Permission Flow
User enters reminders feature
  -> App explains benefit of reminders
  -> User taps Enable Reminders
  -> OS notification permission dialog
  -> If allowed: register FCM token with backend
  -> If denied: show manual enable instructions in settings
--- PAGE 245 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 10
Draft v1.0 | Flutter Mobile App Architecture & UX Delivery Blueprint
14. Offline, Error, and Empty State Strategy
A healthcare app must not appear broken when the network is poor or an AI provider is unavailable. Every major screen 
should define loading, empty, partial, offline, and error states. The user should always know whether the problem is 
temporary and what action can be taken.
Scenario Mobile Behavior Engineering Notes
No internet Show offline banner and cached non-sensitive data 
where safe.
Use connectivity awareness but do not rely only on 
it.
API timeout Show retry state and preserve form input. Use reasonable timeout and cancel support.
AI unavailable Show friendly TARA unavailable message and retry 
option. Do not fake AI response.
Report processing delayed Show processing state and allow user to continue 
app usage. Use polling or refresh.
Empty reports Show explanation and upload CTA. Avoid blank lists.
Empty goals Show starter goals or create-goal CTA. Help user begin.
Permission denied Show settings path and explain feature limitation. No repeated nagging.
15. Subscription and Plan Limit UX
The Free vs Paid model must be reflected in the mobile app without damaging trust. Health-related limitations should be 
communicated carefully. Users should understand what is available, what is limited, and why upgrading helps. The app 
should avoid fear-based monetization.
Feature Free UX Paid UX
AI chat Show daily remaining chat count and reset time. Higher daily limit and smoother usage.
Medicine reminders Limit to basic reminder count if required. Multiple reminders and stock monitor.
Water reminders Limited reminder count. Multiple custom schedules.
Goals One goal or limited goals. Up to five goals or more depending on plan.
Food analyzer Future: one image/day. Future: higher daily image limit.
Family monitoring Not available or teaser. Family account monitoring future feature.
16. Analytics and Telemetry
Mobile analytics should help the team understand product usage and reliability without collecting unnecessary sensitive 
health information. Analytics events should focus on feature usage, conversion, failures, and funnel progression. Avoid 
logging raw medical content, chat questions, report text, or private health details.
Event Purpose Sensitive Data Rule
onboarding_completed Measure activation funnel. No health data.
report_upload_started Measure report feature usage. Do not log file name if sensitive.
report_processing_ready Measure processing completion. Use report_id only.
tara_chat_sent Measure chat usage. Do not log message text.
goal_created Measure goal adoption. Log goal type only if acceptable.
reminder_created Measure habit feature usage. Avoid medicine name in analytics.
subscription_viewed Measure monetization funnel. No health data.
api_error_seen Measure reliability. No payload body.
17. Accessibility and Internationalization
The app should be accessible from the MVP stage. Healthcare apps often serve users with varying levels of vision, 
language comfort, technical confidence, and stress. Accessibility is not optional for a serious health product.
 Use readable font sizes and support system text scaling as far as layout allows.
 Maintain sufficient color contrast, especially for health status chips and alerts.
 Avoid communicating status by color alone; use text labels and icons.
 Provide semantic labels for buttons, inputs, and important cards.
 Use large enough tap targets for reminders, medicine actions, and chat send button.
--- PAGE 246 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 10
Draft v1.0 | Flutter Mobile App Architecture & UX Delivery Blueprint
 Keep language simple and avoid unnecessary medical jargon unless explained.
 Design copy so future internationalization is possible without rewriting logic.
18. Testing Strategy for Flutter
The mobile app should be tested at multiple levels. The MVP does not need enterprise-level automation for every screen, 
but core flows must be verified before client delivery and production release.
Test Type What to Test MVP Priority
Unit tests Validators, date/time reminder logic, DTO mapping, 
error mapping. High
Widget tests Reusable cards, forms, empty states, error views, 
chat bubbles. Medium
Integration tests Login, profile setup, report upload mock, chat mock, 
reminders. High
Golden tests Critical UI components if design stabilizes. Optional
Manual QA Device testing on Android and iOS, permissions, 
notifications. High
API contract tests Verify app models match backend response 
envelopes. High
Performance tests Startup time, scroll performance, chat screen 
memory. Medium
18.1 Critical QA Flows
 New user: onboarding -> signup -> profile setup -> dashboard.
 Returning user: login -> dashboard -> TARA chat.
 Report flow: upload report -> processing -> ready -> ask TARA about report.
 Goal flow: create goal -> update progress -> dashboard reflects progress.
 Reminder flow: create medicine/water reminder -> permission -> notification received.
 Plan limit flow: free user reaches chat/report/goal limit -> upgrade prompt.
 Failure flow: no internet, backend error, AI unavailable, upload failure.
19. Build, Release, and Environment Strategy
The Flutter app should have separate development, staging, and production configurations. API base URLs, Firebase 
projects, logging levels, and feature flags should not be hardcoded directly into screens.
Environment Purpose Configuration
Development Local developer builds and mock testing. Dev API base URL, verbose logs, debug banners.
Staging Client QA and pre-release validation. Staging backend, staging Firebase, production-like 
settings.
Production Real users. Production API, production Firebase, minimal logs, 
crash reporting.
19.1 Release Checklist
 App version and build number updated.
 Correct environment config selected.
 Firebase config verified for Android and iOS.
 API base URL points to intended environment.
 Crash reporting and analytics configuration checked.
 Notification permission and FCM token registration tested.
 No debug logs exposing sensitive data.
 Core flows manually tested on at least one Android and one iOS device/simulator.

20. Performance and App Quality Guidelines
The MVP should feel fast even if AI tasks are asynchronous. Performance should be managed through proper loading 
states, caching of non-sensitive summaries, pagination, lazy loading, and efficient widget rebuilds.
Area Guideline
Startup Keep splash/bootstrap short; avoid blocking on non-critical calls.
Dashboard Load dashboard summary first, then secondary details.
Chat Append messages efficiently; avoid rebuilding entire chat unnecessarily.
Reports Paginate report list; do not download original files unless needed.
Images/files Compress preview images where safe; enforce upload limits.
State rebuilds Use granular providers/controllers to avoid full-screen rebuilds.
Memory Avoid holding large files/OCR text in memory longer than needed.

22. Implementation Sequence
The mobile app should be implemented in a sequence that allows early testing of core integrations while avoiding UI-only 
work that later breaks when backend contracts arrive.
Phase Work Output
Phase 0 Create Flutter project, configure linting, app theme, 
environments, routing skeleton. Running app shell.
Phase 1 Firebase Auth integration, auth screens, secure 
session management. Login/signup working.
Phase 2 Health profile setup, dashboard placeholder, user 
profile APIs. Authenticated user journey.
Phase 3 Reports list/upload/status screens with backend 
integration. Report upload MVP.
Phase 4 TARA chat UI and AI chat API integration. Core AI experience.
Phase 5 Goals and reminders screens with CRUD APIs and 
FCM registration. Habit/reminder features.
Phase 6 Subscription screens, plan limit UI, usage banners. Monetization baseline.
Phase 7 Polish, QA, error states, performance, release builds. Client-ready MVP build.
23. Risks and Mitigations
Risk Impact Mitigation
Overloaded MVP UI App becomes confusing and slow to deliver. Prioritize must-have screens; push 
food/wearables/family to V1/V2.
Unclear AI safety boundaries User may misinterpret AI as medical diagnosis. Use disclaimer banners, careful copy, safety 
responses.
API instability Frontend rework and delays. Freeze API contracts from Volume 9 before 
implementation.
Notification permission denial Reminder feature loses value. Explain value before OS permission prompt; support 
settings recovery.
Sensitive local data exposure Privacy/security risk. Minimize local health data cache; use secure 
storage.
Inconsistent UI App feels unprofessional. Build shared design system before feature screens.
AI latency Chat feels slow. Use thinking states, async processing, and helpful

progress copy.
24. Mobile Acceptance Checklist
 The app launches successfully on Android and iOS.
 Auth flow works end to end with Firebase and backend session mapping.
 Profile setup collects required fields and persists correctly.
 Dashboard displays user-specific health summary, reminders, goals, and TARA CTA.
 Report upload supports PDF/image file validation, upload, processing status, and ready/failed states.
 TARA chat works with loading, response, error, safety, and rate limit states.
 Goals can be created, updated, listed, and displayed with progress meters.
 Medicine and water reminders can be created and notifications can be received.
 Subscription screen reflects free/paid entitlements and plan limits.
 All major screens have loading, empty, error, and offline states.
 No sensitive health data is logged or stored insecurely.
 UI follows a consistent design system and is readable on common device sizes.
25. Handover Notes for Developers
Before implementation begins, the product owner, Flutter developer, backend developer, and designer should review this 
volume together. Any missing screens, API assumptions, plan limit rules, or TARA safety copy should be clarified before 
sprint work starts. The mobile app will define the user perception of Blumetara, so the implementation should prioritize 
trust, clarity, and reliability over feature overload.
Volume 10 Final Recommendation
Build the mobile app as a clean, modular Flutter product with a calm healthcare design system, strict API contracts, safe TARA 
AI UX, secure authentication, clear report-processing states, respectful reminders, and disciplined MVP scope. This will make 
Blumetara easier to maintain, easier to scale, and more credible to users and clients.

Item Details
Document Name Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 11: Admin Dashboard Architecture & 
Operations Console
Purpose Define how the web admin dashboard should be scoped, architected, secured, 
integrated, tested, and operated for the Blumetara AI MVP and future versions.
Primary Audience Product owner, admin dashboard engineers, backend engineers, QA engineers, 
support staff, operations managers, and future maintainers.
Depends On Volumes 1-10: project context, business requirements, MVP scope, system 
architecture, backend, database, AI, RAG/OCR, APIs, and Flutter app.
Out of Scope Final visual brand design, production legal policy text, and real-time medical 
intervention workflows.
How to Use This Volume
This volume defines the administrative and operational surface of Blumetara AI. The dashboard should not be treated as 
a decorative reporting website. It is the control room for user management, report monitoring, AI usage visibility, support 
workflows, subscription operations, audit review, and platform health. A poorly designed admin dashboard can create 
security risk, operational confusion, and accidental exposure of sensitive health-related information. A well-designed 
dashboard gives the business team visibility while preserving strong privacy and access boundaries.
 Use this volume to decide which admin features belong in MVP and which should be deferred to V1/V2.
 Use the screen specifications as the starting point for React/Next.js implementation and QA tests.
 Use the RBAC matrix to prevent overexposure of sensitive user health data to unnecessary admin roles.
 Use the audit and support sections to design safe operational workflows from day one.
1. Executive Summary
The Blumetara AI admin dashboard is the internal web application used by authorized platform staff to manage and 
monitor the system. While the mobile app is the user-facing health companion, the admin dashboard is the business and 
operations cockpit. It provides visibility into users, reports, AI usage, subscriptions, notifications, application health, and 
support issues. For the MVP, the dashboard should remain intentionally lean. It should provide enough visibility to 
operate the product, support early users, and debug issues without becoming a full enterprise hospital admin suite.
Admin Dashboard Principle
The dashboard must expose operational visibility without becoming a privacy risk. Admin users should see only the minimum 
information required for their role. Sensitive health report content should be masked, access-controlled, audited, and never 
casually browsable.
1.1 MVP Admin Success Criteria
 Admins can securely log in and access only authorized dashboard areas.
 Admins can view user accounts, account status, and support-relevant metadata.
 Admins can monitor health report upload and processing status without casually exposing report content.
 Admins can view TARA AI usage metrics, cost indicators, failure rates, and abuse signals.
 Admins can view goals/reminders at a high-level only when required for support.
 Admins can monitor subscriptions and payment status without storing card data.
 Admins can send or manage platform notifications safely.
 Admins can inspect audit logs and system health for operations and debugging.
2. Admin Dashboard Product Role
The dashboard exists to help the Blumetara team operate the platform safely. It should not attempt to replace clinical 
systems, electronic medical records, or doctor portals in the MVP. It is first an operations and support tool. Future

3. Recommended Admin Technology Stack
The recommended dashboard stack is React with Next.js. The dashboard should be treated as a separate web application 
from the mobile app, consuming the same FastAPI backend through admin-specific APIs. It should not connect directly to 
MongoDB Atlas, S3, Firebase, Stripe, Razorpay, or the LLM provider from the browser. All privileged actions should go 
through the backend so that validation, authorization, audit logging, and rate limiting are centralized.
Layer Recommended Choice Reason
Frontend Framework React + Next.js Strong ecosystem, good routing, server/client 
flexibility, easy deployment.
UI Library Tailwind + shadcn/ui or Material UI Fast professional dashboard UI with accessible 
components.
Auth Firebase Auth session + backend RBAC Consistent identity model with mobile app and 
backend role enforcement.
API Client Typed client generated from OpenAPI where 
possible
Reduces contract mismatch between dashboard and 
FastAPI.
Charts Recharts, Tremor, or Chart.js Simple operational analytics without heavy BI 
tooling.
Tables TanStack Table Filtering, pagination, sorting, column visibility, row 
actions.
State/Data Fetching TanStack Query Caching, retries, loading states, invalidation, 
pagination.
Forms React Hook Form + Zod Reliable validation and typed form contracts.
Deployment Vercel, Cloudflare Pages, S3/CloudFront, or AWS 
Amplify
Fast deployment; final choice should align with 
cloud strategy.
4. Admin Architecture Overview
Admin Browser
  -> Next.js Admin App
      -> Firebase Auth session / ID token
      -> Typed API Client
          -> FastAPI Admin API Layer
              -> RBAC + Permission Guard
              -> Service Layer
              -> Repository Layer
              -> MongoDB Atlas / S3 metadata / AI logs / Payment records
              -> Audit Log Writer
Important rule: Admin dashboard must never bypass backend authorization.
4.1 Architecture Boundaries
Boundary Allowed Not Allowed

Browser to Backend HTTPS API calls with auth token, pagination, 
filtering, safe admin actions.
Direct database connection, direct S3 write, direct 
LLM key use.
Admin Auth Firebase identity plus backend role check. Assuming Firebase login alone means admin 
authorization.
Sensitive Data Masked or role-controlled access with audit logs. Unrestricted browsing of medical reports or chat 
history.
Payments View provider reference, plan, status, event history. Storing card data or bypassing payment gateway.
AI Operations Usage metrics, safety flags, error logs, cost 
indicators.
Changing model behavior in production without 
review.
5. Admin Roles and Permissions
RBAC must be enforced by the backend, not merely hidden in the frontend. The frontend can hide unavailable UI for 
convenience, but every admin API must verify permissions server-side. Because Blumetara handles health-related data, 
the default role should have minimal access. More sensitive operations should require higher privilege and should 
always be written to audit logs.
Role Purpose Typical Permissions
Super Admin Founder or trusted platform owner. Full access, role management, sensitive 
configuration, audit review.
Operations Admin Runs daily platform operations. User status, report processing status, notifications, 
analytics, system health.
Support Agent Helps users with account and app issues. Limited user lookup, support notes, non-sensitive 
metadata, ticket context.
Billing Admin Handles subscription and payment support. Plan status, payment references, refund/support 
workflow links.
Content Admin Manages non-medical static content. FAQs, onboarding copy, app banners, health tips 
pending approval.
Read-Only Analyst Views aggregate analytics. Dashboards and reports only, no user-level sensitive 
data.
Developer/SRE Debugs system issues. System health, logs, worker status, error traces, 
limited masked data.

The MVP dashboard should have a compact navigation system. A dashboard with too many sections will slow

platform.

MVP Scope Control
Do not build a complex CMS, hospital portal, doctor portal, insurance dashboard, or advanced BI dashboard in MVP. The first 
admin dashboard should answer: who is using the product, what is failing, what needs support, what costs money, and what 
actions were taken.
7. Screen Catalogue and Specifications
7.1 Overview Dashboard
Field Specification
Purpose Provide a high-level operating snapshot for the platform.
Primary Users Super Admin, Ops Admin, Analyst, SRE
Data Required User counts, active users, report processing queue, AI usage, failed jobs, revenue

Controls/Actions Date range filter, refresh, drill-down cards.
UI States Loading, empty, normal, degraded system, API error.
Risk Notes Avoid showing raw sensitive content on overview cards.

Primary Users Super Admin, Ops Admin, Support Agent
Data Required User profile metadata, account status, plan, created date, last active, support

UI States Loading, no results, user not found, permission denied.
Risk Notes Support roles should see masked/minimal health data only.

Field Specification

Primary Users Super Admin, Ops Admin, Support Agent

Controls/Actions View account, add support note, change status if authorized.
UI States Normal, restricted view, deleted user, suspended user.

authorized and audited.

vector status, error message.
Primary APIs GET /admin/reports, GET /admin/reports/{id}, POST /admin/reports/{id}/retry
Controls/Actions Filter by status, retry failed processing, view metadata.
UI States Queued, processing, completed, failed, retrying.
Risk Notes Raw documents should not be casually downloadable from admin dashboard.
