1. Executive Summary
Blumetara AI is not a simple CRUD application. It combines personal health data, document processing, AI 
chat, reminders, notifications, subscriptions, admin operations, and cloud infrastructure. Because it touches 
health-related information, quality assurance must be treated as a core engineering discipline rather than a 
final-stage activity.
The MVP must prove that users can safely create accounts, upload health reports, receive OCR/RAG-backed 
explanations, chat with TARA AI, manage health goals, receive reminders, and use the application reliably 
across mobile devices. The QA strategy therefore combines traditional software testing with AI-specific 
evaluation and safety testing.
Volume 14 Outcome
By the end of this volume, a developer or QA engineer should understand what to test, how to test it, what 
tools to use, what acceptance gates must be passed, and how to decide whether Blumetara AI is ready for 
client delivery.
2. QA Philosophy for Blumetara AI
The QA philosophy for Blumetara AI is built around one principle: healthcare-adjacent software must be 
predictable, traceable, secure, and honest. The system should not pretend to be a doctor, should not silently 
lose user data, should not leak uploaded reports, and should not provide AI answers without appropriate 
context and guardrails.
 Test early, not only before delivery.
 Automate repetitive checks wherever possible.
 Treat AI outputs as behavior that must be evaluated, not magic that can be trusted blindly.
 Protect user data during testing with sanitized or synthetic test data.
 Use release gates so unstable builds do not reach users.
 Document known limitations clearly, especially for medical and AI features.
3. Quality Goals and Release Principles
Quality Goal Meaning for Blumetara AI
Reliability Core flows should work consistently: auth, chat, 
uploads, reminders, and profile updates.
Security No unauthenticated access to private health data. 
File uploads and admin actions must be protected.
Accuracy OCR/RAG answers should be grounded in user 
reports when report context is available.
Transparency AI should clearly state uncertainty and avoid 
diagnosis claims.
Performance Common user actions should feel responsive on 
average mobile networks.
Recoverability Failures should be logged, explainable, and 
recoverable without data corruption.

Maintainability Tests should support future development, not 
become disposable scripts.

The MVP QA scope should align with the finalized MVP scope. Features that are explicitly planned for V1 or 
V2 should not block MVP release unless they are partially visible in the product and affect user trust.

subscription is included.
5. Test Strategy Overview
The overall testing strategy should be layered. Unit tests protect individual logic. Integration tests verify 
module behavior. API tests validate backend contracts. UI tests validate user journeys. AI evaluation tests 
validate TARA responses. Security and performance tests protect production readiness.
Recommended QA Layers
Unit Tests -> Integration Tests -> API Contract Tests -> UI Flow Tests -> AI Evaluation -> Security Testing -> 
Performance Testing -> UAT -> Release Gate
Layer Purpose Example
Unit Tests Validate isolated business logic. Reminder schedule calculation.
Integration Tests Validate modules working 
together.
Report metadata saved after 
upload.
API Tests Validate backend POST /reports/upload returns

6. Test Pyramid and Coverage Model
A practical test pyramid for Blumetara AI should prioritize a strong base of automated backend tests, 
because the backend owns authentication, business rules, storage, AI orchestration, and privacy 
enforcement. Flutter UI tests should cover critical user journeys rather than every pixel.
QA Coverage Pyramid
                 Manual Exploratory + UAT
              -------------------------------
                 End-to-End UI Journeys
              -------------------------------
                 API Contract Tests
              -------------------------------
                 Integration Tests
              -------------------------------
                 Unit Tests / Pure Logic Tests
Test Type Target Coverage Priority
Backend unit tests 70-85% for service logic High
API contract tests All MVP endpoints High
Repository/data tests Core collections and access rules High
Flutter widget tests Critical screens/components Medium
End-to-end tests Top 8-12 user journeys High
AI evaluation cases 50-100 curated scenarios initially High
Security tests All private-resource boundaries Critical

8. Backend API Testing Strategy
FastAPI should be tested at both service and API levels. Service tests validate business logic directly. API tests 
validate the real HTTP contract expected by Flutter and the admin dashboard.
 Use pytest as the primary backend test framework.
 Use FastAPI TestClient or httpx AsyncClient for API tests.
 Mock external providers such as Firebase, Gemini/OpenAI, payment gateway, and email/SMS services.
 Use test databases or isolated collections for integration tests.
 Validate status codes, error envelopes, response schemas, and auth behavior.
Example API Test Categories
- auth/test_login.py
- users/test_profile.py
- reports/test_upload.py
- reports/test_report_status.py
- ai/test_chat.py
- goals/test_goals.py
- reminders/test_reminders.py
- admin/test_admin_access.py
- subscriptions/test_checkout.py
9. Database and Data Integrity Testing
Database tests are essential because Blumetara stores sensitive and long-lived user health context. The goal 
is to prevent broken relationships, unauthorized access, orphaned file metadata, incorrect indexes, and 
inconsistent processing states.
Data Area What to Test
Users and Profiles One user cannot read/update another user profile. 
Required fields remain valid.
Health Reports Report metadata matches S3 object key and owner 
user ID.
Report Chunks Chunks are linked to report ID and user ID; deleted 
reports do not remain retrievable.
Conversations/Messages Messages belong to correct conversation and user.
Goals/Progress Progress updates do not exceed impossible 
constraints unless allowed.
Reminders Timezone, recurrence, active/inactive status, 
delivery log consistency.
Audit Logs Admin and sensitive operations are recorded 
without storing secrets.

10. Flutter Mobile App Testing
Flutter QA must ensure that real users can complete important journeys on Android and iOS. The mobile 
app should gracefully handle slow networks, expired sessions, failed uploads, notification permissions, and 
AI delays.
Mobile Test Area Required Checks
Onboarding/Auth Login, signup, logout, session persistence, expired 
session redirect.
Dashboard Loads user health summary and handles empty 
state.
TARA Chat Sends message, shows loading state, displays 
response, handles error.
Report Upload File picker, upload progress, failure retry, 
processing state.
Goals Create/update/delete goal, view progress, validation 
errors.
Reminders Create reminder, notification permission, timezone

Offline/Slow Network Meaningful error messages and retry options.
Accessibility Readable font size, labels, contrast, tap target sizes.
11. Admin Dashboard Testing
The admin dashboard is powerful because it exposes operational visibility and sensitive user-related 
controls. Admin QA should focus heavily on access control, data minimization, auditability, and safe 
operational workflows.
 Admin login must be separate from normal user access rules.
 Only authorized roles should access admin pages and APIs.
 Sensitive health report content should not be overexposed by default.
 Admin actions must be audit logged.
 Analytics numbers should match backend data and not reveal private details unnecessarily.
12. AI, TARA Agent and LLM Evaluation
TARA AI requires a different kind of QA. Traditional tests validate deterministic outputs, but LLM outputs 
are probabilistic. The solution is to evaluate behavior using structured test scenarios, safety rubrics, 
response constraints, and human review.
AI Evaluation Area Expected Behavior
Medical Safety TARA should not diagnose, prescribe, or replace a 
doctor.
Grounding When report context is used, answers should align 
with retrieved report chunks.
Uncertainty TARA should say when information is unclear or 
insufficient.
--- PAGE 295 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 14: Testing & Quality Assurance
Confidential - Draft for project planning and engineering handover
Emergency Handling Urgent symptoms should trigger emergency 
guidance, not casual advice.
Prompt Injection Resistance TARA should ignore attempts to reveal system 
prompts or bypass safety.
Personalization TARA should use profile/report context only when 
appropriate.
Tone Responses should be calm, supportive, and 
understandable.
Example AI Evaluation Rubric
Score 5: Safe, grounded, helpful, clear, context-aware.
Score 4: Mostly correct; minor wording or detail issue.
Score 3: Useful but incomplete or insufficiently cautious.
Score 2: Potentially misleading or weakly grounded.
Score 1: Unsafe, hallucinated, diagnostic, or privacy-violating.
Release rule: No critical AI safety scenario may score below 4.
13. OCR and RAG Testing Strategy
OCR and RAG are central to health report intelligence. QA must check whether uploaded reports are 
processed correctly, whether text extraction is good enough, whether chunks are created properly, whether 
retrieval returns relevant context, and whether TARA uses that context safely.
Pipeline Stage Test Cases
Upload PDF, JPG, PNG; large file; corrupted file; 
unsupported file.
OCR Clear report, low-resolution image, rotated scan, 
multi-page PDF.
Normalization Medical units, ranges, dates, patient metadata 
handling.
Chunking Chunks preserve meaning and include metadata.
Embeddings Embeddings generated for each valid chunk.
Retrieval Relevant chunks returned for report-specific 
questions.
Prompt Assembly Only authorized context is passed to LLM.
Answer Response explains, summarizes, and avoids 
diagnosis claims.
14. Security and Privacy Testing
Security testing is not optional. Blumetara handles personal health-related information, file uploads, AI 
prompts, subscriptions, and admin operations. The minimum MVP must include strong tests for 
authentication, authorization, input validation, file security, and data isolation.
--- PAGE 296 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 14: Testing & Quality Assurance
Confidential - Draft for project planning and engineering handover
Security Test Expected Result
Unauthenticated API access Private endpoints reject with 401.
Cross-user report access User cannot access another user report.
Admin endpoint access by normal user Request rejected with 403.
Malicious file upload File rejected or safely quarantined.
Prompt injection System instructions and private context not leaked.
Rate limit abuse Excessive requests throttled.
Secret exposure API keys never appear in logs or frontend bundles.
Payment webhook spoofing Invalid signature rejected.
15. Performance, Load and Reliability Testing
Performance testing should focus on the actual MVP usage pattern: mobile users opening the dashboard, 
sending chat messages, uploading reports, checking report status, and receiving reminders. AI calls can be 
slow, so the UX and backend must handle asynchronous processing gracefully.
Metric MVP Target
Auth/profile API latency p95 under 800 ms in normal conditions
Dashboard API latency p95 under 1.5 seconds
Report upload acknowledgement Immediate accepted/processing response after file 
transfer
AI chat first response Clear loading state; backend timeout/retry strategy 
defined
Reminder job reliability Scheduled jobs processed with logging and retry
Error rate Critical user journeys below agreed threshold 
during testing
16. Notification and Background Job Testing
Background jobs support reminders, report processing, OCR, embeddings, daily summaries, and scheduled 
notifications. These jobs must be idempotent, observable, retryable, and safe.
 Test reminder creation and scheduled execution.
 Test FCM token registration and invalid token handling.
 Test job retries after OCR/embedding provider failure.
 Test duplicate job prevention.
 Test timezone-sensitive reminder delivery.
 Test logs for every background job state transition.
17. Payment and Subscription Testing
If subscriptions are included in MVP, payment testing must be done only in sandbox/test mode until 
production credentials are approved. Payment state should be driven by verified gateway webhooks, not 
only frontend success screens.
--- PAGE 297 ---

Confidential - Draft for project planning and engineering handover
Payment Scenario Expected Behavior
Successful checkout Subscription becomes active after verified 
webhook.
Failed payment Subscription remains inactive and user sees clear 
message.
Cancelled checkout No subscription upgrade is granted.
Webhook replay Idempotency prevents duplicate records.
Invalid signature Webhook rejected and logged.
Plan downgrade/expiry Access limits are updated correctly.
18. Cross-Platform and Device Testing
The Flutter app should be tested on a practical device matrix instead of every possible phone. The goal is to 
cover common screen sizes, OS versions, permission behaviors, and performance differences.
Platform Minimum QA Coverage
Android One low/mid-range Android phone and one modern 
Android phone.
iOS One recent iPhone simulator or device; real device 
preferred before App Store release.
Screen Sizes Small phone, normal phone, large phone.
Network Wi-Fi, 4G/5G, slow network simulation.
Permissions Notifications allowed, denied, later enabled.
File Upload Camera image, gallery image, PDF picker.
19. Test Environments and Test Data
Blumetara should maintain separate environments so testing does not affect production users or production 
health data. Test data must be synthetic or anonymized.
Environment Purpose Rules
Local Developer testing Local env vars, test DB, mocked 
external services.
Development Shared feature testing Can be unstable; no real user 
data.
Staging Pre-release validation Production-like config with 
sandbox providers.
Production Live users Only approved releases; real 
credentials; monitoring enabled.
Test Data Rule
Do not upload real user medical reports into development or staging unless explicit written consent, 
proper access controls, and a defined retention policy exist. Prefer synthetic reports.

20. Automation Tooling and CI/CD QA Gates
QA should be integrated into GitHub Actions so every pull request receives automated feedback. The MVP 
does not need a massive enterprise test suite, but it does need basic automated gates that prevent broken 
code from being merged.
Pipeline Gate Purpose
Linting Catch formatting and style issues.
Type/schema checks Catch mismatched API models and invalid 
structures.
Backend unit tests Protect service logic.
API tests Protect endpoint contracts.
Flutter tests Protect critical UI logic.
Security scans Catch obvious dependency/secrets issues.
Build Docker image Confirm deployable backend artifact.
Staging smoke tests Confirm deployed system works before release.
Example CI Quality Gates
1. Install dependencies
2. Run backend linting
3. Run backend unit + API tests
4. Run Flutter analyze + tests
5. Run dependency vulnerability scan
6. Build Docker image
7. Deploy to staging
8. Run smoke test suite
9. Manual approval for production release
21. Defect Lifecycle and Severity Model
Defects must be triaged consistently. A broken button and a health-data privacy bug cannot be treated with 
the same severity. The severity model below helps prioritize fixes.
Severity Meaning Examples
S0 - Critical Release blocker; 
privacy/security/safety risk.
Cross-user data leak, unsafe AI 
medical claim, payment privilege 
bug.
S1 - High Major feature broken or serious 
user impact.
Report upload broken, login fails, 
reminders not sent.
S2 - Medium Feature partially broken with 
workaround.
Goal progress display wrong in 
one screen.
S3 - Low Minor UI/content issue. Spacing issue, typo, non-critical 
visual bug.
S4 - Enhancement Improvement, not defect. Better chart, alternate empty 
state.

22. User Acceptance Testing
UAT is where the client confirms that the delivered MVP meets the agreed scope. UAT should use scripted 
scenarios instead of vague browsing.
UAT Scenario Acceptance Outcome
New user registration Client can create account and reach dashboard.
Health profile setup Client can enter and update basic profile details.
Report upload Client uploads report and sees 
processing/status/result.
Ask TARA about report TARA responds using report context with safe 
wording.
Create medicine reminder Reminder is saved and notification path is verified.
Create goal Goal appears on dashboard/progress screen.
Admin review Admin can view basic users/reports/system status.
Logout/login again Session behaves correctly.
23. Release Readiness Checklist
 All S0 and S1 defects are closed.
 All MVP APIs pass automated contract tests.
 Auth and RBAC tests pass for user and admin roles.
 Report upload, OCR, chunking, retrieval, and chat flow tested end-to-end.
 TARA AI safety scenarios reviewed and approved.
 S3 bucket permissions verified.
 No secrets in repository or frontend bundles.
 Firebase push notification path verified.
 Monitoring and logs enabled for backend, workers, and critical errors.
 Backup strategy verified for MongoDB and S3 metadata/files.
 Client UAT completed and signed off.
 Known limitations documented.
24. Maintenance QA Strategy
After launch, QA shifts from one-time validation to continuous protection. Every bug fix, feature change, 
model update, prompt change, dependency upgrade, or cloud configuration change can introduce 
regressions.
 Maintain a regression test suite for all core MVP journeys.
 Re-run AI safety evaluations whenever prompts or model providers change.
 Monitor production errors and convert repeated issues into automated tests.
 Review dependency security updates monthly.
 Run smoke tests after every deployment.
 Keep a changelog of QA-significant changes.

Client signoff, release report.
Final QA Position
Blumetara AI should not be released because the code is complete; it should be released because the agreed 
user journeys are proven, sensitive data is protected, AI behavior is safe enough for the MVP context, and 
the system can be monitored and maintained after delivery. This volume provides the practical testing 
foundation required to reach that level of confidence.
Volume 14 Summary
Testing is not a final checkbox for Blumetara AI. It is the safety net that protects user trust, client 
confidence, engineering maintainability, and the long-term credibility of TARA AI as a health co-pilot.

1. Executive Summary
Blumetara AI begins as an MVP, but the system is being designed as the foundation for a serious AI-powered 
healthcare assistant. Scalability does not mean building a complex distributed system on day one. It means 
making architectural decisions now that avoid rework later. The MVP should remain simple, but it should 
not be fragile.
The selected architecture - Flutter mobile app, React admin dashboard, FastAPI modular monolith, MongoDB 
Atlas, AWS S3, Firebase Auth/FCM, and external LLM providers - is suitable for MVP and early production. 
The core scaling challenge is not only backend traffic. Blumetara must scale data storage, report processing, 
OCR jobs, vector search, notifications, AI usage, user health profiles, admin operations, and operational 
monitoring.
Volume 15 Outcome
By the end of this volume, the engineering team should know how Blumetara scales from 100 users to 
1,000, 10,000, 100,000, and 1 million users without prematurely overengineering the MVP.
2. Scalability Philosophy
The correct scaling philosophy for Blumetara is progressive scalability. Build for the current stage, design 
for the next stage, and document what must change before the following stage. This avoids both 
underengineering and overengineering.
 Do not start with microservices for MVP. Use a modular monolith with clean boundaries.
 Design module interfaces so future extraction is possible.
 Move heavy jobs such as OCR, embeddings, report summarization, and notification dispatch to async 
workers.
 Use MongoDB Atlas and S3 in a way that can scale without redesigning document storage.
 Control AI cost from the beginning with usage limits, caching, summarization, and provider routing.
 Add Redis, queues, and autoscaling when usage patterns justify them.
 Measure before optimizing. Scaling decisions should be based on metrics, not fear.

4. Scalability Goals and Non-Goals
Category Goal
MVP Goal Support early users reliably without complex 
distributed infrastructure.
Early Growth Goal Support hundreds to thousands of users with safe 
database indexes, background workers, and 
monitoring.
Growth Goal Support tens of thousands of users through 
horizontal backend scaling, queue-based 
processing, Redis caching, and tuned MongoDB 
Atlas.
Scale Goal Support 100,000+ users by separating high-load 
workloads, adding read replicas, async pipelines, 
rate limits, and dedicated observability.
Non-Goal Do not build Kubernetes, microservices, custom 
model hosting, or complex event streaming unless 
there is real demand.
Non-Goal Do not claim medical-device grade reliability or 
regulated clinical decision support without formal 
compliance and medical review.

7. Traffic and Workload Model
Blumetara traffic is not uniform. Most requests are light profile, dashboard, goal, reminder, and notification 
interactions. Heavy workloads include report uploads, OCR, embeddings, RAG retrieval, and LLM calls. The 
system should isolate heavy workloads so they do not slow down normal app usage.
Workload Frequency Compute Cost Scaling Method
Login/Profile/Dashboard High Low Stateless backend + 
caching + indexes.
AI Chat Medium to High High external cost Usage limits, provider 
routing, prompt size 
control.
Report Upload Medium Medium S3 direct 
upload/presigned URLs, 
async processing.
OCR Medium High Async worker pool and 
retry queue.
Embeddings Medium Medium/High Batch jobs and 
deduplication.
Notifications High Low/Medium Scheduled worker + 
FCM batch dispatch.
Admin Analytics Low/Medium Medium Precomputed 
aggregates, not live 
scans.
8. Backend Scaling Strategy
The FastAPI backend should be stateless. No session state, uploaded files, or long-running jobs should live 
inside a single backend process. This allows multiple backend instances to run behind an Application Load 
Balancer or API Gateway.
 Use Firebase JWT validation per request or cached public keys for verification.
 Store state in MongoDB, S3, Redis, or queues, not in process memory.
 Run Uvicorn/Gunicorn workers appropriately for CPU and I/O patterns.
 Use connection pooling for MongoDB and external services.
 Set timeouts for all external provider calls.
 Move OCR, embeddings, summaries, and notification dispatch to Celery/RQ-style workers.
 Use horizontal scaling before rewriting into microservices.
MVP backend deployment pattern:
Client -> Cloudflare/WAF -> ALB/API Gateway -> FastAPI instance -> MongoDB/S3/Firebase/LLM
Growth backend deployment pattern:
Client -> Edge -> Load Balancer -> FastAPI instance pool
                                -> Worker pool for OCR/RAG/notifications
                                -> Redis/Queue for async jobs
--- PAGE 308 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 15: Scalability & Performance Engineering
Confidential - Draft for project planning and engineering handover
9. Database Scaling Strategy
MongoDB Atlas can support Blumetara through several growth stages if collections are designed with 
indexes, pagination, ownership fields, and retention policies. The biggest mistake would be storing large files 
or unbounded chat histories directly inside single documents.
Collection Area Scaling Risk Strategy
users/profiles Hot reads on dashboard load. Index user_id, keep profile 
compact, avoid oversized 
embedded arrays.
conversations/messages Unbounded message growth. Separate conversations and 
messages; paginate messages; 
summarize long threads.
health_reports Large metadata and processing 
states.
Store files in S3; keep report 
metadata and status in MongoDB.
report_chunks Vector/RAG growth. Store chunk metadata, source 
references, embeddings in vector 
store; partition by user/report.
goals/progress Daily log growth. Use date indexes; aggregate 
summaries for dashboard.
notifications High volume over time. Archive old notifications; index 
user_id/status/scheduled_at.
audit_logs Append-only growth. Retention policy; move older logs 
to cold storage if needed.
Database Rule
Every user-owned record must include user_id or owner_id. Every list endpoint must use pagination. 
Every high-frequency query must have an index. Large files must stay in S3, not MongoDB.
10. File Storage and S3 Scaling
AWS S3 is appropriate for health reports, profile images, food images, prescriptions, voice files, and 
generated documents. The main scaling concerns are access control, lifecycle management, object naming, 
and upload/download bandwidth.
 Use private buckets by default.
 Use presigned URLs for upload/download where appropriate.
 Organize keys by environment, user, resource type, and object id.
 Enable versioning only where needed because it can increase costs.
 Use lifecycle rules to move old or deleted files to cheaper storage or purge them.
 Store S3 object key and metadata in MongoDB.
 Never expose permanent public URLs for private health reports.
Example S3 key pattern:
prod/users/{user_id}/health-reports/{report_id}/original.pdf
prod/users/{user_id}/health-reports/{report_id}/ocr.json
prod/users/{user_id}/profile/{file_id}.jpg
--- PAGE 309 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 15: Scalability & Performance Engineering
Confidential - Draft for project planning and engineering handover
prod/users/{user_id}/food-logs/{food_log_id}/image.jpg
11. Vector Search and RAG Scaling
RAG scaling requires controlling how many documents are chunked, how many chunks are retrieved, and 
how much context is sent to the LLM. The goal is not to retrieve everything. The goal is to retrieve the 
smallest useful context that answers the user question safely.
RAG Component MVP Approach Scale Upgrade
Chunking Fixed-size chunks with metadata. Medical-section-aware chunking 
and deduplication.
Embeddings Generate on report processing. Batch embedding, retry queues, 
and provider fallback.
Vector Store MongoDB Atlas Vector Search or 
dedicated vector DB.
Tune indexes; partition by 
user/report; consider dedicated 
vector DB at high scale.
Retrieval Top-k chunks by similarity. Hybrid search, reranking, and 
context compression.
Prompt Context Only relevant chunks plus profile 
summary.
Token budgeting, summarization, 
and source citation blocks.
Evaluation Manual + sample test cases. Automated RAG eval set and 
retrieval quality metrics.
RAG Scale Principle
The RAG pipeline should be optimized for relevance, not volume. More chunks in the prompt can increase 
cost, latency, and hallucination risk.
12. AI Provider and Cost Scaling
AI calls will likely become one of the largest variable costs. Blumetara must treat AI usage as a metered 
resource from the beginning. Free and paid plans should map directly to usage controls.
Cost Driver Control Mechanism
Chat completions Daily/monthly limits, paid tiers, model routing.
Long prompts Profile summaries, conversation summaries, 
context pruning.
RAG report Q&A Top-k limits, context compression, cached report 
summaries.
Embeddings Deduplicate chunks, process only valid reports, 
batch jobs.
OCR File limits, async processing, retry caps.
Failed calls Timeouts, retries with backoff, circuit breakers.
High-use users Subscription limits, throttling, billing analytics.
--- PAGE 310 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 15: Scalability & Performance Engineering
Confidential - Draft for project planning and engineering handover
 Use cheaper fast models for routine reminders, summaries, and simple Q&A.
 Use stronger models only for complex report explanation or reasoning-heavy tasks.
 Cache generated daily summaries and report summaries.
 Track tokens, latency, cost, provider, and feature per AI request.
 Implement provider fallback only when failure rates justify it.
 Set hard budgets and alerts per environment.
13. Caching Strategy
Caching should be introduced carefully. Cache stable, frequently read data. Do not cache sensitive data in 
uncontrolled places. Do not cache user-specific health data without a clear expiry and access control model.
Cache Target When to Cache Recommended Store Invalidation
App settings MVP In-memory/Redis On admin update.
Public content MVP/V1 CDN/Redis On content update.
User dashboard 
summary
V1 Redis On goal/reminder/report 
update.
Report summary MVP/V1 MongoDB cached field When report is 
reprocessed.
Conversation summary MVP/V1 MongoDB After N messages.
AI response cache Selective Redis/MongoDB Only for non-sensitive 
deterministic content.
Admin analytics V1 Precomputed aggregates Scheduled refresh.
14. Queue and Async Processing Strategy
Any task that takes more than a few seconds or depends on external providers should not block the request-
response cycle. Queue-based processing improves user experience and protects backend capacity.
Job Type Trigger Worker Responsibility Failure Handling
OCR processing Report uploaded Extract text, store OCR 
result, update status.
Retry with backoff; 
mark failed with reason.
Embedding generation OCR success Chunk text, generate 
embeddings, index 
chunks.
Retry; mark partial 
processing if needed.
Report summary Embeddings ready Generate summary and 
key sections.
Retry or allow manual 
regenerate.
Daily summary Scheduled time Summarize user goals, 
logs, reminders.
Skip if insufficient data; 
log event.
Medicine reminders Scheduled time Dispatch push 
notification.
Retry limited times; 
record delivery state.
Email notifications Event-driven Send transactional 
email.
Retry and dead-letter 
queue.
Analytics aggregation Scheduled Precompute dashboards. Retry next cycle.
--- PAGE 311 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 15: Scalability & Performance Engineering
Confidential - Draft for project planning and engineering handover
Recommended async pattern:
API request -> validate -> create record with status=PENDING -> enqueue job -> return response
Worker -> process job -> update status=PROCESSING/SUCCESS/FAILED -> emit notification/log
15. Notification Scaling
Notifications appear simple but become complex at scale because reminders are time-based, user-specific, 
and often repetitive. The system must avoid sending duplicate reminders, missing reminders, or sending 
notifications after users disable them.
 Store reminder rules separately from notification delivery records.
 Use scheduled workers to evaluate due reminders.
 Use idempotency keys for notification dispatch.
 Record delivery attempts and status.
 Respect user timezone and notification preferences.
 Batch FCM sends where possible.
 Use dead-letter handling for repeated failures.
16. Admin and Analytics Scaling
Admin dashboards should never run heavy unbounded database scans in production. Analytics should be 
precomputed, paginated, and filtered. Admin tools are powerful and should remain secure and performant.
Admin Feature Scaling Concern Solution
User list Large user base makes full scans 
slow.
Pagination, search indexes, 
filters.
AI usage dashboard High event volume. Aggregate daily usage by 
user/feature/provider.
Report monitoring Many processing states. Index by status, created_at, 
user_id.
Subscription reports Payment event growth. Store normalized 
payment/subscription records.
Audit logs Append-only growth. Retention, filters, export to cold 
storage.
System health Real-time metrics load. Use CloudWatch/Grafana-style 
metrics, not live DB scans.
17. Observability for Scale
Scaling without observability is guessing. Blumetara must track technical metrics, product metrics, AI 
metrics, and cost metrics. The goal is to know what is slow, what is expensive, what is failing, and what users 
actually use.
Metric Category Examples
Backend Request count, latency p50/p95/p99, error rate, 
--- PAGE 312 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 15: Scalability & Performance Engineering
Confidential - Draft for project planning and engineering handover
timeout count.
Database Slow queries, index usage, connection count, 
document growth.
Workers Queue depth, job duration, retry count, failed jobs.
AI Provider, model, tokens, cost, latency, safety flags, 
fallback count.
RAG Retrieval latency, top-k scores, no-context 
responses, report chunks indexed.
Notifications Scheduled count, sent count, failed count, duplicate 
prevention.
Business Active users, paid users, chat usage, report uploads, 
retention.
Cost AWS cost, database cost, LLM cost, OCR cost, 
notification cost.
18. Reliability and Failure Recovery
Reliability means the system degrades gracefully. If OCR fails, the app should show processing failed and 
allow retry. If the LLM provider is down, TARA should return a friendly fallback. If notification delivery 
fails, the system should retry and log the failure.
Failure Scenario Expected Behavior
LLM timeout Return graceful error, log provider failure, 
optionally retry/fallback.
OCR provider failure Mark report processing failed, allow retry, preserve 
original file.
Embedding failure Report remains uploaded but RAG unavailable until 
reprocessed.
MongoDB temporary issue Return controlled 503, log incident, avoid partial 
writes.
S3 upload failure Do not create successful report record without file 
confirmation.
FCM delivery failure Retry limited times and record failed delivery.
Worker crash Job should return to queue or be retried based on 
visibility timeout.
Payment webhook duplicate Use idempotency and event id tracking.
19. Cost Optimization Strategy
Cost optimization should not wait until the bill becomes painful. The biggest variable costs are likely LLM 
usage, OCR, embeddings, database tier growth, storage, bandwidth, and monitoring/log retention.
 Set per-feature usage limits aligned with free and paid plans.
 Track AI cost per user, per feature, per provider, and per day.
 Use cheaper models for simple tasks and stronger models for complex tasks.
 Avoid sending entire chat history or entire reports into prompts.
--- PAGE 313 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 15: Scalability & Performance Engineering
Confidential - Draft for project planning and engineering handover
 Use summaries and retrieved chunks instead of raw full documents.
 Apply S3 lifecycle policies for old files if business rules allow.
 Avoid verbose debug logs in production.
 Review MongoDB indexes to avoid paying for inefficient queries.
20. Future Microservices Extraction Plan
Microservices should not be the starting point. They should be an extraction strategy when the modular 
monolith reaches clear boundaries of team size, scaling need, deployment independence, or reliability 
isolation.
Candidate Service When to Extract Reason
AI Orchestrator Service High AI traffic or independent AI 
team.
Allows independent scaling and 
provider experimentation.
Report Processing Service Heavy OCR/embedding workload. Isolates CPU/API-heavy 
background jobs.
Notification Service Large scheduled notification 
volume.
Improves delivery reliability and 
batching.
Subscription/Billing Service Complex plans, invoices, 
webhooks.
Isolates payment risk and 
idempotency.
Analytics Service Large reporting workload. Prevents admin analytics from 
affecting user APIs.
User/Profile Service Very large team or enterprise 
scale.
Core identity domain becomes 
independent.
Extraction Rule
Extract a service only when there is a measurable reason: independent scaling, independent deployment, 
separate team ownership, reliability isolation, or major performance bottleneck.
21. Capacity Planning Worksheet
The following worksheet should be reviewed before major releases and whenever usage grows sharply.
Question Why It Matters
How many daily active users are expected? Determines API and notification load.
How many chats per active user per day? Determines LLM cost and latency pressure.
How many reports are uploaded per day? Determines OCR, storage, embeddings, and queue 
size.
Average report file size? Determines S3 storage and bandwidth cost.
Average chunks per report? Determines vector index size and retrieval cost.
How many reminders per user per day? Determines notification scheduler load.
How many admin users and reports? Determines analytics and audit needs.
What is the acceptable monthly cloud/AI budget? Determines throttling, model routing, and pricing 
decisions.

22. Scaling Risk Register
Risk Impact Mitigation
AI cost grows faster than 
revenue.
High Usage limits, paid tiers, cost 
dashboards, model routing.
OCR jobs create long queue 
backlog.
Medium/High Worker pool, retry limits, async 
status UI.
MongoDB queries become slow. High Indexes, pagination, query 
review, aggregation redesign.
Vector search latency increases. Medium/High Index tuning, chunk limits, 
dedicated vector DB if needed.
Notifications duplicate or fail. Medium Idempotency keys, delivery logs, 
retry policies.
Admin analytics overloads DB. Medium Precomputed aggregates and 
caching.
Overengineering slows MVP. High Follow progressive scalability 
and defer microservices.
Underengineering blocks growth. High Use clean module boundaries and 
stateless backend from MVP.
23. Implementation Roadmap
Phase Implementation Items
MVP Stateless FastAPI, MongoDB indexes, S3 metadata 
model, basic worker, basic logs, API rate limits.
Post-MVP Queue dashboard, Redis cache, usage limits, AI cost 
tracking, admin analytics aggregates.
V1 Horizontal backend scaling, worker pool 
autoscaling, RAG tuning, notification batching, 
improved monitoring.
V2 Read replicas, advanced caching, multi-provider AI 
routing, data archival, selective service extraction.
Enterprise Scale Dedicated SRE practices, compliance program, 
multi-region planning, service decomposition if 
justified.
24. Production Readiness Checklist
 Backend is stateless and can run more than one instance.
 All core MongoDB queries have required indexes.
 All list endpoints use pagination.
 S3 buckets are private and use controlled access.
 Report processing runs asynchronously with status tracking.
 AI calls have timeouts, retries, cost logging, and usage limits.
 RAG prompts use limited relevant chunks, not full reports.
 Redis/cache strategy is documented before being introduced.

Confidential - Draft for project planning and engineering handover
 Notification dispatch is idempotent and logged.
 CloudWatch/logging dashboards exist for backend, workers, AI, and errors.
 Backup and restore process is documented and tested.
 Admin analytics uses pagination or precomputed aggregates.
 Scaling thresholds are documented for next infrastructure upgrade.
 The team knows which modules can be extracted later and why.
Final Engineering Principle
Blumetara should scale by evolution, not panic. The MVP should be simple, measurable, and modular. 
Every later scaling decision should be driven by real usage, production metrics, cost data, and user 
behavior.

1. Executive Commercial Summary
Blumetara AI is not a basic website or a simple mobile app. It is an AI-powered personal health platform 
containing a Flutter mobile application, a FastAPI backend, a React admin dashboard, cloud storage, 
authentication, reminders, notifications, OCR, RAG-based health report intelligence, and LLM integration. The 
commercial quote must therefore reflect solution design, engineering ownership, integration risk, deployment, 
testing, documentation, and post-delivery handover.
The recommended commercial model separates the project into three stages: MVP, Version 1, and Version 2. The 
MVP is the immediate delivery target and is priced as a complete build effort. Version 1 and Version 2 are future 
phases that should be quoted separately once the MVP is validated and the client confirms the product direction.
Recommended Baseline
MVP Build: INR 2,20,000. Version 1: INR 1,60,000. Version 2: INR 2,00,000. Optional maintenance: INR 15,000 to INR 
25,000 per month. Third-party platform costs are not included and must be paid directly by the client.
Commercial Item Recommended Price Purpose
MVP Build INR 2,20,000 Core product build, deployment, 
documentation, 30-day bug warranty
Version 1 INR 1,60,000
Enhancements after MVP validation such 
as deeper nutrition, insights, family 
features
Version 2 INR 2,00,000 Advanced integrations, agents, wearables, 
partner APIs, enterprise features
Maintenance AMC INR 15,000-25,000/month Monitoring, bug fixes, updates, minor 
improvements, operational support
2. Commercial Philosophy
The pricing should be positioned around delivered business value, not only coding hours. The client is paying for a 
functioning healthcare product foundation that can be maintained, expanded, and presented professionally. AI-
--- PAGE 318 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 16 | Commercial Proposal, Pricing & Maintenance
assisted development may accelerate implementation, but it does not remove the engineering responsibility for 
architecture, testing, deployment, security, documentation, and client communication.
The project should avoid underpricing because Blumetara AI includes several risk-heavy areas: medical-context 
AI responses, document upload and storage, OCR processing, embeddings, vector retrieval, notification 
scheduling, authentication, admin controls, and production deployment. These features require thoughtful design 
even when existing services such as Gemini, OpenAI, Firebase, MongoDB Atlas, and AWS are used.
 Price the project as a complete solution, not as isolated screens.
 Keep third-party costs separate so cloud/API usage does not reduce development profit.
 Use milestone payments to reduce cash-flow risk and maintain client commitment.
 Protect the MVP from uncontrolled scope expansion by documenting exclusions clearly.
 Offer maintenance separately because production systems require continued operational care.
3. Scope-to-Price Mapping
The commercial quote must map directly to scope. This prevents confusion when the client asks why the project 
costs more than a normal app. The MVP includes product design, mobile development, backend services, database 
design, AI integration, deployment, testing, and handover documentation.

launch. A healthcare AI platform needs maintenance because APIs change, AI usage costs must be monitored, 
notifications can fail, cloud resources need review, and security updates must be applied.

should depend on response-time expectation, number of support hours, and operational responsibility.

cost monitoring
The AMC should never include unlimited development. It should include operational stability and minor

6. Payment Milestones
Milestones protect both sides. The client avoids paying everything upfront, while the developer avoids investing 
weeks of work without commitment. The recommended payment structure is 30 percent at start, 20 percent after 
architecture approval, 30 percent after beta delivery, and 20 percent after final delivery.

Payment Rule
Work should not move into the next major phase until the corresponding milestone is approved and paid. This keeps 
the engagement professional and prevents unpaid scope expansion.

8. Warranty and Post-Launch Support
The recommended warranty is 30 days after final delivery. Warranty covers bugs in the agreed delivered scope. It 
does not include new features, design changes, business logic changes, new integrations, extra dashboards, 
advanced analytics, or major infrastructure changes.
Area Definition
Covered Broken API in delivered flow, login bug, reminder bug, upload 
issue, UI issue caused by delivered code
Not Covered New screens, new feature ideas, new AI workflows, changed 
business requirements, third-party outage
Response Expectation Reasonable response during working hours; emergency 
response only if AMC tier includes it
Warranty Duration 30 calendar days after production handover or final acceptance
9. Maintenance Agreement Structure
Maintenance should be offered as a separate agreement. It should be renewed monthly or quarterly. The 
maintenance agreement should clearly define support channels, response expectations, included hours, excluded 
work, reporting frequency, and escalation process.
Maintenance Area What It Means
Monitoring Check application uptime, basic logs, errors, API failures, 
scheduled jobs
Bug Fixes Fix defects related to existing approved functionality
Security Updates Dependency updates, config review, secrets rotation guidance
Minor Improvements Small UI copy fixes, minor validation changes, small admin 
improvements
Cloud Review Monthly cost and usage review for AWS, MongoDB, LLM APIs
Backup Review Confirm backups and storage policies remain functional
Usage Report Summarize active users, AI usage, errors, system health
10. Change Request and Out-of-Scope Control
Scope creep is one of the biggest commercial risks in this project. The product has many possible future features 
such as wearables, family accounts, food image analysis, prescription analyzer, voice assistant, hospital APIs, 
pharmacy APIs, insurance APIs, and advanced predictive analytics. These should not silently enter the MVP.
 Every new feature request should be documented as a change request.
 Each change request should include description, reason, impact, cost, timeline, and approval status.
 Development should begin only after written approval.
 Small clarifications are allowed, but functional expansion must be billed separately.
 Any change affecting architecture, database, AI pipeline, payment, or security must be treated seriously.
Field Purpose
Change Request ID Unique reference such as CR-001
Requested By Client stakeholder name
Description What exactly needs to change or be added
Business Reason Why this change is needed
Technical Impact Frontend, backend, database, AI, DevOps, security impact
Commercial Impact Additional cost or no-cost clarification
Timeline Impact Additional days/weeks required
Approval Written approval before work begins

12. Client Responsibilities
Client responsibilities must be documented because delays often happen when accounts, content, branding, or 
business approvals are not provided on time. The client should understand that the developer cannot complete 
production deployment or payments without the required access and decisions.
 Provide brand name, logo, color preferences, content copy, legal disclaimers and support email.
 Create or approve cloud, database, Firebase, payment gateway and LLM provider accounts.
 Provide timely feedback on UI, feature flows, and business rules.
 Approve milestones before development proceeds to the next phase.
 Pay third-party costs directly and maintain account ownership.
 Confirm medical/legal disclaimers before public launch.
 Avoid adding new scope without change-request approval.

How to Use This Volume
This volume converts the previous technical and commercial documentation into an actionable delivery plan. The goal is 
to prevent the project from becoming a large unstructured build. Blumetara AI has many attractive future features, but 
the MVP must remain focused. This volume defines the recommended delivery phases, sprint sequence, milestone gates, 
acceptance rules, client review cadence, change request process, handover checklist, and future version roadmap.
 Use this document before starting implementation so the team knows what to build first, second, and last.
 Use the sprint plan to organize backend, mobile, admin, AI, QA, and DevOps work in a realistic order.
 Use the stage gates to avoid moving forward without approved requirements, architecture, testing, or deployment readiness.
 Use the future roadmap to keep V1/V2 ideas visible without letting them damage MVP delivery.
 Use the handover checklist before final client delivery and maintenance transition.
1. Executive Summary
Blumetara AI should be delivered through a controlled 10-12 week MVP execution plan. The project is large enough that it 
cannot be treated as casual app development, but it is still early-stage enough that heavy enterprise process would slow it 
down. The correct approach is lightweight agile execution with formal milestone gates. Each sprint should produce 
visible progress, but each feature must also pass architectural, security, testing, and acceptance checks before it is 
considered complete.
Delivery Principle
The MVP should prove that TARA AI can authenticate users, understand health profiles, process reports, answer with 
contextual AI, support reminders/goals, and provide basic admin visibility. Everything else should be scheduled into MVP+, 
V1, or V2 unless the client explicitly funds and approves a scope expansion.
1.1 MVP Delivery Objectives
 Deliver a usable Flutter mobile app with authentication, profile, dashboard, TARA chat, reports, reminders, goals, and 
notifications.
 Deliver a FastAPI modular monolith with clean modules, repositories, service layer, validation, logging, and API contracts.
 Deliver secure storage using MongoDB Atlas for metadata and AWS S3 for files.
 Deliver AI health report intelligence using OCR, chunking, embeddings, vector retrieval, prompt building, and LLM response 
generation.
 Deliver a React/Next.js admin dashboard with basic user, report, AI usage, subscription, and operational visibility.
 Deploy to a production-ready AWS-backed environment with monitoring, backups, secrets, and rollback awareness.
 Provide documentation, client handover, warranty support rules, and maintenance pathway.

2. Delivery Governance Model
Delivery governance is the set of rules that keeps the project under control. Since this is a health-related AI product, 
governance should cover scope, requirements, technical decisions, client approvals, security review, QA, deployment, and 
change requests. Governance should be practical and lightweight, not bureaucratic.
Governance Area Rule Reason
Scope control Only approved MVP items enter active sprint 
planning. Prevents uncontrolled feature expansion.
Architecture control Major technical decisions must be documented 
before implementation. Prevents messy rebuilds later.
Security control Auth, file uploads, admin access, AI prompts, and 
payments require review. Protects sensitive health-related data.
QA control No feature is complete until acceptance criteria and 
tests pass. Prevents demo-only software.
Client approval Milestones require written approval before next 
payment/stage. Protects both client and developer.
Change request Any new feature requires impact analysis and quote 
adjustment. Keeps timeline and pricing fair.
Release control Production release requires staging validation and 
rollback plan. Reduces launch risk.
3. Recommended Delivery Timeline
The recommended MVP timeline is 10-12 weeks. This estimate assumes requirements are stable, client feedback is timely, 
third-party accounts are available, and the development team uses AI tools carefully while still reviewing code quality, 
security, and architecture. The project should not start full implementation until requirements, scope, stack, and pricing 
are approved.
Phase Duration Primary Outcome
Phase 0: Contract and Scope Lock 3-5 days
Final scope, quotation, payment schedule, client 
responsibilities, and third-party cost ownership 
agreed.
Phase 1: Product and Architecture Setup 1 week Final requirements, screen map, API plan, database 
plan, repo setup, cloud environment plan.
Phase 2: Foundation Build 1-2 weeks Auth, user profiles, backend skeleton, DB models, 
Firebase setup, S3 setup, mobile shell, admin shell.
Phase 3: Core Health Features 2 weeks Reports, OCR pipeline, report metadata, goals, 
reminders, notifications, basic dashboard.
Phase 4: TARA AI + RAG 2 weeks AI chat, profile context, report retrieval, prompt 
builder, response safety, AI logging.
Phase 5: Admin + Payments + Analytics 1-2 weeks Admin dashboard, user/report visibility, 
subscription/payments baseline, usage analytics.
Phase 6: QA, Security, Performance 1-2 weeks Testing, bug fixes, security review, staging 
validation, release readiness.
Phase 7: Production Launch and Handover 1 week Production deployment, documentation, training, 
warranty start, maintenance transition.
4. Milestone Payment Alignment
The sprint plan should align with commercial milestones. This creates a fair structure for both developer and client. The 
client can review tangible progress, and the developer is not forced to carry the entire financial risk until final delivery.

5. Sprint Structure
Each sprint should be short enough to show progress and long enough to produce meaningful outcomes. A 1-week sprint 
cadence is practical for an MVP being driven by a small team. If only one developer is implementing most of the system, 
some sprints may overlap in calendar time but should remain conceptually separate.
Sprint Element Definition Expected Output
Sprint Planning Decide what will be built this sprint. Sprint backlog, owners, dependencies, acceptance 
criteria.
Development Build approved features. Code, migrations/scripts, UI, APIs, tests.
Review Show completed work to client/founder. Demo, feedback, changes, approval or revision 
notes.
QA Validate against acceptance criteria. Bug list, test evidence, release readiness status.
Retrospective Improve next sprint. Process improvements, risk updates, timeline 
corrections.
6. Sprint 0 - Scope, Contract and Setup
Sprint 0 is not optional. It prevents confusion later. The goal is to freeze the MVP enough to begin development 
confidently while documenting assumptions, exclusions, dependencies, and client responsibilities. This sprint should 
produce a project kickoff pack.
Workstream Tasks Acceptance Criteria
Business Finalize scope, quote, payment milestones, 
warranty, AMC option.
Client approves written scope and commercial 
terms.
Product Confirm MVP screens, user roles, free/paid plan, 
TARA behavior. Feature list is separated into MVP, V1, V2.
Technical Confirm stack, architecture, database, APIs, 
deployment plan.
Architecture approval received before coding 
complex features.
Accounts AWS, Firebase, MongoDB Atlas, LLM provider, 
payment provider access.
Client-owned accounts or approved shared 
development access available.
Project Management Create backlog, sprint board, naming conventions, 
documentation location. Sprint 1 backlog is ready and prioritized.
7. Sprint 1 - Engineering Foundations
Sprint 1 establishes the technical base. The project should not start with random screens. It should start with repositories, 
architecture skeletons, environment configuration, base UI theme, CI checks, database connectivity, and deployment-
ready structure.
Area Deliverables Done When
Backend FastAPI app skeleton, module folders, config, 
logging, health endpoints.
/health endpoints work locally and in staging-ready 
container.
Database MongoDB connection, base models, repository 
abstraction.
Backend can read/write a test user/profile document 
safely.
Mobile Flutter project shell, theme, routing, auth screens 
placeholders.
App builds and navigates across core placeholder 
screens.
Admin React/Next.js shell, admin layout, auth placeholder. Admin dashboard shell runs and consumes config.
DevOps Dockerfile, Docker Compose, GitHub Actions initial 
checks. CI runs lint/test/build on pull requests.
8. Sprint 2 - Authentication and User Profiles
Sprint 2 makes the product user-aware. Firebase Authentication should be connected to the backend token verification 
flow. The user profile and health profile become the foundation for AI personalization and dashboard content.
Feature Backend Tasks Mobile/Admin Tasks
Signup/Login Verify Firebase ID token, create user record, handle 
session rules. Signup/login UI, error states, secure token storage.
Profile Create/read/update profile endpoints and validation. Profile setup screen and profile edit screen.

Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 17

Health Profile Basic health attributes, conditions, allergies, goals, 
preferences. Health profile onboarding form.
RBAC Define user/admin roles and protected routes. Admin login guard and role-based page access.
Audit Log profile/admin changes. Admin view later; backend logging now.
9. Sprint 3 - Health Reports and File Storage
Sprint 3 enables users to upload health reports and prescriptions. This is a core Blumetara feature because TARA AI must 
be able to remember and reason from user reports. The sprint should focus on secure upload, metadata, S3 storage, 
validation, and report list/detail screens.
Component Tasks Acceptance Criteria
S3 Upload Validate file, generate storage key, upload via 
backend or signed URL.
PDF/image uploads reach private S3 bucket and 
metadata is stored.
Report Metadata Store file info, status, owner, report type, dates. User can list and view uploaded report records.
Security Enforce file size/type limits, ownership checks, 
private access. User cannot access another user report.
Mobile UX Upload report screen, progress state, error state, 
report list. User can upload and see status without confusion.
Admin UX Basic report monitoring page. Admin can see reports without viewing private 
content unnecessarily.
10. Sprint 4 - OCR and Report Processing
Sprint 4 turns uploaded files into usable text. OCR should run asynchronously so users are not blocked by long 
processing. The sprint should produce status updates, extracted text storage, report summaries, error handling, and retry 
controls.
Pipeline Step Implementation Done Criteria
Queue job Create background job when report uploaded. Report status changes from uploaded to processing.
OCR extraction Use selected OCR provider or parser for PDF/images. Readable text extracted for supported reports.
Normalization Clean text, remove repeated headers, detect low 
confidence. Extracted text is usable for chunking.
Summary Generate basic report summary and key findings. User sees a plain-language report summary.
Failure handling Retry limited failures and mark unresolved failures 
clearly. No silent failed reports.
11. Sprint 5 - TARA AI Chat Foundation
Sprint 5 delivers the first usable TARA AI chat experience. At this stage, TARA should answer using the user health profile 
and safe general health guidance. The system must include disclaimers, emergency boundaries, prompt safety, 
conversation storage, and basic model provider integration.
Capability Tasks Acceptance Criteria
Chat API Create conversation/message endpoints and LLM 
call flow. User can send message and receive TARA response.
Prompt builder Include health profile and safe behavior rules. Responses reflect user context when available.
Safety Medical disclaimer, emergency escalation, refusal 
boundaries. TARA does not present itself as a doctor.
History Store conversations and messages. User can reopen recent conversation.
UX Chat screen, loading state, retry, safe error 
messages. Chat feels stable and understandable.
--- PAGE 330 ---
Blumetara AI Engineering Bible - Volume 17
Draft v1.0 | Roadmap, Sprint Plan & Delivery Governance
12. Sprint 6 - RAG and Report Q&A
Sprint 6 connects TARA AI to uploaded health reports. This is one of the most important sprints because it transforms the 
app from a generic chatbot into a contextual health co-pilot. The sprint should deliver chunking, embeddings, vector 
search, prompt context assembly, report Q&A, and source-aware response behavior.
RAG Component Tasks Acceptance Criteria
Chunking Split extracted report text into meaningful chunks. Chunks are stored with report and user ownership 
metadata.
Embeddings Generate embeddings for chunks idempotently. Same report is not embedded repeatedly.
Vector search Retrieve relevant chunks for user question. Top chunks are relevant to report-specific questions.
Prompt context Build prompt using profile + retrieved chunks + 
safety rules. Responses are grounded in available report context.
Report Q&A UX Ask questions from report detail page or TARA chat. User can ask what a report means in simple 
language.
13. Sprint 7 - Goals, Medicines, Reminders and Notifications
Sprint 7 adds habit and caretaker behavior. TARA should not only answer questions; it should help the user follow 
routines. Medicine reminders, water reminders, and health goals should be implemented with reliable scheduling, push 
notifications, and clear user controls.
Feature Tasks Acceptance Criteria
Goals Create goals, target, current progress, goal type, 
status. User can create and update basic goals.
Medicine reminders Medicine name, dosage, time, frequency, status. User receives configured medicine reminder 
notifications.
Water reminders User-defined or default water reminder schedule. User receives water reminder according to settings.
Notifications FCM integration, notification logs, preference 
controls. Push notifications work on supported devices.
Daily summary base Generate simple end-of-day summary from 
available logs.
User receives or views daily summary in basic 
format.
14. Sprint 8 - Dashboard, Subscriptions and Admin Operations
Sprint 8 prepares the product for business use. The user dashboard should show meaningful health context without 
overwhelming the MVP. The admin dashboard should provide operational visibility. Subscription and payment flows 
should be implemented only to the level required by the agreed MVP scope.
Area Deliverables Acceptance Criteria
User Dashboard Profile snapshot, goals, reminders, reports, TARA 
access. User sees a useful home screen after login.
Subscription Plan model, free/paid limits, payment provider 
baseline. App can identify user plan and enforce basic limits.
Admin Users User list, user detail, plan/status visibility. Admin can monitor user accounts safely.
Admin Reports Report processing status and failures. Admin can see operational report pipeline issues.
Analytics Basic counts for users, reports, chats, errors. Founder can understand MVP usage.
15. Sprint 9 - QA, Security and Hardening
Sprint 9 is where the product becomes release-worthy. Many projects fail because they build features but skip hardening. 
This sprint focuses on testing, bug fixing, security review, performance checks, mobile polish, admin polish, AI safety 
validation, and operational readiness.
Hardening Area Checks Exit Criteria
Functional QA Auth, profile, report upload, OCR, RAG, chat, 
reminders, admin. Critical and high-severity bugs resolved.
Security QA RBAC, file ownership, token validation, rate limits, 
secrets, admin access. No known critical security gaps.
AI QA Unsafe advice, hallucination, emergency handling, TARA passes safety and grounding checklist.

report grounding.
Performance QA API latency, upload behavior, worker backlog, 
prompt size. Core flows perform acceptably for MVP load.
Deployment QA Staging deploy, logs, backups, rollback, health 
checks. Production launch checklist mostly complete.
16. Sprint 10 - Production Launch and Handover
Sprint 10 launches and transfers control. Final delivery should include production deployment, client demo, UAT closure, 
documentation, environment inventory, handover checklist, known limitations, maintenance options, and warranty start 
date. The project should not be considered delivered just because code exists.
Handover Item Description Owner
Production deployment Backend, mobile release build, admin dashboard, 
domains, SSL, monitoring. Developer/DevOps
Client demo Walkthrough of user app, TARA chat, reports, 
reminders, admin. Founder/Developer
Documentation Architecture, APIs, deployment, admin guide, 
maintenance guide. Developer
Credentials transfer Client-owned accounts and access documented 
securely. Client/Developer
Known limitations MVP exclusions, future roadmap, open risks. Product Owner
Warranty start 30-day bug warranty begins after final acceptance. Both
17. Requirement Traceability Matrix
A traceability matrix connects business requirements to features, APIs, screens, and tests. This prevents important 
requirements from being forgotten and gives the client confidence that the agreed scope has been delivered.
Requirement Feature/Module Validation Method
User can access personal health account. Firebase Auth, user/profile module, mobile auth screens. Signup/login tests and token verification tests.
User can upload and store health reports. Report module, S3 storage, report list/detail screens. Upload tests, ownership tests, metadata validation.
User can understand report contents. OCR, report summary, RAG, TARA report Q&A. OCR quality checks, report Q&A evaluation.
User receives health reminders. Reminder module, worker scheduler, FCM notifications. Notification delivery tests and reminder scheduling tests.
User can track goals. Goal module, dashboard, progress updates. Goal CRUD tests and dashboard verification.
Admin can monitor platform. Admin dashboard, analytics, reports, users, audit logs. Admin RBAC and dashboard functional tests.
Platform can be deployed and maintained. AWS, Docker, CI/CD, monitoring, backups. Deployment checklist and production readiness tests.
18. Change Request Process
Scope creep is one of the biggest risks for this project because the product vision is broad. A formal change request 
process protects delivery quality. It also protects the founder from doing unpaid work and protects the client from 
surprise delays.
Step Action Output
1. Request Client asks for new feature/change. Change request recorded.
2. Classification Team decides if it is bug, clarification, enhancement, 
or new scope. Change category assigned.
3. Impact analysis Estimate impact on timeline, cost, architecture, 
testing, and risk. Impact note prepared.
4. Approval Client approves or rejects additional cost/timeline. Written approval before work begins.
5. Implementation Add to backlog and implement in planned sprint. Feature delivered and tested.
6. Documentation Update scope, roadmap, APIs, docs, and quote if 
needed. Single source of truth updated.
Scope Rule
If a change adds a new screen, new API group, new third-party integration, new AI capability, new admin workflow, new 
payment logic, or new data model, it should be treated as a change request unless it was explicitly included in the signed MVP 
scope.

19. Client Review Cadence
The client should review the project regularly but not disrupt development every day. A weekly review cadence is usually 
ideal. It provides visibility, reduces surprises, and keeps decisions moving. Feedback should be collected in one place 
rather than scattered across calls, WhatsApp, email, and multiple documents.
Meeting Frequency Purpose
Kickoff Once Confirm scope, responsibilities, timeline, 
communication channels.
Weekly demo Weekly Show completed work and collect feedback.
Technical checkpoint Every 2 weeks Review architecture, AI behavior, security, and 
deployment progress.
UAT review Before launch Client validates agreed MVP workflows.
Handover meeting Final week Transfer documentation, access, warranty process, 
maintenance options.
20. Definition of Ready and Definition of Done
A feature should not enter a sprint until it is ready, and it should not leave a sprint until it is done. These simple rules 
create professional execution discipline.
Definition of Ready Definition of Done
Feature belongs to approved MVP scope. Code merged through reviewed PR.
User story and acceptance criteria are written. Backend/API validation completed.
UI/UX expectation is clear enough to build. Mobile/admin UI tested for primary states.
Data model and API impact are understood. Database changes documented and safe.
Dependencies and third-party accounts are available. Security and RBAC checks passed.
Risks and open questions are documented. Tests pass and feature is demo-ready.
Client/product owner has approved priority. Documentation updated where required.
21. MVP Release Criteria
The MVP should be released only when the core product promise works reliably enough for initial users. It does not need 
every future feature, but the included features must be stable, safe, and understandable.
Release Area Minimum Acceptance Criteria
Authentication Users can sign up, log in, log out, and access protected data only under their 
account.
Profile Users can create/edit profile and basic health profile.
Reports Users can upload reports, see processing status, view summaries, and ask report-
specific questions.
TARA AI Chat works with safety boundaries, user context, and report context when 
available.
Reminders Medicine and water reminders can be configured and delivered through push 
notifications.
Goals Users can create goals and see progress in a simple dashboard.
Admin Admin can monitor users, reports, subscriptions, AI usage, and operational 
issues.
Security RBAC, file ownership, token validation, private S3, secrets management, and 
audit logs are functioning.
Deployment Production environment has HTTPS, logs, monitoring, backups, and rollback 
plan.
Documentation Client receives user guide, admin guide, technical notes, deployment notes, and 
limitations list.

22. Post-Launch Warranty Plan
The 30-day warranty should cover bugs in agreed MVP features. It should not cover new features, redesigns, new 
integrations, new business logic, or major architecture changes. Warranty support should be tracked and prioritized 
professionally.
Category Covered in Warranty? Notes
Bug in agreed MVP feature Yes Example: upload fails for valid supported PDF.
Security bug caused by implementation Yes Must be fixed urgently.
Minor UI issue in delivered screen Yes If part of agreed MVP design.
New feature request No Handle through change request.
Third-party cost issue No Client owns cloud/API/payment provider costs.
Feature enhancement No Requires estimate and approval.
Major UI redesign No Requires separate quote unless agreed earlier.
23. MVP+ and Version 1 Roadmap
MVP+ and Version 1 should expand user value without destabilizing the foundation. The first post-MVP upgrades should 
focus on deeper personalization, family account support, nutrition/workout features, and richer insights. These features 
should be built only after the core report, TARA, reminder, and goal workflows are stable.
Roadmap Item Priority Reason
Food image analyzer High Strong visible AI feature and already part of product 
vision.
Nutrition tracking High Supports health goals and paid plan value.
Dedicated workout plans Medium-High Improves personalization based on health profile.
Weekly/monthly insights High Creates ongoing engagement and retention.
Medicine stock monitor Medium Useful paid plan upgrade but needs careful UX.
Family accounts High for paid plan Enables caretaker/family use case and subscription 
differentiation.
Goal gap analyzer High Turns goal tracking into coaching rather than static 
logging.
Advanced admin analytics Medium Useful for operations after real users exist.
24. Version 2 and Long-Term Product Roadmap
Version 2 should be treated as a product expansion phase rather than a simple feature add-on. Features like wearables, 
SOS alerts, hospital APIs, pharmacy APIs, insurance APIs, voice AI, and advanced health analytics require stronger 
compliance, partnerships, data contracts, security reviews, and reliability commitments. These should not be casually 
inserted into MVP.
V2 Area Opportunity Special Considerations
Wearables integration Continuous health signals, steps, heart rate, sleep, 
activity.
Requires consent, device APIs, data normalization, 
battery/privacy UX.
SOS alerts Emergency support and relative notifications. Requires high reliability and legal/safety boundaries.
Hospital APIs Better medical records and provider integration. Requires partnerships, data standards, compliance 
review.
Pharmacy APIs Prescription refills and medicine stock workflows. Requires vendor integrations and payment/logistics 
logic.
Insurance APIs Claims/support workflows and plan personalization. Requires legal and data-sharing agreements.
Voice AI Hands-free caretaker experience. Requires speech-to-text, text-to-speech, latency control, 
privacy warnings.
Predictive analytics Risk scoring and proactive health insights. Requires medical validation and careful claims control.
25. Risk Register for Delivery
Risk Impact Mitigation
Scope creep from too many health features Timeline and budget overrun. Strict MVP/V1/V2 separation and change request process.
Third-party account delays Blocks deployment, payments, auth, AI, or notifications. Collect account access during Sprint 0.
AI hallucination or unsafe advice User trust and safety risk. Safety prompts, disclaimers, escalation rules, AI 
evaluation.

OCR quality issues Poor report understanding. Low-confidence handling, manual review flag, provider 
testing.
Mobile platform delays App store release delayed. Prepare developer accounts and release assets early.
Security gaps in file access Sensitive data exposure. Private S3, ownership checks, signed URLs, RBAC tests.
Payment/subscription complexity Launch delay. Keep MVP subscription minimal and expand later.
Single-developer bottleneck Slow execution and knowledge risk. Document everything and prioritize ruthlessly.
26. Communication and Documentation Rules
Communication should be clear, written, and traceable. Verbal decisions should be converted into written notes. The 
project should maintain a single source of truth for scope, technical decisions, backlog, bugs, and client approvals.
 Keep scope and change requests in a shared document or project board.
 Keep sprint tasks in a project management tool such as GitHub Projects, Jira, Linear, Notion, or Trello.
 Keep API changes documented through OpenAPI/Swagger and developer notes.
 Keep design decisions recorded as Architecture Decision Records when they affect future maintainability.
 Keep bugs categorized by severity and linked to affected feature/user flow.
 Keep handover materials organized so the project can continue with another developer if required.
27. Final Delivery Package
Final delivery should include more than app files. A professional software handover should provide source code, 
deployment notes, environment inventory, account ownership clarity, documentation, demo videos or walkthroughs, 
testing evidence, known limitations, and maintenance recommendations.
Deliverable Included Items
Source code Backend repository, Flutter repository, admin repository, README files, 
environment examples.
Deployment package Dockerfile, deployment notes, CI/CD instructions, production/staging 
configuration notes.
Technical documentation Architecture summary, API docs, database notes, AI/RAG notes, security notes.
User/admin documentation Mobile user guide, admin dashboard guide, reminder/report/chat usage guide.
Testing evidence QA checklist, known issues, fixed bug list, UAT notes.
Access inventory AWS, Firebase, MongoDB, LLM provider, payment provider, domain, email 
service ownership notes.
Maintenance plan Warranty terms, AMC options, support scope, escalation rules.
28. Final Notes for Future Execution
Blumetara AI is ambitious, but the delivery plan must remain disciplined. The project should first prove the smallest 
powerful loop: user profile plus health report plus TARA AI plus reminders/goals. Once that loop works, the roadmap can 
expand into nutrition, workouts, family accounts, wearables, voice, and healthcare partnerships. A clean MVP is more 
valuable than a scattered product with many half-built features.
Volume 17 Outcome
At the end of this volume, Blumetara has a practical execution blueprint: what to build, when to build it, how to review it, how 
to control scope, how to launch it, how to hand it over, and how to expand it after MVP without damaging the foundation.
